Now that I have completed this book for you, my sons, which is the last of the science of medicine with its completion, and I have reached the end in it through its expositions and declarations, it seemed good to me to complete it for you with this Treatise which is a part of practice, that is, surgery with the hand.
Since the practice with the hand has fallen in our region and in our time entirely neglected: until perhaps its knowledge perished, and its trace was cut off: and nothing remained of it except small descriptions in the books of the ancients, which were altered by hands: and they fell into error and hesitation, until its intentions were closed, and its power was lost: It seemed to me that I should revive it with the order of this Treatise according to the way of exposition, and declaration, and abbreviation: and to come with the forms of the instruments of cautery and other surgical instruments: which is achieved by the addition of declarations, and by the necessity of its progress.
The reason why a good practitioner of it with his hand is not found in our time is: because the art of medicine is long, and its author must be trained beforehand in the science of anatomy, as Galen narrated, until he knows the benefits of the members, and their forms, and their conjunction, and separation, and has knowledge of the bones, and nerves, and tendons, and their number, and their emergence, and of the pulsating and quiet veins, and the exits of those places.
And because of this, Hippocrates said that the name is abundant with the name, but scarce with the work, and especially in the art of the hand.
We have indeed already spoken of this at the beginning of this book.
For he who is not knowledgeable about what we have said concerning anatomy will not be cleansed but will fall into error by which men are killed: as I have seen many of those who are formed from this science and boast about it without knowledge and without experience.
This is because I saw a foolish doctor incise a scrofulous abscess on a woman's neck, and he cut some arteries in the neck: hence the woman's blood flowed until she fell dead under his hands.
And I saw another doctor who presumed to extract a stone from an elderly man, and the stone was large. He therefore proceeded to do so and extracted it along with a piece of the bladder. Therefore, the man died on the third day.
And I had indeed been called to extract it: and I saw from the size of the stone and the condition of the patient that he would die.
And I saw another doctor who was receiving payment from one of the Dukes in our land for medical services: and it happened that a black eunuch who was with him had a fracture in his leg near the heel: and the doctor, in his ignorance, hurriedly bound the fracture over the wound with bandages and splints with a strong binding, and did not allow the wound to drain.
Then he treated him according to his own desires. Then he left him for several days and instructed him not to loosen the bandage: and he remained thus until his leg swelled with an abscess, and his foot reached destruction.
I was called therefore to him: and I hurried to loosen the bandage: and peace followed, and he escaped from his pains.
However, the corruption was already confirmed in the member: and I could not restrain it.
Therefore, the corruption ceased to spread in the member until it perished.
And I saw another doctor who punctured the cancerous abscess: and it became ulcerated after days, until its wickedness was magnified with its lord.
Which means that when the cancer is purely from a melancholic humor, then it should not be approached with iron at all, unless it is in a limb that can tolerate being totally amputated.
And for this reason, O sons, it is necessary for you to know that the practice with the hand is divided into two parts: namely, an operation associated with safety, and an operation with which there is danger in most conditions.
And I have already warned in every part of this book where the operation brings fear and dread.
Therefore, it is necessary for you to be cautious about it and avoid it, so that fools do not find a way to speak and disparage it.
Take therefore measurements with care and protection, and tend to your patients with ease and firmness, and make use of the better way leading through God's grace to salvation and a praiseworthy continuation: and leave behind terrible illnesses difficult to heal: and free yourselves from that which makes you fear, so that hesitation may not enter into your faith and comfort.
For it remains more for your glory, and higher in this world, and finally for your dignities.
For Galen has already said in some of his admonitions. Do not treat illness badly: lest you be called bad doctors.
Now I have divided this Treatise into three Chapters.
First Chapter.
Regarding the Hot Cauterization and Sharp Medicinal Cauterization, categorized and ordered from head to foot, with forms of instruments and cauterization tools: and everything necessary for the procedure.
Second Chapter.
Regarding cutting and piercing, bloodletting and venting, and wounds: and the extraction of arrows and similar objects: all categorized and ordered with forms of instruments.
Third Chapter.
Regarding restoration, dislocation, and treatment of twisting and similar conditions: categorized and ordered from head to foot, with forms of instruments.
But before I recall the procedure with it, I must say about the benefits and harms of it: and in what complexion it is administered.
I say therefore that the discourse on the quality of the benefit of the cautery and its harm is a lengthy and subtle discussion, a science and an hidden secret.
Also, many wise people have spoken about it and disagreed on it: and for me, a little of their discourse is sufficient, fearing lengthiness.
I say therefore that the cautery is beneficial universally to all complexions, which are with matter and without matter: except for two complexions, which are the hot complexion without matter, and the dry complexion without matter.
In the hot and dry complexion with matter, they disagreed. For some said that the cautery is beneficial in it. And others said the opposite of that, namely that the cautery is not suitable for the disease which arises from heat and dryness: for the nature of fire is heat: and it is inappropriate to be healed from a hot and dry ailment with something hot and dry.
And he who says the opposite said that through the cautery there is benefit in every hot and dry disease which occurs in human bodies: for when you compare the body of a man and its moistures to the temperament of fire, you find the body of a man to be cold.
And indeed I say through his words: because from experience it has already revealed that to me on several occasions.
However, it should not come to that unless one who has already been tested and trained in the chapter on the last exercise of cauterization, and knows the diversity of human complexions and the disposition of diseases in themselves, and their causes, and their accidents, and the duration of them.
From the other complexions there is no fear for you: especially in cold and moist diseases. For all doctors have now agreed on them: and they have not disagreed about treating them with cauterization.
And know, sons, that from the secret of healing with cauterization by fire, and its goodness over cauterization with burning medicine is this: for fire is simple, whose action does not reach beyond the part that is cauterized: and it does not harm another connected part except with slight damage.
The action of burning medicine reaches to that which extends from the members: and it may cause a disease difficult to heal in the member, and it may even kill.
But fire, because of its subtlety and the goodness of its substance, does not cause that, unless there is an excess.
Now this has become known to us through experience, because of the length of service and study with the art, and standing on the truth of things: and because of this, I am excused for the length of the discourse.
And if it were not, because it is not permitted to this my book, I would bring you the hidden secret in fire, and the quality of its operation in the bodies expelled by itself, by which it expels diseases demonstrated philosophically, which would be sharpened by your minds.
And know, O sons, that they disagree on the time when it is appropriate to perform cauterization, and they place the better time in spring.
And I say that cauterization is appropriate at all times: because the harm caused by the time is overshadowed by the benefit that is brought with the cauterization. And especially if the cauterization is for pains caused by necessary, strong, urgent pains that do not tolerate delay: because it is feared that a greater harm may occur, which enters due to the time, than a small harm.
And do not let this fall into your minds, O sons, which is not feared except by the common people and foolish doctors, namely that there is no recurrence of that disease which is cured by cauterization: and they place this consequence, and things are not as they think: because cauterization is only in place of medicine, which alters the complexion and dries the humors which are the cause why pains occur.
However, cauterization exceeds medicine by the speed of its healing and the power of its operation and the strength of its dominion: and it is possible for the disease to return at some time according to the complexion of the sick person, and the location of his disease, and its power: and what is prepared in his body from the aggregation of excesses in him: and what comes to him in his acquisition from foods and similar things from those causes, unless the disease is one for which cauterization is administered.
A subtle illness in the limb of few excesses and moistures, like a tooth cauterization, because of pain, and similar to it, for it is possible that the pain does not return in it. But that happens in few cases.
But the common saying again, that cauterization is the last resort of medicine, is a correct statement: not in what they intend by it themselves: for they believe that there is no cure which compares with medicine, nor with anything else after the failure of cauterization.
The matter is contrary to that, and the intention, that cauterization is the last resort of medicine, is not what it seems: for when we administer modes of cure in certain illnesses, and those medicines do not help, then we apply cauterization at the end, and it does help: thus it follows that cauterization is the last resort of medicine, not according to the understanding of the common people and many foolish doctors.
The ancients said that cauterization with gold is better than cauterization with iron: and they said this only because of the equality of gold and the nobility of its substance: and they said that the site of the cauterization does not produce pus. But that is not absolutely true: for I have already tested it and found that it does not do that in some bodies without other factors.
And cauterization with it is good and better than with iron, as they said. However, when you heat the cauterization with gold in fire, it is not clear to you when it is heated to the degree you want because of the redness of the gold: and when it quickly cools down, and if you add more heat to it, it melts in the fire and turns into sheets.
Therefore, the craftsman falls from that into employment: and because of this, the cauterization is done more quickly and closer with iron among us, from straightness to the operation.
And indeed I have already arranged this Chapter on Cauterization according to the chapters: and I have ordered them from head to foot: so that it may help the seeker find what they want from it.
Chapter II.
This cauterization is applied to the dominance of moisture and coldness over the brain: which two are causes of phlegm, and the abundance of fluids flowing from the head to the regions of the eyes and ears, and an abundance of sleep, and toothache, and sore throat: and generally all illnesses that occur due to coldness, such as paralysis, phlegm, epilepsy, apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
The method of cauterization is to instruct the patient to purge with a cleansing and dissolving medicine for three nights or four, according to the requirement of the patient's strength, age, and habit.
Then instruct him to shave his head with a novacula. Then have him sit between your hands in a square position, so that he has placed his hands on his chest.
Then place the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his eyes. Wherever therefore your middle finger reaches, mark that place with ink.
Then cauterize with olive oil; this is its form.
Then place it on the marked spot with ink, by the descent whereby your hand is gradually tightened, and you will rotate it. Then quickly remove your hand and look at the place.
If you see that the amount of the head of alkil or the amount of zehurub is now exposed from the bone, then raise your hand. And if not, apply your hand with the same iron, or with another one if it cools down: until the bones appear, which I have told you about.
Then take some salt, and dissolve it in water, and soak the cloth in it, and place it on the spot: and leave it for three days.
Then place on it a cloth soaked in butter, and leave it on the spot until the burn scab is removed. Then treat it with the ointment tetrapharmacon until it is healed.
They have said that the longer the wound remains open, it discharges pus: therefore it is better and more beneficial.
And some of them said that the skin should be cauterized down to the bone: and the cautery should be held until something of the density of the bone is burned.
Then it is scraped after that which was burned from the bone, then it should be treated.
And others say that it is necessary to use the cautery until it makes a strong impression on the bone so that the bone falls off, which becomes like the shape of a knife: or an instrument which women place with a small amount of ink: and they estimate that vapors of the head are exhaled from this location, and the wound is left open for a long time.
Then it should be treated until it becomes solidified.
To me, these two types of cautery do not seem to apply to everyone but only to certain individuals according to the way of fear.
And to leave it, in my opinion, is better for its safety.
For the head is weakened by the breaking of its natural continuity: as we have testified in other members: and especially when the head of the sick person is weak by nature: and indeed the first type of cautery is safer and better for me, and I use it: therefore act with it for safety.
Chapter III.
When chronic pain occurs throughout the entire head and persists in the patient, they use herbs, cochiis, head purges, oils, and emplasteries. And especially if it has already been cauterized with the cautery we mentioned and it does not help at all: then consider. For if the head of the patient is strong in its natural constitution, and is not weak, and finds intense cold: then cauterize with another cautery a little under it. Then cauterize the entire horn of his head with a cautery, so that it does not penetrate the skin, and uncover from the bone the amount we have mentioned. And cauterize it with one cautery on the back of his head, in the place which is called the vase: and it is the place where the cupping vessel is placed: and raise your hand in this, and do not uncover the bone. For the patient finds because of that a very severe pain, and different from the pain of all the other head cauterizations.
And I will say this is the Cautery in its place: and it must be a cautery with which the horns of the head are cauterized, and the back of it more subtly than the cautery with which the middle of the head is cauterized.
Chapter IV.
When pain and swelling occur in part of the head, or the pain extends to the eye, and it is cleansed with purifying medicines for the head, and the rest of the treatment which I mentioned in the divisions of diseases is administered, and if it does not improve: then cauterization on it is according to two methods: either cauterization with sharp burning medicine, or with iron.
The cautery with sharp and burning medicine is to take one garlic clove, and peel it, and cut off its ends from both sides. Then cut the painful area with a wide lancet until you make a place under the skin where the tooth is caught.
Introduce it under the skin until it is hidden; then bind over it with a poultice of proper constriction, and leave it for fifteen hours; then release it, and remove the garlic, and let the wound be for two or three days; afterwards apply to it a cloth soaked in butter until pus forms at the site; then treat it with an ointment until it heals.
And if you wish to do this with some burning medicines, which I have written about in the twelfth treatise, on Burning Medicines.
The cauterization of it with an iron is according to this method. A cautery with fire, whose form is this.
And it is called Clauilis: because the shape of its head is like the shape of a nail, in which there is something curved, and in the middle of it there is a small protrusion.
Then place it on the area and hold your hand steady: and you should rotate the iron gradually with speed: and the amount that is burned should be according to the thickness of the skin, like its midpoint. And lift your hand so that the artery below is not burned and a flow of blood occurs.
Then soak the bandage in salt water, and place it on the area, and leave it for three days: then apply the bandage with butter: afterwards treat with ointment until it heals.
And if you wish, cauterize this half of the head with the second knife tip of the Cauterizer. And beware of cutting the artery in this half of the head, not properly the old one.
On the method of cauterizing in the old half of the head.
When you treat half of the head, using what we have said from the previous treatment and what we have mentioned in the divisions of diseases, and if the treatment does not help: and you see from the illness that what we have said about the first cauterization with medicine or with fire is insufficient, then it is necessary to heat the knife cauterizer until it whitens after you mark the place of pain with a line whose length is half a finger, or something like that: and remove your hand once, and hold it until you cut the artery and reach the bone.
However, you must be careful not to cauterize the moving jaw used in chewing, so that the side or the nerve which moves it is not burned, causing spasms.
And be on guard and beware of the flow of blood from the artery that has been cut. For in cutting it there is fear, especially for one who does not know what he is doing, and who is not skilled or experienced: and he leaves the operation at the very beginning.
And I will come with a reminder of the treatment of blood flow occurring from an artery according to its method, and in its place in this book.
If you see from the illness that this cautery is not sufficient for it, and you see the body of the sick person tolerating the cautery in the middle of the head as we have narrated, treat the wound until it is healed.
And if you wish, administer the cautery that we mentioned in the chapter on the extraction of the artery with a cautery having two knives. For cautery is better than this and more beneficial.
Regarding the method of cauterization for ear pain.
When pain occurs in the ear due to cold and is treated with solutions and other treatments that we mentioned in the division, and the pain does not subside, then apply cautery with fire: and it is that which is called Punctum, whose form is this.
Then make punctures with it after igniting it around the entire ear, as it revolves: or around both, if the pain is in both at the same time. And keep the cautery away from the root of the ear for a moment after you have marked the places with encaustic: and let the quantity of cautery be ten points on the entire ear, and about that.
Then treat the areas until they heal.
Regarding the method of cauterization for torture.
Chapter VII.
Torture which is treated with cauterization is only of the kinds that occur from phlegm, according to what we said in the divisions of diseases.
And avoid cauterization for the kind that occurs from dryness and spasm of the nerve.
When you treat this kind of torture with plasters, and head purges, and gargles, and your treatment does not help, then it is necessary to cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, and the second a little below its temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips.
And place your cauterization on the opposite side of the affected area. Because softening does not occur unless in the part that appears healthy.
And the form of cauterization is to cauterize directly at the upper end of the ear under the horn of the head a little, and another at the temple, whose length should be according to the length of the thumb. And place your hand with the cautery until the amount equal to the thickness of the skin is burned.
And this is the form of the cautery, and it is a type of knife, whose shape is as mentioned before; however, it is not as fine as you see: and it must be a knife with a slightly excessive thickness.
Then treat the areas with what precedes: until it is healed.
On the method of cauterizing in old apoplexy.
When apoplexy becomes old, and you treat it with what we have said, and your treatment does not help, and the patient does not have a fever, then cauterize him with four cauteries on each horn of his head, and a cauterization in the middle of the head, as we have said, and a cauterization on the back of the head, according to what has preceded: and the method of the cauterization should be according to what has preceded.
It is also cauterized with a cautery on the mouth of the stomach: and it is the last resort.
Then it should be treated with what has preceded.
Chapter IX.
It is necessary that in the drink given first to the patient there be hyraceum and pills cleansing the brain.
Then shave the patient's head entirely, and place on the back of his head a plaster of mustard as described in the chapter on plasters: and apply it several times.
This is indeed the method of cauterization: and do it according to the same order which I said there.
If therefore he is healed by that, it is good. If not: then make three cauteries on the back part of his head, which should descend from the upper part of the head to the lower part of the eye: and place between each cauterization the thickness of a finger.
Then care for the cauterization, with what precedes it.
If however you wish for an addition, and the patient is tolerant of it: then make a cauterization in the middle. If you wish for an addition: then cauterize it over the two horns.
Then care for it until it heals: let the cauterization be oiled according to the form which was mentioned.
On the method of cauterizing in paralysis and softening.
Chapter Ten.
It is necessary that you proceed with the cleansing of the head with hellebore, and with what we have said.
Then shave the head of the patient: afterwards cauterize it with a cautery in the middle of the head, and with a cautery on every horn of the head, and with a cautery on the back of it, and with three on the cervical vertebrae.
If however you need in the illness a softening of the body more than those, and the patient is tolerant, and the illness is strong: then cauterize it with four cauteries on the vertebrae of the back, and the last with a cautery, until it is burned deeply from the skin as much as possible, and lift your hand. Then care for it until it heals: and thus oil the cautery.
On the method of cauterizing in epilepsy.
The epileptic is not cauterized, unless his epilepsy is due to phlegm.
Therefore, you should first cleanse his brain with hellebore and with the other treatments we have mentioned in the division: when the patient is severe, or tolerant in receiving medicines.
If it is a child who does not tolerate medicines, then a gargle and cleansing mastications for the brain are administered, after improving the food over many days.
Then shave his head, then cauterize it with one cautery in the middle of the head, according to the preceding method: and with another cautery on the back of his head, and with a cautery over all the horn of his head. If the patient is strong and tolerant, then cauterize him with the cauteries I mentioned for those having paralysis, and softening of the body over the cervical vertebrae, and dorsal vertebrae: and let it be an olive oil cautery according to the preceding method.
If the patient is a child, then apply a fine cautery according to this method.
Regarding the method of cauterizing in melancholy.
When the cause of melancholy is corrupted humors and thick phlegm, then cauterize him with the cauteries we mentioned for those having paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholy is an excess inclined towards melancholy, and the body of the patient is moist, then give him in drink that which will cleanse his brain, according to what has been mentioned in the division: then shave the head of the patient, and make afterwards a properly made tortella from linen, like a circle.
Then place it in the middle of the head: and the patient sitting squarely shall be held on all sides.
Then apply the ointment. And it is better from old sheep's butter. And heat it over the fire with moderate heat, to a degree that can be tolerated by a finger when inserted into it. Then clean it in the middle of his head in a circle, and leave it until it cools.
Do this for the patient once every week, along with the rest of his good regimen, until he is healed.
Or if you wish, cauterize it by making very many small points, except where you hold the hand with the cautery: let it be smelled.
For this type of cautery moistens the brain with its quality.
Then place on it a cloth soaked in butter or hen's fat.
On the method of cauterizing for water descending to the eye.
Chapter XIII.
When the beginning of water in the eye is declared to you by the signs I mentioned in the division, then begin and purify the patient, with what cleanses his head.
And keep him away from all moistures, and have him sit in a bath, on fasting for several days.
Then instruct him to shave his head, and cauterize it in the middle of his head. Then cauterize it over both temples with two cautery points, if the onset of water descent occurs in both eyes at the same time: or from one side, if the onset of water is in one eye: and cut off with the cautery all veins and arteries which are under the skin: and let the cautery be long in width across the temples: and beware of blood flow.
If you see anything of it, then cut it off immediately with whatever medicine is possible: and I will come with the wisdom which is in the extraction of arteries, and their cutting off, and beware of blood flow.
And sometimes it is cauterized on the neck, below two bones, with two finally produced cautery points.
Regarding the method of cauterizing in ancient tears.
When the tears of the eyes are ancient and persistent: and they are above the veins and arteries which are on the external surface of the head, it is verified that this is due to cold, phlegmatic excesses: then cauterize with the same cautery as I described in the onset of descending water, a cautery in the middle of the head, and two cauteries over both temples, and two cauteries on the neck below two bones. And if additional treatment is needed, then cauterize it on all sides of the eye carefully, above the end of the eyebrow with a small cautery.
On the method of cauterizing for nasal odor.
When you treat it with what we mentioned in the division and the treatment does not help: then hurry and give the patient infirmocochias for three nights; then shave his head and cauterize it with a medium cautery, with olive oil. Then cauterize it with a key cautery, two cauteries, above the eyebrows slightly under the hair.
And be careful of the artery, lest you cut it.
And this is the form of the key cautery.
On the method of cauterizing for the relaxation of the eyelid.
When the eyelid of the eye is relaxed due to illness or moisture, then cauterize the eyelid with one cautery, using this lunar cautery.
And if you wish, cauterize it slightly above the eyebrows with two cauteries on each side: and they should be placed away from the temples: and the length of each cautery should be according to the length of the eyebrow: and do not extend your hand with the cautery, but according to the amount that the third eyelid is burned.
On the method of cauterizing the eyelid when the hairs turn and pierce the eye.
Cauterization is done in two ways: either with fire; or with burning medicine.
In cauterization with fire, instruct the patient beforehand to remove his hairs, if he is one of those who clean them, until they grow out and are even. If they prick him at their origin: then bind his eyes with a cloth, so that they do not move, until they heal.
When they grow out and are even, then place the patient's head in your lap: then mark above the eyelids of his eyes with a stencil, in the shape of a myrtle leaf: and let the beginning of the mark be near the hairs.
Then place the cautery imbued in egg white: or in psyllium mucilage on the eye.
Then heat the cautery, which is of this form.
Then cauterize over the figure you marked gradually in many places until the surface of the skin, which is like the shape of a myrtle leaf, is properly burned entirely visible.
And the sign of the healing of your work is: if you see the eyelid already contracting, and the hairs rising at the point of the eye.
Raise then your hand then: and leave him for three days.
Then place the cautery with butter on it until the eschar is removed. Then care for it with ointment until it is healed.
If any of the hairs return after an hour, and the eyelid softens: then apply the cautery again to that place, as you did at first.
If the hairs are on the lower [lid]: then cauterize it until it rises to its natural position: and equalize so that the hairs do not poke the eye.
It is that you should instruct the patient to let the hairs grow until they lengthen and even out. Make a shape of a myrtle leaf from cloth paper.
Then take from known soap and from unslaked lime one ounce each; then grind them together well, and make it quickly so that it does not cool. Then spread it over the paper you made in the shape of a myrtle leaf, and place it over the eyelid of one or both eyes. And place under the eye a cloth soaked in egg white: and let the patient's head be in your lap.
And place your index finger on the medicine and press it for a moment. And you should move it whenever the patient feels the bite of the medicine: for its bite is like fire.
Therefore, while this bite which he discovered persists, then discontinue the medicine, and move it with your finger. Therefore, when the bite ceases, then remove the medicine, and wash the eye with water.
And then consider, if you see the eyelid rise, as it rises with contraction by fire or with incision, it is good: and if not, then repeat on it from the medicine on the spot where the medicine does not leave a mark and does not darken, until your operation equals and the eye contracts.
Then place Cow-dung with butter on it until the burned skin is removed. Then treat it with a diaphoretic ointment, or another, until it heals.
And it is necessary for you during the operation to guard with utmost caution that nothing from the medicine falls into the eye.
If the eyelid softens after some days, and something struggles out from hairs in the eye, then repeat the medicine on the spot that softens from the eyelid itself, as you did at first. Then treat it until it heals.
And this is the form of the myrtle leaf.
And you should know that the eyes of humans differ in size and smallness. Therefore, let your consideration be according to this: and the way of righteousness is not hidden from him who has a zeal for this art.
On the method of cauterizing in lacrimal fistula.
When you treat a fistula, with what we have said about the divisions of diseases, and your treatment does not help: then, you must cauterize it according to this method.
Instruct the patient to place his head in your lap, and let the attendant hold his head between his hands in such a way that it does not move or shake with his head.
Then place a cloth soaked in egg white or in psilios mucilage over his eye: then cauterize with fire, the form of which is this.
Let it be concave, like the shape of a vulture's feather quill from one end, with which the cauterization is done: and if you want it to penetrate to the other end, and if you want it to go upwards, try it thus.
However, this concave shape is better for your work.
Then express the fistula if it is open, and extract the pus from it, and dry it: and if it is not open, then open it and extract its pus.
Then place the cauterization tool, which is made very hot, on it.
And hold your hand near the cauterization tool by the eye, towards the nasal side, so that your hand does not waver or disturb the patient: and place the cauterization tool on the eye fat, and burn it.
If therefore you reach with the beginning of your cautery up to the bone, it will be well. And if not: then apply the cautery once, or twice, if you need that: and leave it for three days.
Then apply a poultice with butter, and treat it with a drying ointment until it heals.
If forty days have passed and it has not healed: then apply a sharp corrosive medicine over it until the bone is exposed: and scrape it according to how it comes in its chapter.
And there is another method of the cautery for fistulas, which some first mentioned. Attend to the location of the fistula and find it: then place a fine camahan into the fissure, that is, a fine cannula, whose form is this. And pour into it the quantity of a drachm of molten lead, and hold your hand with a good retention of the cannula, and do not move the patient at all, so that the molten lead does not run or reach his eye.
And it is necessary to place on the patient's eye a poultice soaked in egg white, or in water.
For the lead burns the site of the fistula and heals it with a marvelous healing.
If the fistula is healed with what we have said about the cautery and treatment, it is good. And if not, then it is necessary to administer the nasal passage and redirect the fistula to the course of the nose, according to how it will come to its own proper place.
On the method of cauterizing in fissures of the lips.
Fissures often occur on the Lip, which are called Chaps, and especially on the lips of children.
Therefore, when you treat these fissures, with what we have said in the division of diseases, and if the treatment does not help, then make a small knife-shaped cautery with fire according to this form.
And its concavity should be according to the fineness of the knife.
Then place it ignited quickly on the fissures until the cautery reaches the depth of the fissures.
Then treat it with cerote until it heals.
On the method of cauterizing in oral fistulas.
When an abscess occurs at the root of the gum, or in the palate, or at the roots of the teeth: then it forms pus and bursts: afterwards it becomes chronic, and pus runs, and a fistula is formed: then you treat it, and if the treatment does not help, then you must heat a cautery according to its size so that it fits into the fistula. Then insert it heated into the opening of the fistula and hold your hand until the heated iron reaches its depth and end: do this once or twice.
Then treat it afterward with what we have said about the treatment until it is healed.
If therefore the pus is removed and it heals, it will be good. And if not, then it is necessary to expose the place and remove the corrupted bone according to what will come upon its head.
On the method of cauterizing in gums and softened teeth.
When the gum is softened due to moisture and the teeth are loosened, and you treat it with medicines and it does not improve: then place the patient's head in your lap.
Then with a fire cauterize it, whose form will come after this, so that you place a cannula on the tooth: and insert into it a ignited cauterium quickly: and hold your hand for a moment until the patient feels the heat of the fire has reached the root of the tooth.
And lift your hand: then repeat the cauterization several times, as you wish.
Then the patient should fill his mouth with salt water and hold it for one hour: and then spit it out.
For the loose tooth is secured, and the softened gum is tightened, and the corrupted moisture is dried.
On the method of cauterizing for tooth pain.
When the pain of the tooth is due to cold, or there is cold in it, or a worm, and treatment with medicines does not help: then cauterization is applied in two ways: either cauterization with butter: or cauterization with fire.
The cautery of it with butter is to take cow's butter and boil it in an iron spoon or in a vessel. Then take the cloth and wrap it over the end of the bandage. Then submerge it in boiled butter: and place it on the painful tooth quickly, and hold it until it cools: then repeat it several times, until the heat penetrates to the root of the tooth.
And if you wish, submerge wool or cloth in cold butter, and place it on the aching tooth: and place a heated iron on top of it until the heat reaches the deep cavity of the tooth.
The cautery of it with fire is to use a brass tube or an iron tube. And let there be something thick on the body of it so that the sharpness of the fire does not reach the mouth of the patient.
Then with fire cauterize it, whose form will come: and place it on that tooth: and hold your hand until the cautery cools.
Do this several times, for the pain will be removed, either on that same day or another day.
And it is necessary after applying that cautery that the patient fill his mouth with good butter and hold it for one hour: then spit it out.
And this is the form of the cautery.
Cauterize with whichever end you wish according to what is possible: and this is the form of the tube.
On the method of cauterizing in strophulus.
When strophulas are caused by phlegm and cold humidities, and are not obedient to digestion through medicines, and you wish to digest them quickly: then use a concave cautery, whose form is this.
Having two open ends, so that smoke may escape from the cautery at one end: and place it ignited upon the aposteme once, and a second time if needed, until it reaches the depth of the aposteme.
If the aposteme is small: then place the cautery according to the size of the aposteme.
Then leave it for three days, and place upon it a poultice infused in butter until what the fire has burned is removed.
Then treat it with tooth ointment until the cane-shaped form heals.
On the method of cauterizing in hoarseness of voice and constriction of breathing.
When humidities overcome the lung channel, and especially when it is with a cold disposition, then it is necessary that the patient be first evacuated with dissolving medicines.
Then cauterize it at the nockeri near the root of the throat in a depressed area: and beware, lest you reach the throat with the cautery, nor on the skin, except slightly.
Then cauterize it with another cautery near the joint of the neck at its last vertebra ultimately: and let the cautery be according to the manner which preceded.
Then care for it with what has precedeed until it heals.
On the method of cauterizing in diseases of the lungs, and cough.
When cough and disease of the lungs are from cold humidities, and the patient does not have fever, nor consumption, and the disease is chronic: then cauterize it with two cauteries above the clavicle in depressed, mild, empty places. And with another cautery in the middle of the chest between the two nipples: and let the cautery be a cannula according to the form which preceded.
And if you wish your cauterization to be done by pricking with a cautery which is called Point, whose form preceded in the pricking of ear pain: and let the pricks be from thirty points up to about another.
Then care for it with what has precedeed until it heals.
And now let the cautery have three branches: according to this form. Therefore, it is alleviated with that cauterization when you do three cauteries with it once.
Chapter XXVII.
When the head of the helper is dislocated due to moisture and does not return to its place at the time of its usual return from dislocation until it becomes accustomed to returning, then it dislocates from a small movement, which occurs as we have already testified, then you must first reduce the dislocation. Then the patient should lie on their back or on the healthy side. Then lift the skin that is inside the Titillici upward with the fingers of your left hand: and if the joint dislocates inward.
Then take a cautery with two prongs heated by fire. Its form is this.
Then cauterize the skin until it penetrates to the other side, and the figure of the cauterization will come with four cautery marks.
And sometimes the cauterization is done with a cautery having three prongs, hence the figure of the cauterization then has six marks: and the prongs are according to the fineness of the wire.
And this is the form of the cautery having three prongs.
And sometimes one is added to this manner, hence there are eight cautery marks.
Then place ground onions with salt on the cautery. Then make the patient adhere to tranquility, so that the limb is not moved for some time until it is strengthened.
And if the dislocation is upward, and that rarely happens, then cauterize it above the shoulder with a key cautery or by puncturing with many cauters.
For the joint is strengthened, and the moisture is removed: and the sick person is healed.
On the method of cauterizing the stomach.
When cold and excessive moistures occur in the stomach, causing it to deviate from its natural disposition, and phlegm increases around it, and usual methods of treatment are not beneficial: then the sick person should lie on their back and extend their legs and hands. Then cauterize with three cauters, a spoon-shaped cautery of the size of one finger and a key cautery, and two cauters below from both sides of the single cautery, until the shape of the cauters forms a triangle. And space them apart so they do not join, when they would form pus.
And the depth of the cautery should be two-thirds the thickness of the skin.
And the shape of the cauters should be according to this form without addition: and if you wish, cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach according to this form: and let the cautery which is used for this cautery be one according to the shape of a circle according to this form.
And the stomach is cauterized by pricking one who fears this cautery: and it is to mark a point on the stomach according to the size you wish with encaustic; then cauterize it with a puncture cautery; then treat it with the preceding treatment until it heals.
On the method of cauterizing the cold spleen.
When pain occurs in the spleen due to cold and moisture, or from thick wind, until it departs from its natural complexion by expelling excesses, and the patient is treated with what we have said but does not improve: then the patient must lie on their back, and mark out three cautery points with encaustic according to this figure and in the same quantity below the spleen near the hypochondria, where a person's elbow reaches. And let there be space between each cautery equal to the thickness of a finger, and let the cautery be straight according to the length of the body, and do not press your hand with the cautery too much.
And let the quantity burned be according to the thickness of the skin, a quantity not exceeding half of it: and let the patient stand on their feet.
If, however, he cannot stand, then let him lie down, with his legs extended and arms raised.
This is the form of the cautery.
And it is possible for you to cauterize these points with a knife cautery when you have finesse and prudence in the art.
And beware that you do not proceed too deeply in cauterization, so that the thickness of the entire skin is burned, causing the whole body to be burned and reaching the intestines: for the skin there is thin, so be aware of this.
On the method of cauterizing abscesses of the liver.
When it happens that a swelling appears and you want to know if this pus formation is in the substance of the liver or in its covering: then if it is in the substance of the liver, the patient suffers from pain and heaviness without sharpness; and if it is in the covering of the liver, there is intense sharp pain with it; and you see now that its treatment has tired out its doctors.
Therefore, the patient should lie down on his neck. Then mark the place of the pus formation with cautery: then heat the cautery which resembles a rod. And this is its form. And cauterize with it once, until the skin is entirely burned and reaches the siphac, until all the pus comes out: then treat it with the treatment for burnings, until it heals.
And one should not use this type of cautery unless their study in the art of medicine is prolonged: and through whose hands such illnesses occur repeatedly with experience: then indeed they may dare to perform such an operation.
But to leave it alone is better in my opinion.
Regarding the method of cauterizing in pleurisy.
The ancients said, use a cautery with roots of aristolochia for cold pleurisy in the following manner. And it is that you take from the dried long roots of aristolochia one longer root, which is found among them, and let it be as thick as a finger. Then submerge it in oil: and ignite it in fire. Then cauterize with one cautery where the fork joins the neck, and with two small cauteries under the slightly inclined glands on the side that is below the beard.
And with two cauteries also where the fifth and sixth ribs incline towards the back slightly: and with another cautery in the middle of the chest, and another above the stomach. And with three cauteries from the back: one where the two spatulas meet: and with two cauteries from the two sides of the chest, the lower cautery being between the two spatulas.
And you should not compress your hand with the cautery, but let the skin be clearly smelled.
And some ancients have said that there are those who use a cautery similar to a rod: they heat it and insert it between the ribs until they reach the abscess with it, and the pus comes out: as we have said regarding the abscess of the spleen.
But in this perforation with the cautery, there is a fear that either the patient dies immediately, or an ulcer forms at the site, which has no cure.
Regarding the Method of Cauterizing the Spleen Chapter XXXII.
When you treat spleen disease, with what we have said about treatment in the division of diseases, and your treatment does not help, then cautery is applied in three ways, which are all correct.
One of which is to make three cauters, or four by lining according to the length of the spleen according to the figure of the liver's cauterization, whose figure preceded.
And let there be between each cauterium the thickness of a finger, or more or less.
And let the method of the cauterium, which we have mentioned in the cauterization of the liver, be equal.
And do not press your hand with the cautery: and let the patient lie supine on his back.
And another method of cauterization is: to ignite a cautery having two prongs, which we have mentioned in the chapter on the dislocation of the shoulder: and elevate the skin which is directly over the spleen, where the left elbow of the patient reaches: and let your elevation be such that you raise the skin according to the width of the body, so that the cauterizations fall according to the length of the body.
Then insert the two prongs that are very hot until you penetrate the skin from the other side: then withdraw the cautery: thus four cauterizations are made.
And if you wish, cauterize with another cautery having three prongs.
Then care for the cautery after you leave it to emit pus for many days: for it is more beneficial than all that have preceded in the treatment.
Regarding the method of cauterization in hydrops.
Cautery does not apply in hydrops, unless properly positioned.
When you treat the water swelling with the methods of cure that we have mentioned in the division, and if the treatment does not help, then you must cauterize it with four cauterizations around the navel, and one cauterization on the stomach, and another cauterization on the spleen, and a cauterization on the liver, and two cauterizations behind the back between the vertebrae, and one in line with the chest, and another in line with the stomach: and let the depth of the cauterization be close to the thickness of the skin.
Then leave the cautery open so that it may discharge pus over a long period of time.
And do not evacuate the patient from treatment after cautery with it: which requires that two intentions be combined: and healing will hasten to him with God's help.
The form of the cautery with which the stomach is cauterized should be key-shaped: according to its previous form: and that with which the back is cauterized should be olive-shaped: according to its previous form.
On the method of cauterizing the feet and legs.
When abscesses form in hydrops and are filled with yellow water: you must cauterize on the back of the foot at the nockerati, which is between the auricularis and anularis: and lift your hand with the cautery, and do not twist it: then lift your hand: and do not repeat it at all.
For yellow water will exude, and the cautery should be in this form.
Then make two cauteries on each leg, and let the cautery be made with the knife-like end of the cautery: and let a cautery be made along the length of the leg, one below the knee, and another below it, about the middle of the leg: and on each hip two cauteries: and leave the open cautery without treatment for a long time: so that some water may sweat out of it: then treat it with the other things we have said.
On the method of cauterization for abdominal treatment.
Chapter Thirty-Five.
When the abdominal ailment arises from cold and humidity, weakening the retaining and digestive powers in the stomach and intestines: and it is treated with methods of healing but does not heal: and you see the patient tolerating the cautery of abundant power, then cauterize him with a large cautery on his stomach, according to what precedes in the cautery of the stomach with the circular cautery, and four subtle cauteries around the navel, with a subtle claw-shaped cautery: and a large cautery on the alcatin above the alhosos, or two cauteries.
And if you see excessive humidity and the patient tolerating it, then cauterize him with a cautery on the comb area, and a cautery on all the ilium: and perhaps add two small cauteries on the stomach near the large one.
For it is an effective treatment, whose benefit does not fail.
On the method of cauterizing hemorrhoids.
Chapter Thirty-Six.
When there are many old hemorrhoids in the anus, or one, and they arise from thick, cold humors, or corrupted moistures, and are treated with what we have said in the section on treatment, but if the cure does not help: then cauterize with three cautery points above the lower spine under the almeidati somewhat triangularly, and beneath the navel with a cautery almost two digits away.
And if you think that his stomach is overly cooled, and his food is not digested, and you see his face swollen with pus, then cauterize him on the stomach with a large cautery, as previously described: and with a cautery on his liver, and another on his spleen with a key-shaped cautery: and leave the cautery open for some time: then treat him until he is healed.
Chapter XXXVII.
When you cut off althelul, then heat the cautery which resembles a rod. Then insert the heated cautery into the cut althelul: and hold it with your hand until the cautery reaches the opening of the vein from which blood flows: do this once or twice.
If there are many althelul, then cauterize each one with a cautery as we have described. Then treat them with what helps heal them from ointments until they are healed.
And if you cauterize it with a large cautery on the alcatin, it is less effective in treatment.
On the method of cauterizing an anal fistula.
Chapter Thirty-Eight.
When the patient does not obey the cutting and procedure which we have described in its place, and is terrified by it, perhaps he is healed with a cautery.
When therefore an anal fistula occurs in someone and becomes old, pus runs from it, and corrupted humors. It is therefore more appropriate to probe it with a fine探针. Then know the quantity of its depth with a probe.
Then ignite the cautery, which is like a rod. Then insert the ignited cautery into the fistula itself and the amount in which the nail entered.
And repeat the cautery on it until all the corrupted bodies are burned, once, or twice, or thrice, according to the amount of your need.
And guard yourself from burning the nerve, if it is there, or large veins: or if the fistula leads to the bladder or to the intestine, then guard yourself from all these areas.
And do not do this unless the fistula is in a fleshy area: and you think that it is not penetrating.
Then care for the area until it heals.
If the area is sealed and materials are removed from it and remains so for a long time: then you know that it is now fully healed.
And if materials do not separate from it, then you know that it is penetrating, or there is a corrupted hole in its depth, or something like that, of which the recollection will come in its place.
Regarding the method of cauterizing the kidneys.
When pain occurs in the kidneys due to cold or severe flatulence, and it is reduced because of the illness of the infirm, then it is necessary to cauterize it over almethen on the kidneys, with a nail-shaped cautery over the entire kidney, as previously mentioned.
And perhaps we cauterize it a second time in the almidah. Therefore, three lined [things] will come. Therefore, they will be more final in healing.
On the method of cauterizing the bladder.
When debility and softening due to cold and moisture occur in the bladder, so that the patient cannot retain urine, then cauterize it on the lower part of the sumen above the bladder, where the hairs of the comb begin, and with one cautery on the right side of the sumen, and another on its left: and let the length of that lateral cautery be according to the size of the thumb knot: and cauterize it with the lower back cautery, or two cauters if necessary for that: and let it follow the previous cautery at the clavicle.
On the method of cauterizing the womb.
When cold and moisture occur in the womb, preventing conception and corrupting its menses, and delaying their onset, and pain occurs at their arrival, then it is necessary to cauterize it with three cauters around the navel, as we said in the cauterization of the bladder, and with one cautery below the scapula on the back, or with two cauters: and let the cautery be at the clavicle.
On the method of cauterizing the ankle in dislocation.
When mucous humidities are poured out to the hip socket of Anchae, and become the cause of its departure from its place: and the sign of this is that one leg is extended over the other when they are placed side by side: and the site of dislocation is found empty in it.
Therefore, you must cauterize the affected area over the hip socket of Anchae with a similar circular cautery: after you mark it with encaustic around the circumference of the socket, as it turns: and let the socket itself fall in the middle of the circle.
If this cautery is not available to you, then cauterize it with three cauteries using a large oil cautery: and the depth of the cautery should be according to the thickness of the entire skin.
Then care for it until it is healed.
Regarding the method of cauterizing in sciatica.
When pain occurs in the hip socket and its cause is cold and humidities: and the patient is treated with what we mentioned in the division, but the treatment does not help and it becomes chronic: then it is necessary to relieve the patient of thick humors with foul pills, or with artificial pills, and similar ones. Then cauterize him.
And the method of cautery for this is according to two methods: either a cautery with burning medicines, or a cautery with fire.
The cauterization with fire is according to many methods.
One of which is to cauterize above the lid of its container with three triangular cauteries, according to this shape. And give them a good or bad depth. And let the space which is between each cautery be the thickness of a finger: and let the cautery be olive-shaped.
Sometimes, however, the cautery is made in the middle on top of the lid of its container. Therefore, there are four cauteries.
And if you wish to cauterize with a circle, whose form preceded in the cauterization of the dislocation of the lid, with one: so that the circle contains the entire lid.
And burn the thickness of the entire skin.
This is the method of cautery for sciatica, when the pain is attached to the lid itself, and does not extend to the hip and leg.
If it extends to the hip and leg, then cauterize it with two cauteries on the hip, on the spot where the patient indicates there is pain, and with your cautery on the thigh four fingers towards the woodland side: and let the cautery be knife-shaped.
And let the depth of the cautery be according to the thickness of the skin.
If the patient indicates that the pain extends nearly to the toes of the foot, then cauterize it where they indicate with a pinpoint cautery, three, four, or more if it is needed.
And if he indicates that the pain is under the knee towards the leg, then cauterize that place with one surgical cautery.
And be careful in all your cauterizations so that you do not go too far with the cautery to the point of burning a nerve or a large artery, and thereby bring about a very harmful damage or contraction on the patient.
And indeed I have seen one or another of those who cauterized above the ankle and went too far in the cauterization, and the leg swelled until a tumor followed to the foot, and it was completely perforated and the entire foot corrupted; then peritonitis occurred, and death followed that.
If the pain is in both parts at the same time, cauterize both according to this method.
And some wise men have said about the cauterization of an anchor, for which this is the method of cautery. Make a similar instrument from iron, whose diameter is half a palm: and let it be at its opening according to the thickness of a kernel of a finger, or slightly less: and within that instrument be a third instrument.
And let the space between each instrument be the width of a thumb joint: and let the instruments be open on both sides: and let their depth be about one or two thumb joints: and make them handles of iron suitably fitted to the instruments.
Then it is heated in the fire until it turns red and throws out sparks: then it is placed on the anchor's ulcer of the patient lying on their healthy side. Therefore, cauterize him with three round cauteries in one turn.
Then leave him for three days. Afterwards, apply plasters with butter: and leave the wound open for many days. Then treat him with ointment until he is healed.
Albucasis says, we have used this type of cautery little, O sons, because of the terror of its appearance: and moreover, because we find few who can endure it.
However, it is among the good cauteries for one who endures and finds its proper place.
The cautery with burning medicines is such that you make two jars having a perforated ring, into which descends the hinge of its lid made of bronze or iron, the length of the wall: each should have two knobs, or something like them, in height.
And let the space between the two be the width of a finger, and let them be open below and above: and let them be able to clamp together according to this form.
Then place it on the lid of the anchor, with the patient lying on the healthy side. And press your hand strongly on the lid of the anchor. Then pour between the two circles with hot water, which has been heated briefly with fire, and keep it for the duration of an hour: and let the patient tolerate its bite and its burning, for he will find the bite like fire, until the bite subsides.
Then lift your hand with the instrument, and clean the entire area around the wound with warm water: then leave it for three days.
And place butter on it until the blackness of the burn is removed: and leave it for several days, and pus will flow from it. For it is the last in healing.
Then treat it with ointments until it heals.
If the pain extends to the thigh or leg: make a poultice on what contains water, according to how you did on the wound equally.
And this is the method of warm water: and I have already written about it in the treatise on the correction of medicines. Take alkali and unquenched lime, each one part: grind both, and place them in a new pot, whose lower part has one small hole through which a finger can pass: and place another glass pot under the bottom of the pot: then pour sweet water over the alkali and lime to submerge both by a finger's depth: after which you should press them with your hand firmly: and leave the pot until the sharp water descends into the lower glass pot.
Then collect all that water and pour it over another lime: and distill until it is renewed.
For it will then be very strong in sharpness, which is used in many medical procedures and in the cauterization of other parts. For it causes its own burning action.
And among the medicines are those with which the ankh is cauterized, such as tesiie, and mango paste, and lime with soap, so that each is thoroughly mixed.
And Galen indeed reported the treatment of an ancient man who was cured of the pain of the ankh and the sciatic vein: and he praised it greatly. And he said that no other treatment was needed, and that he was cured in one attempt, until he reported that he perhaps entered a bath carried in and exited it already healed.
And it is taken from green seitaragi: and if green is not found, take the dry, fresh: and grind it much with some fat, and place it on the ankh where there is pain, or on the leg, or on the hip: and bind it, and leave it for a duration of three hours, or to the extent that the patient feels the sedation of the burning. Then put him into a bath.
When therefore his body becomes moist, put him into the bath. For the pain retreats, and it is healed.
And know that one should not use the cautery with these medicines unless after the evacuation of the body.
And Dioscorides also said that goat dung, when used to cauterize the sciatic vein, helps it: and the cautery is made in this way. Wool is taken and soaked in old oil and placed on the deep place which is between the big toe of the foot and the instep, and it is closer to the instep.
Then take dried goat dung, and ignite it in fire until it becomes charcoal.
Then place it on the wool, and leave it until it is extinguished. Then do it again. Do not stop doing it until the sensation reaches the nail through the treatment and the pain ceases.
And this method of cauterization is called Vaccinum cautery.
Regarding the cauterization for back pain.
Pain in the back sometimes occurs due to various causes, whether from a fall, or from a blow, or from excessive evacuation, and similar things, from the infusion of cold and moist matter; and cauterization is only applicable in this particular type which arises from the infusion of cold matter.
Therefore, after evacuating the patient with foul pills and similar treatments, three lines should be made on the back where the pain is, according to the width of the area itself. After marking with encaustic on each line five cauteries or more according to the quantity that comes from the patient's tolerance and strength: and the cauterization should be done with a cautery point.
And if you wish, cauterize with three or four cauteries using a median claw cautery according to this form.
On the method of cauterizing at the beginning of gibbosity.
This disease often affects small infants.
And the sign of the onset of this in children is that it occurs upon him a constriction in breathing during elevation and movement: and you find at the last vertebrae of the spine and its joints that it has already begun to protrude above the other vertebrae.
When therefore you see it and wish to treat it, then cauterize it with a circular cautery according to this form.
And let the cautery take effect on every part of the vertebra equally: and if you wish, cauterize around the vertebra with a point cautery in two lines, or three: and let the points be close to each other.
Then care for the area until it heals with what we have said.
And beware of applying the cautery to the gibbosity that occurs in nerve spasm.
On the method of cauterizing in gout and joint pains.
When joint pains are caused by cold humidities that are dispersed to any part of the body, then when the pains occur in the feet, it is customary among physicians to properly call this gout.
When therefore gout of cold causes is treated with methods of cure and the pains are not removed, then the cautery removes them.
And it is so that you cauterize him after evacuation around the joint of the feet, with many cauteries: and let the cautery be Oleander.
And if you need to prick on the surface of the foot, then do it with a puncture cautery. And if the pains ascend up to the knees or other joints, and this often happens, then cauterize over the entire knee with three or four cauteries on all sides, with this same Clavic cautery.
And if more of this cautery are necessary for you, then cauterize it. And do not plunge your hand with the cautery, but let it be about the thickness of the skin only.
And if the pains ascend to the knees and the back, then apply what we have said about the cautery in its chapter.
And if the pains are only in the hands, then prick around the wrists as two lines are drawn.
And if the pains remain in the fingers, then prick them on every joint and on the palm of the hand.
And if the pains ascend after days to the elbows or shoulders, then cauterize both on all sides.
And do not evacuate the patient from good regimen or from the reception of medicines. For if good regimen is established and the phlegm is evacuated, he will be healed with the help of God by this cautery.
On the method of cauterizing in hernias.
When a hernia occurs in the groin, and the intestine or bowel descends near the testicle, then you must advise the patient to abstain from eating on his day. And let him use laxatives, so that the stool may descend from his abdomen.
Then let him sit between your hands on his back: and advise him to hold his breath until the bowel or intestine appears or exits.
Then reduce it with your fingers, and mark with cautery below the hernia at the opening of the crest, with a mark whose end resembles half a circle directed towards the upper part of the body.
Then apply the cautery with this form of fire until it becomes white and emits sparks. Then reduce the intestine or bowel to its concavity. Then let the assistant place his hand on the area to prevent the intestine from protruding: and you shall have parted the patient's thighs, and placed a cushion beneath him, and another servant on his legs, and another on his chest who holds his hands.
Then place the cautery on the marked spot, with your hand holding the cautery straight. And hold it until you reach the opening with it: or repeat with it another time, if you have not reached the opening with it on the first try.
And wisely observe from the exit of the intestine during your cauterization hour, lest you burn it, and by this happen to the patient either death or great harm.
And you should know that when you do not reach the mouth with the cautery, your operation does not help.
And it is necessary that the cautery for infants be fine, according to their size.
Then care for it with other ointments until it heals.
And let the patient lie on his back for forty days until the wound is sealed.
And it is necessary that you provide nourishment for the duration of his healing, which soothes his stomach: so that the intestine does not come out during effort and defecation.
Then when he wants to rise after forty days, administer a properly made bandage, and let it remain for another forty days.
And he should be reduced from labor, and from fullness of food and drink, and from loud voices.
For when he follows this regimen, he is healed with complete healing.
And I will speak of the treatment of ruptures with incision in its chapter.
When ruptures occur in the rest of the abdomen and are initial, and you wish that they do not worsen, then cauterize the rupture with a round cautery according to its size: and let one-third of it be burned from then on. Then care for it with what we have said: and nothing more shall be added.
And some have said first: that the rupture should be cauterized with a triangular cautery, according to this shape.
After it is marked with encaustic, and a line is placed across the width on the upper side of the rupture, and another line below. And place your hand in the middle with a key-shaped cautery.
But the first cautery is easier and better.
Regarding the method of cauterizing for pains due to falls or blows.
Chapter XLVIII.
When pain occurs in some limbs due to a fall or blow, and that pain persists for a long time, and treatment with medicines does not help, then it must be cauterized with a Point cautery.
And the cautery should be appropriate for the entire member according to its size, and its tenderness, and its weakness, and its strength, and the location of the twist, and the pain from it.
If it is healed by the first cautery, it is good. If not: then repeat on the same cautery.
For it is customary for these pains to shift from one member to the adjacent one. Therefore, it is necessary to address them with cautery until the patient is healed.
Of the method of cauterizing in leprosy.
Lepers are sometimes greatly benefited by the cautery. And especially the type of leprosy that occurs due to the putrefaction of phlegm and melanchole: when you wish to cauterize it, consider carefully.
If the leprosy is stubborn, and you have treated it with what we mentioned in the division, and it does not diminish nor remain stable: and you fear that the corruption may spread over the entire complexion of the patient: then cauterize him on the head with five cauteries: one in the middle of the known part of the head, and the second below it towards the forehead at the end of the hair, and two on the two temples, and one behind on the nape of the neck.
And finally, apply your hand with the cautery for a moment until it makes a small imprint on the mouth, and the scabs are removed from it: so that the expiration of gross vapors from it may be alleviated, and cauterize also over the spleen itself, as previously described.
If the leprosy has already spread over the patient and appears clearly: then it is necessary to cauterize with these cauteries which we mentioned in the chapter, and a cautery on the tip of the nose, and two cauteries on both jaws, and two cauteries on the cervical vertebrae, and six on the dorsal vertebrae, and one large one on the alahosos near the tail bone and one above it, on the almeidati: and two on the hips: that is, one on each hip, and two on the knees: one on each knee, and two on the shoulders, and two on the elbows, and two on the tender areas of his chest: and cauterize him on every joint, from the joints of his hands and feet: and cauterize on every heel of his feet, and on the palms of his hands.
And beware of the nerves which are above the posterior part of the heel, lest you burn them.
And sometimes it is cauterized with one cautery on the mouth of the pelvis, and another on the mouth of the stomach, and another on the spleen.
And you should know that the more you apply the cautery, the greater the benefit and the more it helps.
And you should know that the sick person does not find pain in the cautery as much as healthy people do: because their body is already numb.
And it is necessary that the cauteries be of various sizes and smallness according to the limbs and joints: according to which precedes from the kinds of instruments.
Then treat the cautery with flour of the herb and honey, and continue the treatment until it is healed.
Regarding the method of cauterizing in stupor.
When some limb is numb and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, and does not heal, then cauterize the numb limb with cauteries according to the size or smallness of the limb.
And let your cautery penetrate slightly into the thickness of the skin. Then treat it with an ointment until it is healed.
And sometimes it is cauterized for a kind of numbness that affects the hand and foot at the vertebrae of the back near the exit of the nerves that move that limb: and the numbness is removed.
But let not one who is not wise in the anatomy of the members and the exit of the moving nerves presume upon it.
Chapter Fifty-One.
When Alvarus becomes old and none of the medical skills are effective on it: then cauterize over it with a deep cautery briefly, according to the thickness of the skin, until the whiteness is removed and its color changes.
Then treat it with the flour of the herb, and lentils with rose oil, and leaves of arnoglossa, and blood of a dove, and blood of a swallow: let there be one part of each; mix all these together, and spread them over cloth, and apply in place until it heals.
On the method of cauterizing in cancer.
When cancer is beginning and you wish to stop it: then cauterize it with a circular cautery around it, as it revolves.
The wise have said that it should be cauterized with the final cautery in the middle.
But it does not seem right to me: for I fear that it may ulcerate: and I have already seen this happen several times.
And it is better that it be cauterized around it with a circle, as we have said: or with many cauteries.
On the method of cauterizing in adubelati.
When someone has an abscess and its maturation is delayed either due to excess causing it or due to the age of the patient if they are frail and have little blood, or due to time and a need to hasten the maturation of the abscess, then cauterize around it with many small cautery points. Then release her. For it will hasten with the maturation.
If you wish to perforate it with a cautery, then use fire with the cautery, which has this form.
And place it in the middle of the abscess until it penetrates the skin: and let the cautery be applied so that the subsequent course of the disease may be alleviated.
Then care for it until it is healed.
About the method of cauterizing in a corrosive disease.
Chapter LIV.
A corrosive is nothing but corruption in a limb that spreads and corrodes it: just as fire eats dry wood.
If you see a corrosive in a place that can tolerate cautery with fire, then use many cauteries, small and large claviculae, according to what is suitable for the place where the corrosive is.
Then cauterize it from all sides until you root out the entire corruption, and nothing of it remains entirely.
Then leave it for three days, and place ground sulfur with oil on the cauterized areas until all the eschars are removed, and all corruption is gone.
Then treat it with flesh-producing ointments.
If you see that after three days flesh is born healthy, in which there is no corruption, it is good.
And if not: then apply the cautery again over what remains of the corrupted areas.
And it is sometimes treated with sharp medicine when corrosive. For it arises from the place of the cautery.
However, cautery with fire is faster in providing relief: and I have already mentioned its cautery with sharp medicine in the division: so take it there when you need it.
Regarding the method of cauterizing in claws and warts.
Chapter LV.
This illness often occurs in the lower parts of the feet: and it is a thick, filtered substance that harms the foot.
And there are indeed two methods of cautery for these: cautery with fire and cautery with hot water.
As for cautery with fire, make a concave cautery similar to the feather of a vulture: it should be made of iron according to the size that can contain the claw on all sides: and it should have fine edges.
Then place it ignited upon the nail. Then rotate the hand with the cautery around the nail until the cautery reaches the depth of the nail: and leave it for three days until it begins to discharge pus. Then apply plaisters to it with wild mallows, crushed with salt: and leave the plaister on it during the night. For it will be eradicated from its roots.
Then treat the area with a flesh-generating ointment until it heals.
If they are not converted and often occur on the surface of the body, especially in hands and feet: then apply cautery to them with warm water: and it is as follows, take a tube of metal, or iron, or from an eagle's quill: and place it over the nail, or althelul. Then pour a small amount of warm water into the tube: hold your hand, and rotate it with the pressure of your hand for a moment, so that the edge of the tube is impressed on the root of the nail, and let the warm water find its way to the depth, to the root of the nail: and let the patient wait a moment over the effect of the warm water's action for about an hour.
Then leave it, for the nail is eradicated with its roots.
Do this one by one until you have addressed all of them that are in the body.
Then treat them after they are eradicated with something that generates flesh from ointments.
On the method of cauterizing in trembling.
When trembling occurs in someone due to cold in the nerve, or from quartan fever, or another cause: then it is necessary to cauterize with four or five cauteries on the vertebrae of the back, and a caustic between each vertebra, and on his chest with a caustic, and on his stomach with a caustic.
For trembling is calmed with olive oil cautery, and recovery from cold illness is hastened.
On the method of cauterizing Albathir.
Chapter LVII.
Sometimes in the body, Albathir causes ugly boils, that is, pustules, which are caused by corrupted thick materials.
Therefore, when they first appear, they should be cauterized on the entire head of the pustule with a fine cautery using myrtle wood, the end of which is burned with fire. Or with the root of long aristolochia. Or with a lentil-shaped cautery.
And sometimes they are cauterized at the beginning of their expulsion according to this method: and they do not increase: and the excess causing them is dispersed, and they are healed from them.
However, it should be done after evacuation with bloodletting.
On the method of cauterizing in blood flow from an artery in a wound.
It often happens that blood flows from an artery which is cut at a wound, whether occurring externally, or at the incision of an abscess, or of a member's cautery, and similar cases; and it becomes difficult to stop it.
Therefore, when this happens to someone, then quickly reach with your hand to the opening of the artery, and place your index finger on it: and press it strongly until the blood is blocked under your finger, and nothing can escape from it.
