Therefore, you must extract what is apparent from them where the sight falls, after pressing the tongue with an instrument near the light, and it becomes clear to you what is in the throat.
And what is not apparent to you and hidden in the throat, you must make the sick person vomit before the food is digested in the stomach. For perhaps the attached matter will be expelled by vomiting.
Let the sick person swallow a piece of ginger, or the root of lettuce, or let them swallow a piece of dry bread: or take a piece of soft dried sea sponge: tie it to a string, then swallow it. When it reaches the place where the spines are, or the bone, and is pulled out, then it comes out.
If it does not come out with what we have said, then use an instrument made of lead according to this shape.
Let it be thicker than the radius for a moment, and at its end let there be a curvature, which he can introduce into his throat with ease: and let him hold his head raised upwards.
And let him be careful not to touch his epiglottis, so that he does not cause a cough, and push the bone or spine with it, or let the physician insert it with his own hand.
But what the sick person inserts is better: because of his knowledge of the location of the attached object: and push it downwards, or pull his hand upwards with the instrument, doing all this according to the amount prepared for him, until it comes out.
Regarding the removal of leeches.
Chapter XXXIX.
When the leech is treated with what I said in the division concerning treatment with medicines, and it does not help, then examine the patient's throat in front of the sun, or near the sun after you press his tongue with the instrument which I described to you.
If your sight falls upon a leech, remove it with a small hook, or with fine tweezers properly.
If it is not possible with them: then take a concave tube, and insert it into the patient's throat up to near the throat; then introduce a heated iron into the concavity of the tube. Do that many times: and let the patient abstain from water for the whole day.
Then let him take a vessel full of cold water, and open his mouth over it: and bring his mouth close to it, and let him not swallow anything from it: and move the water with his hand once an hour. For the leech immediately falls when it feels the water.
If it does not come out with what we have mentioned, then fumigate the patient with bugs, or with ashes using the instrument I described for fumigating the throat.
Do that many times, for it will fall.
And the method of operation in fumigation is to take a pot in which there are burning coals with fire: and the pot should be covered with a cover, in the middle of which there is a hole: and the end of the instrument should be placed in that hole.
Then throw the fumigation, and let the sick person put his mouth at the end of the tube, and close his mouth so that the fumigation does not escape, until you know that the fumigation has already reached the leech. For the leech will fall immediately.
If it does not fall, then repeat the fumigation many times.
And let the sick person endure thirst, and eat salty foods, and garlic, and not drink water.
Therefore, it is necessary to proceed with this regimen.
And this is the form of the instrument with which the leech is extracted from the throat when it falls upon it by sight.
It is similar to forceps, as you see: except that it has this curvature which is inserted into the throat. And the end of it is similar to the mouth of a bird which is called a stork, in which there is the roughness of a file: when it grasps something, it does not release it at all.
Regarding the opening of abscesses, their incision, and general care.
Chapter XL.
There are many kinds of abscesses, of various types, according to the recollection of them, that is, one and another in this book: and they are diverse in their puncturing and incision by two methods.
One is of the kind of abscess in itself and that which it encompasses from humidities.
And the second mode is due to the places where it occurs in the body.
For an aposteme occurring on the head is different from an aposteme occurring on the anus: and an aposteme occurring in a fleshy part is different from an aposteme occurring in joints: and each of them has its own judgment from the operation.
And among the apostems are those which should not be lanced until the pus in them is matured and complete: and among them are those which should be lanced while they are raw and do not mature according to completion.
Like the apostemes which are near the joints.
For when an aposteme occurs near a joint and extends to be part of it until what is around it putrefies, the ligaments or nerves of that joint may be corrupted: hence it is a cause nearer to the contraction of that member.
Or it is an aposteme near a principal member: for if you delay piercing it until it matures, it will harm either that member or the principal member through it.
Or it is near the anus, pierce it therefore while immature: and you should not lance an aposteme that is raw and undigested, unless it is near the anus, so that it does not putrefy deeply and extend to the interior of the anus, and become a fistula, or result in something at its end that cannot be healed.
You must know the time for lancing an aposteme that has matured according to completion: and this is when there is a subsiding of pain, recession of fever, and reduction in redness, and pulsation, and sharpness at the head of the aposteme: and other signs.
And it is necessary that you make the same perforation in the lower part of the abscess, and of more prominent elevation: and let the perforation go along the length of the body, if the abscesses are in parts of hands and feet, and areas of tendons, and cords, and nerves, and arteries, and finally in all equal places where there is no reflection.
In those that are reflected, proceed with the perforation according to that member.
When the abscess is in fleshy areas: then it is better to leave the perforation until its digestion is confirmed, as we have said according to the completion.
For if you pierce it before that, the course of the pus is prolonged, and there is much filth and dirtiness, and perhaps its lips and depth may harden.
And some abscesses are pierced according to the width of the body in necessity: or according to what the member needs.
And it is necessary that you administer a small perforation in small abscesses, and a large perforation in large abscesses: or many incisions according to the similarity of the size of the abscess.
And there are abscesses in which it is necessary that the skin be scooped out: and cut when it has become like cloth, and reached the point where it is already dead: such as those that occur in many, like dubet and buboes.
And there are some that are cut with a three-angled incision. And from them is one by which it is cut like the figure of a myrtle leaf.
Like the abscess of the groin.
And from them are those in which round incision and crescent-shaped incision are made: and similar to these from the incisions.
That which does not have a head, like mild superficial abscesses, should be pierced with a superficial puncture, or only flat.
And it is necessary, when the abscess is large, and has already collected much pus, and you pierce it, that you not hurry and extract all the pus at that hour: rather extract a part of it. Then cleanse the abscess until the next day. Then extract some of the pus again.
Do this repeatedly according to the progression, until it is expelled: especially if the patient is weak in strength, or a pregnant woman, or a small child, or an aged invalid: for the animal spirit is often resolved from the body with the discharge of pus: and perhaps the patient dies, and you do not perceive it.
Therefore, be cautious with this chapter with great care.
And after your piercing with which you pierce these abscesses, it is necessary to clean the wound: and observe. If the wound of the abscess is small, or it is a flat incision, then apply lint from linen, or old cloth. And if there is a large abscess, and many perforating cracks are present, then you must insert lint into every crack until they reach each other.
And if you have cut away part of the skin in an abscess, or scraped around it: then it is necessary to fill it with old felt, or as when a cloth is stitched, or shaved with linen down without moisture: and bind it until the third day.
Then discard it, and treat it with the appropriate ointment until it heals.
If a flow of blood occurs during your operation, then administer cold water and vinegar, after the cloth has been soaked in them: and place it on the site of the bleeding multiple times.
If the flow of blood persists, then it is necessary to administer treatment, and care, and powders, which I have described in many places in this book, and by division.
If it is during the winter season, and the site of the abscess is near many nerves: then it is necessary to pour powder with warm wine and oil: and place them on the areas.
And if it is during the summer, and the areas are fleshy: then it is necessary to place powders soaked in water and oil, or with wine and oil, and all of it should be cold. Until the third day arrives, as we have said, then it is necessary to open the abscess, and clean it, and administer what is appropriate for its treatment until it heals.
This is therefore what is necessary from the knowledge of the treatment of swellings universally.
According to the path of distinction, I have already spoken about every swelling, how the way to its cure is treated separately in chapters.
Chapter XLI.
On the incision of swellings that occur on the skin of the head.
Small swellings occur on the skin of the head, and they are of the kinds of Knots, which are contained in the membranes that serve as their sacks: they are like the fat of a hen.
And their kinds are many.
Some are fatty: some contain moisture similar to mud: some contain moisture similar to boiled dishes and poultices: and others similar to these, and some are hard like stone.
And in the incision of all of them and their removal, there is no fear, as long as an artery does not oppose at the site of their incision.
And the procedure in their incision is to examine them with an instrument whose form comes after this, which is called the Introducer, until you know what it contains.
For if it contains moisture, then cut it with a longitudinal superficial incision: according to this form.
And begin the incision from line b to line g. When the moisture is evacuated, then scrape the cyst that contains the moisture, and do not leave anything of it entirely.
For it often returns if something of it remains.
Then submerge the cloth in Egyptian ointment, if it is available: and if not, in water and salt: and fill the wound with it, and leave it until the next day. For it will corrode what remains from the cyst.
Then repeat over the cloth with the second Egyptian method, and the third, and if you need it, until you are confident that nothing remains from the cyst, then treat the wound with ointment until it heals.
If the abscess contains a fatty knot: then cut it according to this shape, with the incision having the form of a cross: and place hooks between the two lips of the incision, and scrape it from all sides: and attempt your skill in extracting the tissue that contains it.
If however the artery opposes you, then do what I will tell you next.
And similarly do for the abscess, if it is stony, by the same incision and treatment as we have said.
And the incision on a stony abscess is easier: because it contains little blood and moisture. And sometimes there are some of these abscesses that are on the head in certain individuals, which contain no moisture at all.
This is because I cut into an abscess on the head of an old woman, and found the abscess to be like a solid, hard, rough, white stone that could not be broken: and if anyone struck it, it would wound them.
In other swellings occurring on the head, besides these swellings which occur on the heads of children, and near the roots of the ears, the incision of all of them should be superficial.
Or make the puncture always from the lower part of them, so that the course of pus may be alleviated towards the lower parts.
Then care for it with what is appropriate for its treatment.
Regarding the incision of strophulas on the neck.
Chapter XLII.
These swellings often occur on the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin; and sometimes they occur on the rest of the body.
And regarding those that occur on the neck, there can be one or many: and they are generated from each other: and every strophula among them is within its own proper covering, just as it is with the knots and swellings of the head, as we have narrated.
And the types of these strophulas are many. And among them are stone-like ones: and there are those that contain moistures: and there are malignant ones that do not obey treatment.
In that one which you see among them of good disposition to the touch, whose color is clearly near the skin's color, and which moves to every part, and is not attached to the neck's nerves, nor to the vertebrae, nor to the artery, and is not deep: it is necessary to incise it superficially from the upper part to the lower part of the body along line b. to line g., and scrape it from all sides: and extend the two skin lips with a hook, or with multiple hooks if you need them, as we have said in the swellings of the head, and extract it gradually.
And it is for caution, so that a vein or nerve is not cut.
And let the scalpel not be very sharp: so that it does not add to your hand with the incision, or disturb the patient, and you cut what is not necessary.
If you cut a vein or artery and it prevents you from the operation, then apply ground zegi or certain powders that stop the flow of blood to the wound, and bind the wound, and leave it until the sharpness of the inflammation subsides and the wound softens: or it begins to turn and wants to become putrefied.
For the blood is stopped with a bandage. Return to your operation until you complete it.
Then probe with your index finger if anything of the small Strophulus remains; then cut them and clean them.
If there is a large vein at the root of the Strophulus: then you must not cut that Strophulus from its root: rather, you must tie it with a strong double thread and leave it until it falls off by itself without harm.
Then fill the wound with old cataplasm that you have already immersed in Egyptian ointment. Then care for it.
If the entire Strophulus is cut, then you must bring together the two lips of the wound: and sew it immediately, as soon as you see that there is no excess remaining.
If you see that there is excess remaining because of the size of the Strophulus, then you must proceed to cut its root and remove it: and apply the suture as we have said.
And which contains moistures from sties, pierce it with a superficial puncture: so that the site of its maturity may be apparent to you: and place the puncture from what follows next below in the body, as we said.
Then apply after the puncture a licinia with ointment, and similar things to it, so that it corrodes what remains of the corruption, until when you see the wound already cleansed: then treat it with a flesh-generating ointment until it heals.
Chapter XLIII.
On the incision of the epiglottis caused by an abscess occurring inside the throat.
The ancients said this incision in the epiglottis, and I have not seen anyone in our land who has done it: and this is the writing of their words.
In those suffering from synanche, however, it is necessary to avoid incising the epiglottis: for no benefit is gained by that: therefore, because all the veins and lungs are weakened.
In those who have a hot abscess in the mouth, or throat, or both tonsils, when there is no illness in the canal, it is necessary to use incision of the epiglottis, to avoid destruction which results from obstruction.
Therefore, when we want to do this, we should cut the epiglottis below three or four rings of the epiglottis, with a small incision in width, in what is between two rings by the amount that the section is in soft tissue, not in cartilage: and this place is suitable for incision because it is devoid of flesh, and blood vessels are distant from it.
If the surgeon is timid, then he must extend the skin of the throat with a hook. Then he should incise the skin until he reaches the canal: he should avoid the blood vessels, if he sees any of them.
Then he should cut the sifac that we mentioned: it is indicated by the discharge of phlegm from the canal when it is severed, and by the cutting off of the voice.
And leave the wound open for some time.
Therefore, when the time of suffocation is past, bring together the two edges of the skin wound, and suture only the skin itself without the cartilage.
Then apply medicines that promote flesh growth until it is healed.
Says Albucasis. The summary of this discourse that we have mentioned is not applicable unless they see that one of these abscesses has swollen the patient's throat: and the patient is raised above death, and wants his breathing to be cut off: they go to cut the Epiglottis so that the patient may breathe over the wound site in some manner and be saved from death: and for this reason, they ordered to leave the wound open until the malice of the illness is consumed, and it lasts for three days or nearly so: then they order to suture the wound and treat it until it heals.
And what I have seen myself is that one servant took a knife and thrust it into her throat, cutting with it a part of the windpipe.
And I was called for her treatment, and I found her groaning, as it is the groan of a dead person.
I uncovered the wound, and I found that the blood that had come out of the wound was little. I was relieved that she had not cut the vein, nor the gut; and wind was coming out of the wound.
I hurried and treated the wound, and cared for it until it was healed: and nothing happened to the maid except a hoarseness in her voice: and she returned after days to a better state of health.
Therefore, I say that there is no fear in the incision of the epiglottis.
Concerning the incision of the throat hernia.
Chapter XLIV.
This swelling named throat hernia is a large swelling according to the color of the body: and it is very common in women.
And it occurs in two ways: either it is natural, or it is accidental.
In the natural case, there is certainly no danger.
The accidental case occurs in two ways: one of which is similar to fatty knots. And the other way is similar to the swelling that occurs from the结扎动脉。 And there is fear in it, and one should not presume to approach it with iron unless it is small: and you should examine it and investigate it with the probe. If you find it similar to a fatty knot, and it is not hanging with any veins: then cut it like knots are cut: and extract it with what it contains from the cyst, if it is in a cyst: and if not, then examine all of it. Then care for the area with what is necessary for the treatment, until it heals.
Chapter XLV.
Regarding the incision on types of knots.
There are many types of knots, and I have already mentioned all their types in the division: and it is necessary that I explain here the difference between a knot and an excrescence: as it may cause confusion.
I say, therefore, that with an excrescence there is heat, and fever, and severe pains, until the effervescence of superfluities is calmed, and putrefaction is complete: for then the fever and heat subside.
With a knot, there is no heat, nor fever, nor pain, and they are contained in cysts called sifachin, which are their own sacs, and they are according to the color of the body: and their beginning is like a chickpea, and they grow like a batecha, being larger or smaller.
And they are of two types: either fatty: or containing moisture. And the colors of the moisture are many, according to what I have said in the division.
Therefore, when you come to the treatment of a knot, you should examine it and inquire about it first with an instrument called Intromissum, according to how its form will be presented in the chapter that follows this.
And the method of investigation of abscesses and all nodes is to take this instrument and insert it into the moister place that you find in the abscess: and you rotate your fingers with it gradually until you know that the instrument has now penetrated the skin. Then move your hand according to the measurement of the size of the abscess.
Then withdraw what was inserted, and examine what comes out in its wake.
If then a flowing moisture comes out, whatever the color may be: then cut it with a superficial incision, as I have said in the case of other abscesses.
And if no moisture comes out in the wake of what was inserted, then you know that it is thick: therefore cut over it with a cross-shaped incision, according to this form, as I have taught you: and suspend it with hooks, and remove the skin from all sides easily: and keep the fistula, if you can, over it, so that you extract it along with the node.
If, however, the cyst bursts during the operation, and it is not possible to extract it whole, for this often happens, then remove it in pieces until nothing of it remains.
For if any part of it, small or large, remains, the node will return in full measure.
If it overpowers you and a small part remains: then fill the wound at the completion with certain sharp corrosive powders: bind the wound, and place over it something warm where the abscess sits, and care for it with the rest of the treatment until it heals.
If there is a large knot, then sew its two lips, and treat it with what causes flesh to grow.
If however there is a pulsating vein opposite you, or non-pulsating: then hurry, and fill the place with ground zegi, and leave it tight for two days, or three, until the wound putrefies, and the blood boiling ceases: then return to cut what remains of the Knot.
Chapter XLVI.
Regarding the outer instruments for cutting and piercing.
From these are the forms of introducers, and they are of three kinds.
From these, there is the large one, and from these is the medium one, and from these is the small one.
Let them be made from square-ended alfulud iron, appropriately, so that they may quickly enter into the abscess.
And these are the forms of the experiencers, and no, that is, the perforators: and one of them is named beris, that is, perforating: and they are of three kinds.
From these, there is the large one, the medium one, and the small one.
They are used to investigate abscesses, sinuses, fistulas, and buboes from what is between them of bones.
And others are made round, smooth, and blunt, like large needles with which chairs are sewn, from citrine, or from bronze, or iron, or silver.
And the better ones are those made from lemon.
And there is also an experience with black lead, which is used to test fistulas, whose concavities have reflections, so that they are reflected with their softness with those reflections.
And there are again three species. For from them there are long ones, from them medium ones, and from them short ones, according to the quantity of the amplitude of the fistula and its constriction.
The form of hooks, and they are of many species.
For there are simple ones among them, that is, those which have a single curvature: and they are of three species as you see, Large, Medium, and Small.
And there are blind hooks among them: and they are of three species.
And there are hooks having two curvatures among them, and they are of three species: and there are hooks having three curvatures among them, and they are of three species: and all these are necessary in their place.
And these are the forms of scalpels, with which knots and abscesses are cut and skinned: and they are of three species: for there is a large one, a medium one, and a small one.
The ends of them with which the cutting is done are sharp, the other ends are not sharp: and they are not used in this manner unless to provide assistance in skinning knots near the fear of cutting a vein or nerve: and that through them the patient may be healed and find temporary relief from burning which is found in skinning abscesses.
They are made of copper, and they resemble a still with which alcohol is made: and at the wide end there are hidden points of spatulas: and through it runs to the inside, and to the outside when you wish, as you see.
The form of the spatulas which are hidden between the fingers for puncturing abscesses: and the patient does not feel them: and they are of three varieties, large, medium, and small.
Forms of lancets with which the flow of blood is cut off: and they are of three varieties, large, medium, and small.
They shall be made of copper or brass, round, to a moderate length, as you see: and they should be slender.
And it is necessary that you have these varieties of lancets, large and small: to cut off the blood quickly in an emergency, and then when medicine is not present for you.
However, do not use them to cut off blood from every part of the body, and use them only in fleshy areas: such as the thighs, hips, arms, nipples, abdomen, groin, and similar fleshy, moist parts.
And sometimes small instruments similar to the blades of knives are made from them according to their shape: with which blood is cut off when it flows from the place of bloodletting or from a vein or artery incision: and sometimes they are made round according to this form.
Chapter Forty-Seven.
The treatment of men's nipples which are similar to women's nipples.
Sometimes the nipples of some men swell at the completion of sleep (that is, when they begin to be polluted in sleep) until they resemble women's nipples: and they remain foully abscessed.
Therefore, whoever wishes to avoid this, should cut above the nipples in a crescent shape, according to this form from line b to line g. Then remove all the fat. Then fill the wound with a flesh-forming medicine. Then sew together the two edges of the wound, and care for it until it heals.
If the nipple inclines downward and softens due to its size, as happens with women: then it must be cut on both of its upper sides with two similar crescent-shaped incisions, each of which is connected to the other at the ends of each, until there is a larger line containing a smaller one, according to this form from line b to line g. Then remove the skin that is between the two edges, and take away the fat, and administer what we have said about suturing and powders, which is necessary for the cure, until it heals.
If you cannot complete the incision that you need to make due to the restlessness of the patient or due to blood flow: then you must fill the wound with a sponge soaked in a corrosive ointment, and leave it until it corrodes what remains of the fat. Then care for it until it heals.
On the puncturing of an abscess, which occurs under the armpit.
Chapter XLVIII.
These abscesses which occur under the armpit are of the hard species of Strophularia, which contains cysts, and from them come those that contain moisture.
Those that contain moisture should be cut with a crescent-shaped incision, according to this form, from line b to line g. When all the pus in the abscess has been evacuated, then fill it with old lint and leave it until the next day.
Then remove the lint and treat it with a suitable ointment until it heals.
If the abscess is of the hard knot species of Strophularia, then incise it as we have said in the section on incising Strophularia equally.
If the wound extends to discharge pus, then apply a cautery to it as we have said in what has been previously stated.
Chapter XLIX.
On the incision of an abscess that occurs due to an Artery and Vein.
When an artery is ruptured and the skin above it becomes hardened, an abscess often results from this. Similarly, it happens with veins, resulting in an abscess and swelling.
And the signs by which it is known that the swelling and inflammation are due to the Artery and Vein are: for when the swelling is due to the artery, it is long, gathered in the depths of the body: and when you press the swelling with your fingers, you feel as if it were making a hissing sound.
And that which is due to the Vein, is round on the surface of the body.
And to cut on this swelling is an error, and especially so when it is under the armpits, and groins, and neck, and in many parts of the body: and it is very large. Therefore, the care of it should be avoided with iron, and what is also in the extremities or in the head should be avoided.
Therefore, for that which comes from the swelling of the arterial opening, find a cut in the skin in length. Then open the cut with hooks, then the artery; and free it from the tunics until it is uncovered.
Then insert a needle under it, and make it penetrate all the way to the other side, and tie the artery with a double thread in two places, according to which I taught you in the extraction of the two arteries which are in the temples.
Then pierce the area between the two ligatures with a scalpel until all the blood within it comes out and the swelling is resolved.
Then apply treatment that generates pus until the ligatures fall off: afterwards treat it with appropriate ointments until it heals.
If it is an abscess due to the cutting of a vein, then you must hold with your hand as much of the abscess with the skin as you can. Then insert the needle under the place you are holding with your hand, and make it penetrate: and let there be double thread in it until you draw it out from the other side. Then tie it with the abscess with a good binding: according to what I told you about binding a grape, from two sides with the two ends of the thread.
If you fear that the thread will be pulled out, then insert another needle with another thread under the entire abscess at the needle's incision: press and hold your threads in four places.
Then cut the abscess in its middle until what is inside comes out: then cut off the excess skin, and release what was tied from it.
Then place on it the poultice which you have submerged in wine and oil. Then administer the treatment which is done with plasters and ointments until it heals.
Chapter L.
Regarding the abscess that occurs from the twisting of nerves.
As an abscess occurs in arteries and veins, so does an abscess occur in nerves: which happens to them through percussion or excessive labor and similar causes: and it most often occurs in places like the helper joints or heels, and in any place where joints are moved: and it is a severe abscess.
Its color resembles the rest of the body, and it is in most conditions without pain: and when it is squeezed with vehemence, the patient feels a sensation similar to stupor.
And it is not a deep-seated abscess in the body, but rather it is under the skin, and it can be moved in all directions, nor does it move forward or backward to the rear.
Therefore, what is present at the joints should not be penetrated with iron. For perhaps a contraction may occur.
In those cases where it is on the head or on the forehead, incise the skin with a scalpel. If it is a small abscess, then hold it with forceps, and cut it off from the root.
And if it is large, then suspend it with a hook, and scrape it: then remove it, and close the wound with stitches: and care for it until it heals.
Chapter Fifty-One.
Concerning the incision of an abscess that occurs in the abdomen.
Sometimes, many people experience growths in their abdomens and other parts of their bodies, called Fungalia, named by similarity to fungi.
Their root is subtle, and their head is large, and their lips are turned outward. And some of them are small: and some of them become greatly enlarged.
And indeed I have seen a man, and in his abdomen were two tumors, which were more like mushrooms than other things: there was no difference between them, white, small roots, and their lips were inverted, and ended, and moisture always flowed from them.
So I cut them, and found one to weigh nearly ten and eight ounces and the other nearly six ounces. And the operation in cutting them is such that you should then consider if the patient is moist, and the color of the tumors is white, moist, with fine roots: then cut it with a broad spatula, and have cautery irons ready in the fire.
For often much blood is expelled at the cutting of it: therefore hurry if the blood overcomes you, then cauterize it.
If you see the patient fearful and timid about being cut with the iron, then take a properly made lead wire, and tie it around the tumor: its size is as we have said, and leave it for two days.
Then add to the lead binding. Therefore, do not stop binding with lead whenever it presses on the tumor, until it is severed and falls off by itself without effort.
If the tumor has a thick root, then there is something to fear and be anxious about in its cutting, especially if it is in the abdomen.
However, it is possible to cut through half of it. Then cauterize it so that it does not return.
Then care for it until the wound heals.
And beware lest you presume to incise the tumor which is of a dark color, has little sensation, and an ugly appearance: for it is indeed a cancerous abscess; and I will come with a reminder of Cancer after this.
Chapter LII.
On the treatment of the navel prominence.
The navel prominence occurs for many reasons. Or from fissures of the sifac, which is above the belly: and althub or intestine protrudes from it, according to what happens in other hernias. Or from the blood that flows from a vein or an artery, according to what has been mentioned. Or from wind confined in it.
If it is due to a fissure of the sifac and the protrusion of thirbi: then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the body: and it is soft, without pain: and its position varies. And if it is due to the protrusion of the intestine, then its position is much more diverse than what we have mentioned. When you press it with your fingers, it disappears: then it returns, and there may be a sound with it: and it swells greatly at the entrance of the bath, causing much labor.
If it is due to moisture, then it is soft and does not disappear when you press it with your hand, nor does it retract or increase.
And if it is due to blood, then with these signs the abscess appears black on the slope.
And if it is due to flesh generated: then the abscess is heavy, thick, hard, and fixed according to a single quantity.
And if it is due to flatulence, then its touch is gentle.
And the procedure is such that you should then consider if the prominence of the navel is due to blood of Arteries, or Veins, or flatulence: then you must refrain from its treatment. For there is fear and dread, as I have taught you in the chapter where I said about abscesses due to artery and vein.
And if the prominence of the navel is due to the intestine or the colon: then you must advise the patient to hold their breath and stand stretched out. Then mark with cautery around the entire navel. Then advise him to lie supine in your hands on his back. Then circle with a broad spatula around the navel over the place you marked with cautery. Then extend the center of the abscess upward with a large hook. Then bind him tightly around the circumference with thread or with silk cord firmly: and let the knot of the binding be strong.
Then open the center of the extended abscess above the binding. If you find it already caught by a ligament: then extract the hernia, and insert your index finger into it, and push the intestine towards the interior of the abdomen: and if you find a polyp, then take hold of it with a hook, and cut off its excess.
If however the artery or vein is opposite you: then tie it tightly around. Then return to your operation. And take two needles, and insert two strong threads into them: and insert the two needles around the area you made around the abscess in the form of a cross, which you make to penetrate.
Then bind the abscess at four points above the needles: and if you wish, remove the needles, and leave the area until the extended flesh putrefies: and falls off by itself: or cut it when it becomes thin and putrefied.
Then treat it with the appropriate ointment until it heals.
If the protrusion of the navel is due to hard flesh in it or moisture: then it is necessary to hollow out the abscess as we have said. And extract the blood or moisture that you find in it.
Then treat it with what consolidates the area.
Chapter LIII.
Regarding the treatment of CANCER.
We have already spoken about the classification of types of cancer and how to approach its treatment with medicines: and we must be cautious when treating it with surgery so that it does not become ulcerated: and we have discussed cancer generated in the uterus and precautions for its treatment.
And the ancients said that sometimes the Cancer is in a place where its removal is possible: such as Cancer which is in the breasts, or in the thigh, and those similar, from parts located for extracting all of it: especially when it is beginning small.
When however it becomes old, and is large, you should not approach it.
For I could not heal anyone from it: nor have I seen anyone before me who has reached that.
And the operation on it, when it is located as we have said, is to proceed and release the patient from black bile several times. Then bleed it if you find it with obvious fullness.
Then prepare the patient for the preparation in which he is placed for the operation.
Then throw into the Cancer hooks that are suitable for it. Then scoop it from all sides with the skin, according to the exploration, until nothing remains of its roots: and let the blood flow, and do not cut it quickly, but press the areas, and wipe all the thick blood with your hand, or with whatever is possible there from the instruments.
If, however, the thick blood flow from the incision of an artery or vein opposes you, then cauterize the vein until the blood is stopped. Then care for it with the rest of the treatment until it is healed.
Regarding the treatment of dropsy.
Chapter LIIII. We have already narrated in the division of the types of Hydropisis, and how the aggregation of water occurs: and the signs of every type, and its cure with medicines.
And that which is treated with iron is only the asclitis type alone: and it is not approached with iron in the timpanitis type: nor thoroughly in the hyposarcae type: for that is mortal.
When you have already treated this type of Hydropisis timpanitis with medicines, and your treatment has not helped: then consider. For if the patient has already acquired weakness, or there is another illness with him besides Hydropisis: such as if he has cough, or diarrhea, and similar to these: then beware of treating him with iron: for there is fear in that.
But if you see a patient of abundant strength, and there is no illness with him besides Hydropisis alone: and he is neither a child nor an old person: then the method of operation is as follows, that you lift the patient standing between your hands, and a helper behind him should press his belly with his hand to drive the water to the lower part of the chest.
Then take a spine-like spatula according to this shape. Let it have two sharp ends, long, with an acute tip like a spatula. However, let there be some gradual shortening in it, so that you do not penetrate with it during the operation all the way to the intestine and damage it.
Then consider. For if the generation of dropsy is from the intestines, then it is necessary to extend with a cut from the navel by the length of three fingers, towards the lower area directly above the pubic bone.
If however the generation of dropsy is due to illness of the liver: then let your cut be to the left from the navel by three fingers.
And if its generation is due to the spleen, then the cut should be on the right side: and it is also not appropriate for there to be a cut on the side on which the patient wishes to lie, so that the excess fluids do not flow to that weak spot.
Then pierce the entire skin with the instrument. Then insert into that incision, and lift your hand with the spatula between the skin and the sifac, as if you are flaying it: and let the amount that is flayed be the size of a nail, or about that.
Then pierce the sifac until the spatula reaches the empty space: and that is the location of the water. Then extract it, and insert into the opening an instrument, which has this form. And it is similar to a cannula: made of silver, or brass, or bronze, smooth, polished: which has at its lower part a small opening, and on its sides are three openings, two from one side, and one from the other side: and the face is its cut end, according to the manner of cutting a reed, as you see: at its upper end is a ring.
For when the instrument reaches the water, then it descends immediately upon the instrument, therefore evacuate from water in an hour a medium quantity.
For if you evacuate more than is proper from it, perhaps the patient may die in an hour by the dissolution of his animal spirit; or he may suffer a syncope that approaches death.
But evacuate from it according to the quantity of its strength, and according to what the dispositions of the patient signify to you from the strength of his pulse, and from its goodness.
Then remove the instrument, and retain the water.
Which is because it is retained immediately due to the skin which holds the hole that is on the syringe; of which I have spoken, so as to pierce it according to that method.
Then repeat the procedure the next day, if you see the patient tolerate it: and also evacuate a small quantity from the water.
Do this for several days without fear, and guard against error: until there is only a little of the water left.
But if you fear for the patient and leave much of the water: then care for him with burial in warm sand, and much sweating in a bath and sun, and let him thirst: and treat him with drying medicines until he is healed: and cauterize over the stomach, the liver, and the spleen, after the extraction of water: as I have spoken in what precedes.
Regarding the care of infants who are born with their urinary passages not perforated.
Chapter LV.
When one of the infants exits the womb of his mother, and his meatus urinis is not perforated, or there is a narrow opening, or it is not in its proper place.
Therefore, it is necessary to intervene with the piercing of it immediately upon birth with a very fine spatula, according to this form.
Then place a thin pin made of lead in the opening and tie it: and keep it there for three days, or four.
When he wants to urinate, it should be removed, and he will urinate. Then replace it.
And if you do not place the lead, it is possible that the urine which flows over the area may prevent it from closing.
He whose opening is narrow is treated with lead, as we have said, for many days, until it is enlarged.
Those in whom the opening is not in its proper place are injured. This is because, in those who are born with it, the opening is at the end of the head of the penis: therefore, he cannot urinate forward until he lifts the penis upward with his hand. He cannot procreate because the sperm cannot reach the matrix properly: and it is a very foul disease.
And the method of the operation is to have the patient lie on his back. Then extend the head of the rod with your left hand strongly, and cut the head of the rod from the priapi place, with a sharp point or an acute scalpel: like the cutting of a reed, or as you root something, so that its middle comes similar to the head of the rod: and so that a hole falls in the middle according to what is necessary.
And be careful during your operation from blood flow. For it often happens that. Therefore, apply to it what stops the blood, and treat the wound until it heals.
Regarding Albather, which occurs in the foreskin and head of the penis, and corruption, blackening, and adhering.
Chapter LVI.
These Albathers often occur on the penis, and they are protrusions of ugly flesh.
And from them, some are malignant, and some are not malignant.
Therefore, if it is not malignant, you should suspend it with a fine hook and cut it off until you cleanse it entirely. Then place upon it a poultice soaked in Egyptian ointment. Then treat it after that with diaphrynion ointment until it heals.
If the Albather is malignant and of ugly color, then you should apply a cautery to it after its incision and treatment.
If however Albather is on the foreskin of a captive, not circumcised, and there is part of Albather within the foreskin, and part of it outside: then you must remove the Albather which is inside first, until when it consolidates, then care for the outer part: because when you care for both at once, the foreskin does not heal without being pushed forward.
And it also happens that in the testicles and foreskin there is blackening and corruption. Therefore, you must scoop out all that is already blackened, and what is about to be corrupted, or is already corrupted.
Then apply on it after that honey which has been mixed with the flour of pomegranate rind and crushed sieve herbs.
Then care for it with the rest of the treatment until it is healed.
If however a blood flow occurs, then apply the cautery with a crescent-shaped cautery, according to this form.
For cautery is beneficial for two conditions simultaneously, namely for blood flow and a wound when it becomes corrupted.
If the head of the penis is corroded and destroyed entirely in an hour: then you must insert a lead tube into the urethra so that the patient may urinate over it.
In cases where the foreskin adheres to the head of the penis, and this adherence does not occur unless in one whose foreskin is healthy and does not require circumcision: and sometimes it happens due to a wound or an abscess: therefore you must scrape it with a blunt spatula until the bond is loosened and the head of the penis is freed on all sides.
And if it is difficult to distinguish them precisely, then it is necessary to remove something from the head of the rod, and from the foreskin. Which is because the foreskin when it is thin, perhaps is pierced quickly because of its thinness.
Then separate the foreskin from the head of the rod with a fine linen cloth that has already been moistened in cold water, so that they do not stick together again.
Then it should be treated with astringent wine until it is healed.
Chapter LVII.
Regarding the cleansing of infants and the treatment of errors that befall them.
Circumcision is not a solution of continuity like other wounds; however, since it is by our operation, by our will, and its use is properly for children, it is necessary that we mark in it a better operation and a lighter way leading to healing.
I say, therefore, that the ancients did not mention circumcision in any of their books because they do not use it in their laws, and it is only what we have acquired through experience.
Which is because I have found the majority of surgeons and phlebotomists to use cleansing by circumcision with a lancet and scissors: and they use cauterization, binding with thread, and incision with a scalpel.
And indeed, I have already tested all these methods and have not found a better one than cleansing with scissors and binding with thread.
For in the cleansing with the knife, the skin often escapes. For the skin of the foreskin has two layers: therefore perhaps the upper skin is cut, and the lower layer remains: thus it is necessary to make another incision to cut the other, causing future pain. And with the cleansing which is done by alfecti, that is, awls, which tailors use, the end of the male member is not cut: because it might enter its opening.
In cleansing with the hoof, perhaps the iron slips and ruins your operation: and the skin of a boy is short by nature, and often they are born in such a way that they do not require cleansing: and I have already seen this.
However, the cleansing with scissors and tying with thread has proven to be a good experiment for me: because the scissors are proportionate to the incision: therefore, the sharpness which is above is like the sharpness which is below. When you press your hand, the two sharp edges are aligned, and they cut according to a single operation at one time: and a compression of similar shape is made, holding the skin of the rod from all sides, with which there is no error at all.
And the method of the operation is to make the boy understand, especially if he is one of those who comprehend quickly, that you do nothing but tie a thread on his rod: and leave him until the next day.
Then make him rejoice and be glad in every way possible for you, according to what his understanding receives. Then make him stand between your prepared hands, and let him not be seated: and conceal the scissors in your sleeve, or under your foot, so that the boy does not see them at all, nor any of the instruments.
Then insert your hand to his rod, and blow on the skin, and pull it up until the head of the rod comes out. Then clean it from the filth that collects on it.
Then bind the marked area with double thread. Then tie below it temporarily with a second bandage. Then hold with your index finger and thumb the place of the lower bandage firmly, and cut between the two bandages. Then lift the skin up quickly, and extract the head of the rod. Then let the blood flow gradually (for it is better) and put powder on top: and above the powder a cloth in which is spread the yolk of an egg boiled in rose water, mixed with good fresh rose oil: and leave it on until the next day: and care for it with the rest of the treatment until it heals.
The form of the scissors for cleaning is this.
Let the two ends be blunt and inclined: so that the branch of the nail does not protrude: and let the length of the two sharp edges be equal to the length of the two handles.
The error occurring in cleaning is: because the inner skin may entirely or partially escape at the incision.
Therefore you must extend it with your fingernail from the area before the formation of an abscess: and cut it according to equality.
If you cannot hold it with your fingernail, then extract it with a hook, and cut it.
If three days have passed and what is under the nail remains swollen, having formed an abscess: then leave it until the hot abscess settles, and remove the scab with ease, and cut it according to how it is prepared for you: and beware of the tip of the nail. For it will not harm it.
Treat it with what consolidates the wound from the powders, which we have discussed in the chapter on powders: and if it is cut beyond measure through the skin and extends to deeper areas, it will not harm it either.
Treat it with what we have said until it heals.
Chapter LVIII.
Regarding the extraction of retained urethral fluid in the bladder.
Retention of urine in the bladder occurs due to obstruction caused by a stone, or coagulated blood, or pus, or generated flesh, and similar things from those methods of treatment we mentioned in the division.
And if the urine does not resolve and you see that its retention is due to a stone already present in the neck of the bladder: then it is necessary for the patient to be bent over on his knees. Then let his feet be placed upon his back, and let him stretch out his belly from the upper part of his back, and let the sick person hold his breath as much as possible for him. Therefore, it is drawn with the neck of the bladder for the expulsion of the stone to the rear: hence the urine is discharged.
If it is not resolved by what we have said and the condition is severely affecting the sick person: then you must administer its extraction with an instrument called a syringe, which has this form: It should be made of silver, and be fine, smooth, hollow like the tube of a bird's feather in fineness comparable to a ray, long to the length of one and a half palms: it should have a fine tube at its head.
And the method of urine exiting through it is to take a doubled thread, and tie wool or cotton at its end with a good knot: and insert the end of the thread into the lower part of the syringe: and cut with scissors if there is any excess wool, but insert it into the tube forcibly, like an alzer.
Then anoint the syringe with oil or butter, and egg white: and have the sick person sit on a seat, and inject the bladder, and its rod with moist oils, and olive oil, and warm water.
Then insert the syringe into the rod easily until it reaches the root of the rod.
Then double it above the part of the navel.
Then push the syringe inside until it reaches the bladder, and let the sick person feel that it has already reached the empty space: and this is not done according to this order unless because the passage through which it goes is twisted.
Then extend the thread with wool gradually. For Vrina will follow the wool.
Then withdraw it, and make Vrina run through the urine passage: and repeat the syringe, and do not cease to do this until the bladder is evacuated, and the patient finds relief.
Regarding the quality of bladder irrigation with a clepsydra.
Chapter LIX.
When an ulcer occurs in the bladder, or blood congeals in it, or pus is compressed within it, and you wish to distill water and medicines into it: then it should be done with an instrument called a clepsydra, and this is its form.
For it is closed, that is, sealed. And in it there are three holes, two on one side, and one on the other side, as you see.
And the concave area, in which is placed that which pushes, should be according to the size that fits it without addition, until when something is drawn with it, moisture is attracted: and when it is pushed, it is expelled far away: as a clepsydra does, from which naphta, that is, Greek fire, is projected in battles.
When you wish to project moisture into the bladder, insert the end of the clepsydra into the moisture, and draw with it that which pushes upward, for the moisture is drawn into the concavity of the clepsydra.
Then insert its extremity into a rod, according to what we have narrated in the syringe. Then push the moisture with that which pushes it, for that moisture reaches the bladder immediately, so that the patient feels it.
The form of a subtle clyster with which the bladder is cleansed.
Let it be made of silver or brass, whose head should be higher and similar to a small alcamah, and below it there should be a groove in which the ligament falls.
Then take the bladder of a ram and put the moisture in it with which you want to cleanse the bladder. Then tie it between two grooves with a strong ligature and double thread: and warm that moisture slightly over the fire.
Then insert the extremity of the clyster into a tube, then press your hand over the bladder with a proper tightness along with the moisture until the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder.
If you do not have a bladder available, then take a piece of parchment, and make a circle out of it, and pierce it all around its circumference. Then insert a strong thread into those holes as they turn. Then assemble the circle as you would assemble a sibling: after you place in it what you wish from moistures, oils, and waters.
Then tie it to the instrument: and do with it as you did with the bladder by pressing with your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
Chapter LX.
On the extraction of Stone.
We have already discussed the classification of stone types and its treatment with medicines: and I have mentioned the difference between a stone generated in the kidneys and the bladder, and the signs of it all: and I have spoken of the stone on which manual operation and incision is performed: and this is the stone properly generated in the bladder: and that which is embedded in the penis: and I am narrating this with clear exposition and abbreviation.
I say therefore, that the stone generated in the bladder most often affects children.
And from its signs is that urine exits the bladder similar to water in its fineness: and white sand appears in it, and the patient rubs his penis, and labors with it, and hangs down frequently. Then it rises, and the anus protrudes with it in many of them.
And the healing is easy for children up until they reach fourteen years. And it is difficult in the elderly. In young adults it is moderate, being between the two extremes: and the larger the stone, the easier the treatment: and if small, the treatment is conversely more difficult.
Therefore, when we arrive at the treatment, it is necessary first to cleanse the patient with aclyster that will expel all the feces in their intestines: for it sometimes prevents the discovery of the stone during the examination.
Then the patient should be taken with his feet and shaken, and moved downward: so that the Stone may descend to the bottom of the bladder, or jump from a height several times.
Then make him sit between your prepared hands, and his hands should be under his hips, so that the bladder may be entirely inclined downward.
Then examine him, and touch him externally.
If therefore you feel the Stone in the space, then immediately proceed with the incision over it.
If it does not fall under your touch at all, then you must clean the index finger with the oil of your left hand if the patient is a boy: or the middle finger if he is a full adult: and insert it into his anus, and search for the Stone until it stands under your finger: and gradually turn it toward the neck of the bladder.
Then press on it with your finger, and push it outward toward the location where you wish to make the incision: and command one attendant to press the bladder with his hand, and command another attendant to lift the testicles upward with his right hand: and with the other hand, to move away the skin that is under the testicles from the site of the incision.
Then insert the sharp spatula, whose shape is as follows. And find the area between the anus and the testicles, not in the middle, but to the left side of the buttocks: and make the incision over the stone, with your finger in the anus: and let the incision be transverse, so that the outer part of the incision is wider and the inner part narrower, according to the amount that the exit of the Stone from it should not be larger.
For perhaps the finger compresses the stone at the site of the cut, and it exits without difficulty.
And know that from the stone which has angles and edges, its exit is made difficult because of that.
And from it is smooth, similar to a gland, and round: and its exit is made easy.
Therefore, for the one that has angles and edges, add to the fissure.
If it does not exit thus, then you must be ingenious with it: either grasp it with forceps properly, the end of which is like a crescent, which grasps over the stone and does not slip away from it; or insert under it a delicate instrument with a curved end.
If, however, you cannot grasp it thus, then enlarge the opening slightly. If anything from the blood overpowers you, cut it with a scalpel.
If however there is more than one stone, then first push the larger one towards the bladder opening. Then incise over it. Then push the smaller one after that; and similarly do if there are more than two.
If it is very large, then it is unskilled to cut it with a large incision. For it happens to the patient one of two things, either that he dies, or there is a continuous dripping of urine; because the place does not heal entirely.
But administer the expulsion of it until it comes out: or extract pieces of it from the fracture with scissors until you have removed it bit by bit.
When therefore you have completed your operation, then fill the wound with frankincense, and aloe, and dragon's blood: and bind it, and place upon it cloth soaked in oil and wine, or rose oil, and cold water: so that the hot pus may be set.
Then lay the patient on their back, and do not loosen the bandage until the third day. When therefore you loosen it, moisten the area with water and much oil.
Then treat it with dyafinicon ointment and basilicon ointment until it heals.
If however a hot pus and corroded substances and things like them happen in the wound: such as if blood congeals in the bladder and urine is prohibited by it: and it is known from the discharge of blood with urine. Insert therefore your finger into the wound and draw out that blood. For if it remains, it causes the corruption of the bladder and its putrefaction.
Then wash the wound with vinegar, water, and salt: and treat it with whatever is suitable for its healing until it is healed.
And it is necessary during the entire course of treatment to bind the two thighs together for the purpose of the medicines that are placed on the area.
If the stone is small and is in the channel of the penis, and it is fixed there, and the passage of urine is prevented: then treat it as I describe before you reach the stage of cutting. For often you will be spared from cutting through this treatment, for I have already proven it.
And it is that you take the perforator from alum iron, whose form is this, with a triangular end, sharp, fixed in wood.
Then take a string and tie it to the penis below the stone so that it does not return to the bladder.
Then insert the perforating iron into the penis with ease until the perforator reaches the stone itself: and rotate the perforator with your hand on the stone gradually: and try to penetrate it until you make it go through the other side.
For the urine is discharged immediately.
Then press your hand on what remains of the stone from the outer part of the penis. For it breaks apart and exits with the urine, and the patient is healed.
If this treatment is not prepared for you, due to something that prevents it: then tie a string below the stone and another string above the stone. Then cut above the stone on the penis between the two strings. Then extract it. Then untie the ligature and clean the clotted blood that forms in the wound.
And it is not necessary to tie the thread under the stone, unless so that it does not return to the bladder: and another binding above, unless when the thread is loosened after the exit of the stone, the skin returns to its place, and covers the wound: and for this reason you must do this when you tie the upper thread, so that you raise the skin upwards, so that it returns at the completion of your work, and covers the wound, as we said.
Chapter LXI.
On the extraction of stones in women.
A stone is rarely generated in women.
If however a stone should occur in any of them, then the treatment is difficult, and it is prohibited due to many methods.
One of them is: that the woman may be a virgin.
And the second is, that you do not find a woman who will expose herself to a physician, when she is chaste, or among those who have husbands.
The third is that you do not find a woman well skilled in this art, especially the manual procedure.
And the fourth is the distance from the location of the stone: therefore it requires deep incision, and there is fear in that.
If necessity provokes to do that, then it is necessary to take a woman physician, well skilled: and she is rarely found.
If you are deprived of that, then seek a chaste and subtle physician, and present a well-educated midwife in women's matters, or a woman who understands part of this art: therefore make her present, and especially entrust to her to do everything you instruct regarding the examination for the stone.
First of all, he should see if the woman is a virgin: then he must insert his finger into her anus and seek the stone.
If he finds it, he should press it with his finger, and then instruct the midwife to insert her finger into the patient's vagina and search for the stone, after placing her left hand on the bladder and compressing it firmly.
If he finds the stone, then he must gradually move it from the opening of the bladder downward with all his strength until he reaches the root of the hip with it.
Then he should incise above it at the midpoint of the vagina near the root of the hip, on whichever side the stone is felt: and his finger should not be removed from the stone, pressing under it; and let the incision be small at first. Then he should insert a probe above that incision.
Then he should insert a probe above that incision. If he feels the stone, then he should increase the incision according to the amount proportional to how the stone exits from it.
And you should know that there are many types of stones. Among these, there is a small one and a large one, a smooth one and a rough one, a long one, and a round one with branches.
Know therefore its types, so that it may be indicated to you by this regarding what you desire.
If the blood overcomes you, then apply ground zegi to the area and keep it for one hour until the bleeding stops.
Then return to your operation until the stone comes out: and do so that you prepare with you of the instruments which I said in the extraction of the stone in men, to help you through them in your operation.
If the flow of blood overcomes you, and you know that the expulsion of blood is from an artery which has been cut: then place powder on the place, and bind it with linen in a suitable binding: and do not change it: and leave the stone, and do not extract it. For perhaps the weak woman will die. Then care for the wound.
Therefore, when the sharpness of the blood is calmed after days, and the place becomes putrid, then return to your operation until the stone comes out.
Chapter LXII.
Regarding the incision of a watery hernia.
Watery ramex is not present unless there is an aggregation of moisture in the sifac album, which is under the skin of the testicle containing the egg: and it is named sifac.
And sometimes it is in its own little pouch, which nature has prepared for it in the part of the egg until it is rotten: which is another egg, and it is the skin of the testicle between the sifac album, which we mentioned: and that does not occur except rarely.
And the generation of this ramix is from the weakness that befalls the testicles: therefore this material is poured out to them. And sometimes it happens from a blow on the testicles.
And this moisture has many colors. For its color either tends towards yellow, or it is blood red, or foul black, or it is water white, and that which is more.
And the signs by which it is known where the collection of water is, are these. For if there is in the white scrotum that we mentioned, then the abscess is round in length somewhat like the figure of an egg: and the testicle does not appear, because the moisture contains it on all sides.
And if the moisture is in its own small pouch, then the abscess is round like a part of an egg, and because of this, a person thinks that it is another egg.
And if the moisture is between the skin of the testicles and the white scrotum, then it becomes noticeable.
When therefore you wish to know the color of the moisture, then test the color of the moisture in the abscess with a square probe, whose form has been mentioned previously. According to what appears after the insertion of the probe, judge about what is inside it.
When therefore we come to the treatment with iron, then it is necessary to advise the patient to be bled if it is possible for him, and you see his body full.
Then he should lie on his back on something slightly elevated, and place many cloths under him.
Then sit you on his left, and command the servant to sit at his right, who extends the rod to one of the two sides of the scrotal skin, and to the mirach part of the belly.
Then take the broad lancet and cut the scrotal skin lengthwise through the middle, nearly to the pecten: and let the incision be made according to a straight equidistant line which divides the scrotal skin until it reaches the white sifac covering: and peel it away, and beware from this so that you do not cut it: and let your peeling be on the part which hangs more with the egg: and carefully examine with the peeling as much as is possible for you.
Then pierce the water-filled sifac with a wide puncture, and draw out all the water.
Then separate the two lips of the incision with hooks, and extend the sifac upwards, and do not touch the scrotal skin that encloses: and cut the sifac however it is possible for you to cut it, either in its entirety or piece by piece, especially the thin side of it. For if you do not examine it carefully, safety is not achieved in its incision, lest the water returns.
If the egg protrudes outside its skin during your operation: then when you have completed the incision of the sifac, reduce it. Then bring together the two lips of the scrotal skin with suture.
Then care for it like other wounds until it heals.
If you find an egg corrupted by other blackness, then it is necessary to tie the vessels which are the suspenders, fearing the flow of blood.
Then cut off the testicle with the suspender, and extract the egg: then care for it as we have said.
If water has gathered in two parts, then know that there are two branches: cut the other part accordingly as you did in the other equally.
And if it appears to you that the operation is one, then do as follows: afterwards clean the blood. And introduce into the incisions wool soaked in oil, or in rose oil: and place outside another wool which you have soaked in wine and oil, and spread it over both testicles, and the abdomen: and put on top doubled cloths, and they are poultices: and bind them with a bandage that has six according to this form.
Then let two cloths be taken, and sweated, and filled with crushed la na according to this likeness: and the ends by which it is pressed should be made of chamois or wet wool: and they should be gathered together with a binder at the waistband of the breeches: and one end should cover from the anus up to the back, and the second end should cover towards the hip area: and the two ends above on both thighs below, and the other two ends over the two groins, and the whole binder should be gathered together at the waistband of the breeches.
And sometimes this ramex is treated artificially with a cautery instead of incision with an iron: and it is as follows, take a delicate knife-like cautery, and cut the skin of the testicles with it: and it is ignited, as we have described: until when the white membrane containing water is revealed: then take the cautery according to this form.
It is assimilated to the Greek letter.
Then pierce it with that knife, and ignite it until all the moisture escapes.
Then extend the knife with hooks, and scar it with a fine ignited cautery, and cut it as much as you can until you root out all of it.
And be careful with the egg, lest the fire touch it.
And you should know that this operation is safer, farther from blood flow, and better than the operation with incision.
If however something opposes you at the time of incision, or at the time of cauterization, such as a warm aposteme, or blood flow, or something else: then you must treat what opposes you from that with a cure suitable to it, according to what has been stated.
If however the patient is timid and does not endure this operation due to its horror: then administer the piercing as I describe it, and proceed.
When it is confirmed to you by what we have said about the significations that the flux is watery: then it is necessary to make the patient sit on an elevated seat.
Then pierce the aposteme on its lower part with a broad spatula: and make the piercing according to the length of the body, and let the opening be wide until all the water flows out.
Then place a poultice on the area, and bind it, and leave it so that the remaining water may flow out: then treat it until the wound heals.
If however the obstruction is to the flow of water at the time when you pierce it: and this is not due to anything other than that the white membrane causes an obstruction at the opening of the wound, and prevents the exit of the water: then it is necessary to insert a quill into the wound, or an instrument with which the water of dropsy patients is extracted, whose form has been mentioned previously: or add in the operation of the wound temporarily.
And you should know that the water returns and accumulates after six months, or around that time. When it therefore accumulates, then it should be pierced in the same manner, and the patient will spend his days.
Chapter LXIII.
On the treatment of fleshy ramus.
Know that in the cutting of this ramus, there is great fear leading to peril in many conditions. Therefore, it seems to me that its dismissal is salvaging from it.
And I remember the procedure on it and the appearance of the abscess.
I say therefore that many abscesses occur in the body parts from which the testicles are composed: and this happens for many reasons, namely.
Or from acute or sharp excess that is discharged toward the testicles. Or from percussion.
And the color of the abscess is according to the color of the body, and no pain is found in it: and it is a heavy abscess.
And perhaps it is a stony abscess, whose color is dark, and it has no feeling.
And sometimes it occurs from the knotting of the arteries and their swelling: as has already been mentioned: or from the swelling of the veins.
That which is among them from the swelling of the arteries is recognized by the condition of the abscess when you press it with your fingers. And you should not touch it at all.
That which occurs from the swelling of the veins does not disperse anything when compressed with fingers.
And now it is possible that a section may be made on this type and on the other flesh: and it is as if you were to cut the skin of the testicles. Then extend the egg upward, and extract it with a white suture: and free the suspensory ligament from the vessels, and tie the vessels: and cut the suspensory ligament after you free it from all parts of the egg.
If the egg is consolidated with those flesh parts that have grown, then you must pull the egg and cut it.
And if there is adhesion between something of the suture, or in what is between the vessels: then you must free that entire adhesion and cut it with a circular incision.
If there is flesh growth in the area of adhesion which is behind: then you must cut all of it and extract the egg, as we have said.
When therefore your operation is complete, then fill the wound with wool soaked in rose oil and wine: then care for it with the rest of the treatment until it heals.
Chapter LXIIII.
On the care of shoots, which is done with vines.
Witis is a hidden swelling wrapped in a certain folding, similar to a botr, with a softening of the testicles: and it makes movement and exercise difficult for the patient, as well as walking.
And in the treatment of this illness, there is fear, because of that which preceded and was remembered.
However, we must say the treatment for it according to what the first practitioners did.
I say, therefore, that you should have the patient sit on an elevated seat. Then push the suspensory of the testicles downward. Then hold the skin of the testicles with your fingers, near the vessels that are close to the stem: and another assistant should hold them and stretch them forcefully.
Then make a transverse cut with a broad and sharp spatula directly across the vessels until the vessels are exposed.
Then remove the outer layer from all sides, as we have told you in the extraction of arteries that are in the temples.
Then insert a needle with double thread into them, and tie it at the first location where Witis occurs: and tie it again at the last location. Then cut it in a straight middle section according to the length of the body, and extract what gathers from corrupted feculent humidities.
Then treat the wound with the treatment of other wounds, in which pus is generated, so that the vessels nourishing one of the testicles fall. For it is not evil through that.
If the Vine affects all the vessels, then it is necessary to remove the testicles with the vessels: so that the egg is not deprived of nourishment due to the incision, and does not waste away or dry out, and is not rendered useless by them.
Chapter LXV.
Regarding the treatment of intestinal branches.
The outcome of this branching is from the incision that occurs in the extended sifach over the belly in the groin area from the mirach of the belly.
Therefore, the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the testicles. And this rupture is either from the sifach or its extension.
And these two types occur from many causes: either from a blow, or jumping, or shouting, or lifting a heavy object, and similar actions.
And the sign is when it is from the extension of the sifach. It occurs gradually over a long period of time and does not happen suddenly: and it is an equal swelling towards the depths: therefore, because the sifach compresses the intestine.
And the sign of it when it is from the cutting of the intestine, because it causes a sudden and intense pain at the beginning: and it is a different swelling appearing near under the skin: and that is due to the protrusion of the intestine, and its course to the exterior intestine.
And sometimes it comes out with the intestine twisted: and this is called Intestinal Ramex, and twisting: and sometimes it happens with flatulence.
And sometimes the feces enter the intestine and are retained there: and it is harmful to the patient: because it causes severe pain, especially when it is pressed.
And in the treatment of this kind of illness with iron there is fear: therefore one must be careful of accidents in it.
And the method of the procedure is to instruct the patient to return the intestine with his hand to the inner cavity, if it obeys the return. Then lie him down on his back between your hands: and raise his legs.
Then extend the skin that follows the skin upwards, and cut the entire skin of the testicles along its length. Then insert hooks into the two lips of the incision according to what is needed to open the incision with them: and the incision should be of such quantity that it is possible for the egg to come out of it.
Then remove the outer layer of the sifak and what is under the skin of the testicles until the white, hard sifak is revealed on all sides: then insert your index finger into what follows the testicle, between the white sifak that is under the egg's skin, and between the second sifak, and loosen with it the adhesion that is at the back part of the egg.
Then move with the right hand the skin of the testicles towards the inside: and with this extend the white saph with the left hand upwards: and raise the egg with the saph to the part of the incision: and command the assistant to extend the egg upwards: and you release the adhesion, which is at the back after complete separation.
And seek with your fingers that there is nothing there of the intestine wrapped in the hard white saph. If however you find anything of it: then push it downwards towards the abdomen.
Then take a needle with thick thread, made linen from ten threads: and insert it at the last saph, that is, of the tunic, which is under the skin of the testicles following the incision: then cut the ends which protrude from the thread until there are four threads. Then arrange some of them over some in the shape of a cross: and tie with them the white saph, of which we spoke, because it is under the skin of the testicles tied very strongly, until none of the vessels that nourish them can send anything to them: so that a hot aposteme does not result from it.
