And place another ligature outside the first ligature, less than two fingers away from it. And after these two ligatures, release from the saph that is under the skin of the testicles a quantity equal to the size of a finger: and cut the rest entirely according to its roundness, and remove the egg from it.
Then cut in the lower part of the skin of the testicles where blood and pus flow: as we have described in what has been mentioned before.
Then apply wool soaked in oil, and place on the wound: and apply the bandage which we mentioned. And sometimes the white swelling which we mentioned is cauterized after its incision, fearing the flow of blood. For it often happens. And remove the bandage, until it falls off by itself.
If however its falling off is delayed, then bathe it with warm water: and apply to it what we mentioned, until it falls off.
Then treat the wound with the rest of the treatment for wounds, until it is healed.
Chapter LXVI.
Regarding the windy ramus.
In this windy ramus, I have not seen anyone who has dared to attempt its treatment with iron.
And at first, they said that it happens as we have mentioned in the ramus that is with the vine. Which is to bind the vessels after cutting and easily apply something over them: then cut in the middle, and finally treat it with what opens it, until the vessels fall off: and treat the wound as we have said, until it heals.
Chapter LXVII.
Regarding the rupture that occurs in the groin.
When rupture occurs in the groin, as we have said, and the area protrudes, and nothing of the intestines descends to the testicles: and if it does descend, it is only a little, and it returns at all times: but if time is prolonged with it, a fissure is added to the swelling, until the intestines descend into the swelling.
And it happens from the stretching of the sifach, which is in the groin, as we said. Which is because the sifach is stretched: then it is softened, and the area becomes apstedematous and prominent.
And its treatment is with a cautery, as was previously narrated.
And sometimes it is treated with an iron, according to this method: and it is that the patient lies on their back under your hands. Then cut the swollen and prominent area of the rupture with a horizontal incision, according to the length of three fingers.
Then grasp the alsifak and what is under the skin until the white sifach is revealed, which is under the skin that follows it.
Then take the probe and place it on the prominent area of the sifach, and press it deeply into the abdomen.
Then sew the two prominent areas above the end of the probe from the sifach together with a suture; then remove the end of the probe.
And do not cut the alsifach at all, nor stretch the egg, nor anything else, as I made you know in the treatment of intestinal rami.
Then treat it with the treatment for wounds. When you cut the stitches, clean it, and dress the wound until it is healed.
For the sifach contracts, and does not add to the prominence of the rupture.
And the cautery is better in this place: because it is closer to healing.
Chapter LXVIII.
On the softening of the skin of the testicles.
The skin of the testicles is often softened in some men, because of which the flesh between them is also softened, and its appearance is marred.
Therefore, it is necessary for the one who is asked to treat it to make the patient lie on his back and cut away all the softened skin down to the natural skin.
Then bring together the two lips with a suture: and if you wish, first remove the excess of the softened skin with three or four sutures, and secure the suture firmly.
Then cut between the sutures.
Then treat it as you would other wounds until it heals, and the threads fall out.
Chapter LXIX.
On castration.
Know that castration is excommunicated in our law: and because of this, it would be permissible for me not to mention it in my book: and there is no need to mention it, except for two methods.
One of which is that it should be known by the doctor when asked about it: and so that he may know its treatment if it happens to someone.
The other reason is that we often need the castration of certain animals for our benefit through them, such as rams, goats, and cats, and similar animals.
I say therefore, that castration is performed in two ways. Or by rubbing. Or by making an incision and cutting.
In that which is done by rubbing, the way of the operation is: that we make the animal sit in warm water until its testicles soften and relax and hang down; then rub them with your hand until they dissolve and do not appear under touch.
In castration by incision and cutting, it is necessary to hold the animal and press the skin of its testicles with your left hand.
Then ligate the suspensorium, and cut above all the egg with one cut, until when two eggs come out: then incise them after you have skinned each one, and do not leave anything on them except a fine suture over the vessels.
And this method of castration is better than the one done by rubbing: because rubbing may leave some part of the testicles, whereby the animal lacks desire for intercourse.
Then care for the wound until it heals.
Chapter Seventy.
Regarding the treatment of hermaphrodites in two methods.
A hermaphrodite is of the male according to two methods. One of them is that there appears between the testicles, on the skin of the testicles, a figure resembling a female vulva, with hair: and sometimes urine flows from that part on the skin of the testicles.
In women, however, there is one type, and it is the woman's womb above the comb like a man's small testicles entirely, protruding to the outside: of which one is like a man's penis, and two like two testicles.
And the treatment for the three types, two from men, and one type from women, is: because it is necessary to cut the excess flesh until the impression of them disappears. Then treat them with the treatment of other wounds.
In the second type of men, from which urine exits, which is in the skin of the testicles, there is no operation, nor is there any treatment for it at all.
Chapter LXXI.
Regarding the incision of tentigines, and protruding flesh in women's wounds.
Tentigo perhaps adds itself above the natural part, until it becomes disfigured and its appearance is丑陋：有时在某些女性中它会增大到像男性一样扩散，甚至影响交配。
Therefore, you must hold the excess of the flap with your hand or with a hook, and cut; and do not delay in cutting, especially at the deep root: so that blood flow does not occur.
Then care for the wound itself until it heals.
The flesh arising is the flesh that grows at the opening of the womb until it fills it; and it may extend outward in the likeness of a tail; and because of this, some first call the ailment tailed. Therefore, we must cut it as we cut the flap, and care for it until it heals.
On the treatment of alraatica, which is an unperforated female ulcer.
Chapter LXXII.
Alraatica is an unperforated female ulcer, or a small opening. And it is either natural or accidental.
Accidental alraatica results from a preceding ailment: it may occur due to added flesh growth, or if fine or thick; and it can form either in the depth of the womb, on its sides, on its upper part, or lower part: it prevents intercourse and conception, childbirth, and may also prevent menstruation.
And its diagnosis is made by the obstetrician's observation if the obstruction is clearly apparent.
If it is not apparent, then seek it with your fingers or with a probe.
If, however, the swelling is from a fine boil and it is close to the two lips: then hurry and break it open.
And it is that you place small particles on the two lips.
Then place your fingers of both hands simultaneously, and the woman should be on her back with her legs spread apart. Then extend the two lips with force until the fine boil is broken and the swelling is opened.
Then take wool, and soak it in oil, and place it on the area: and the woman should apply it every day so that the area does not heal in another way.
If, however, the boil is large and thick: then it is necessary to cut it with a broad spatula similar to a myrtle leaf.
If, however, the swelling is from flesh grown, then suspend it with hooks, and cut it: and let there be with you medicines that stop the flow of blood without mordication, such as acacia, and dragon's blood, and frankincense compounded with egg white.
Then apply a large lead cannula so that the wound does not heal quickly, keep it for several days: and apply lint from dry linen, then treat with the remaining treatment until it is healed.
And sometimes other flesh growths arise in the matrix: therefore, they must be cut according to this method: for it is not a cancerous abscess; no opposition should be made with iron at all for a cancerous abscess that is in the matrix.
Chapter LXXIII.
On the treatment of hemorrhoids, and red botches in the pudenda of women.
Hemorrhoids are the opening of vein orifices, from which much blood flows continuously.
When hemorrhoids become old, they turn into tumors: and I have already spoken about their types and signs: and here I will say which of them can be cured, and which cannot.
I say that hemorrhoids which are at the opening of the womb and are not apparent to the senses: then there is no cure for them with iron.
Those among them that are at the opening of the womb and which can be sensed are those that can be cured.
Therefore, it is necessary to put the woman in a cold room. Then extend the hemorrhoids with scissors, or with a coarse cloth, and cut them from their roots.
Then powder over them at the flow of blood from one of the powders of caustics without biting: such as acacia, dragon's blood, frankincense, and similar substances.
Then press her feet against the wall for one hour. Then place her in cold water.
If the flow of blood persists, then have her sit in a decoction of sumac, pomegranate rind, oak galls, and similar substances.
Then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and vinegar, and make a poultice with it on his back.
If therefore the blood is cut with it, it is good: and if not, make suction blisters adhere to his back without scarification.
Then take wool, and soak it in the juice of tarathit, or the juice of arnoglossae, or the juice of alaulat branches, that is, agaricus, Pontic wine, and make it adhere to the place.
When therefore the abscess rests, then treat the area with ointments until it heals.
Albarth red is similar to the heads of alhaasse, and it has a rough appearance.
Therefore, you must cut what appears from it, according to what I said in thethlil equally: and treat it until it heals.
Chapter LXXIV.
Regarding the perforation of the uterus that occurs in the matrix.
Many types of abscesses occur in the matrix, such as cancer, stone abscess, ulcers, adubelati, alekilati, that is, herpes, aestiomemus, and fistulas, and hemorrhoids, and ragadiae, and thelil, and hot abscess.
And indeed I have already spoken of all these illnesses and their types, and their signs, and their treatments in the division: it is necessary that I speak in this treatise about the hot abscess that occurs in the matrix, when it is among those abscesses that collect pus, and you wish to know how its opening is made with an iron.
Therefore, you must consider. Then if the pain of the abscess at the beginning is sharp with its percussion, and flame, and fever: and you see it reddening: if sensation falls upon it, then do not hurry with its puncture: and treat it with what aids maturity, until when the sharpness of the symptoms subsides.
Then it is necessary to have the woman sit on a seat that slopes down two seats, and recline, or lie on her back, and bring her feet together towards the lower part of her abdomen: and let her thighs be spread apart, and place her arms under her knees, and bind each with a suitable ligature.
Then let the midwife sit on the right side and administer the instrument with which the womb's opening is dilated.
And it is necessary when you wish to administer this instrument, that you insert with the sound the depth of the woman's womb: so that what enters from the instrument is not more than the depth of the womb, and injures the patient.
If the instrument is longer than the depth, then it is necessary to place small pieces on the covering of the womb's depth: so that the entire entry of the instrument is prevented from entering into the depth of the womb: and it is necessary to set the spiral that runs in the instrument, from the upper side: and to hold the instrument, and for the assistant to turn the spiral until the depth of the womb is opened.
Therefore, when the exit is apparent and is touched by hand and is soft and tender: then it is necessary to cut it at its head with a broad spatula.
Therefore, when the pus is drained, then you must place on the wound a linen soaked in rose oil: or green oil, which has some astringency: and place the linen, and remove the incision deeply in the matrix.
And place externally on the matrix, and on the comb clean wool soaked in water, in which sloes have been boiled.
Then it should be treated after two days with an ointment that is suitable for it, until it heals.
And sometimes the matrix and the wound are cleansed by being irrigated with water and honey: then with water in which the root of lily or long aristolochia has been boiled: then return to the ointment.
If the wound is hidden inside the matrix, then you must refrain from treating it with iron, but rather treat it with what we have said in the division.
Chapter LXXIV.
Teaching on Obstetrics, how live embryos should be treated that have been expelled in an unnatural form.
It is necessary for the obstetrician to know first the natural form of childbirth.
From its signs, therefore, it is that when you see a woman compressed in the lower parts, and she desires to breathe in air, and is relieved by what is on her from the labor, and the exit of the embryo is hastened: then you know that this birth is according to the natural form, and its exit is head first, with the afterbirth following it: or hanging, or dangling from the navel.
When therefore you see these signs, then it is necessary that his belly be compressed so that the embryo descends quickly.
For when it descends over its head, the afterbirth descends with it, and it is cleansed of those excesses by a good cleansing.
Whoever is beyond this birth is unnatural, unpraiseworthy.
For sometimes the fetus exits on its feet, and its body comes out before its head, and one of its feet or hand; or its head and hand come out; or the umbilical region comes out: and it may turn around its neck, and similar unpraiseworthy configurations.
It is therefore necessary for the obstetrician to be wise and subtle in all these matters, and to beware of error and deception: and I am showing every configuration among them, and how the method is in it, and what it signifies, and to stand by it.
When the fetus exits on its head by its natural exit, and it becomes violent for the woman, and the birth becomes difficult for her, and you see that her strength is now weakened: then make her sit on a seat, or let women hold her: and fumigate her womb with boiled fenugreek and with moist oils.
Then the obstetrician should insert a small spatula between her fingers, and open the afterbirth with it, and cut it with her nail until what is inside in moisture comes out: and press the woman's belly until the fetus descends.
If it does not descend, then the woman must be given an enema of fenugreek mucilage with sesame oil.
Then instruct him to be compressed after the enema: and make her sneeze with condisi, and hold her mouth and nose for one hour. For the fetus will come out immediately.
If two hands of the fetus come out first, you must gradually and easily return them. If it does not obey at the entry, then place the woman on a seat and lift her feet up: then shake the seat on the ground: and the woman should be held so that she does not fall during the shaking.
If therefore the hands do not come out and the fetus dies: then cut them and extract the remainder of the fetus: and tie its hand with cloth, and extract it equally: for it will come out.
The embryo exits on its feet. When the fetus exits on its feet, then it is necessary to push them upwards: then gradually turn the fetus: afterwards equalize it.
Then take one of its feet and gradually extend it.
When they come out up to the thighs, then instruct her to be compressed, and make her sneeze with condisi: for it will come out, if God wills.
And if it does not come out with what we have mentioned, then gradually return the fetus until you place it according to its natural form. For it will then come out with an easy exit.
If it is prevented with all that we have mentioned: then take from the mucilage of orache, and oil of sesamin, and gum dissolved: and pound all in a mortar well: then anoint with it the womb of the woman, and below her belly. Then make her sit in warm water until she achieves hypochondria.
Therefore, when you see that her lower parts are already warmed, then make for her a sieve of myrrh: and place it. When she holds the sieve for one hour, then make her sit on a seat. Then make her sneeze: and hold her mouth and nose: and press the lower part of her belly with a gentle pressure. For the fetus will come out immediately.
The exit of the fetus is over the knees and hands. When it exits in this manner, then she will gradually bear the insertion of her hands. Then the woman should lie back on her neck, and let her feet hang down below: and she should be lying on the bed, and clasp her hands. Then press above her belly gradually. Then remove what is under her feet from the pillows until she is prepared on the lower part. If the fetus does not come out, then take her feet, and move them with a vigorous motion. Then press what is above the hypochondrium gradually, until the fetus ascends to the upper regions. Then he should insert his hand and gradually align the fetus: and instruct the woman to compress herself until the fetus exits.
The exit of the fetus hanging transversely from the hands. Skill will be required in the reduction of his hand. If he cannot reduce it, then lift the woman and make her walk.
If she cannot walk, then make her lie on a bed: and shake her legs with a violent shaking.
Then apply the liniment that you have prepared from mucilages.
If labor begins for her, then make her sit on a seat. Then attend to the reduction of the hand, and align the fetus according to its natural form: and make the woman sneeze, and instruct her to compress herself until it exits.
The exit of the fetus over its neck, with hands spread out, and its face is toward the back of its mother. The midwife must hold the hand of the fetus, then gradually revolve it and align it with ease.
When it is aligned, then place on its mouth what we have mentioned made from oil and mucilages.
Then instruct her to move gradually. Therefore, when you have done that, then make her sit on a seat, and command her to lean to the right side. Then command her to hold it in: and make her sneeze when you apply it.
The exit of the fetus prepared on the side. When it descends to the opening of the matrix in this manner with the afterbirth, then tear the afterbirth with your nail until it is emptied of moisture.
If it is suspended over the face of the fetus and its neck, then cut it from the navel: so that it is not retained, and causes death.
Then push the fetus inside until you place it as is proper: and command the woman to compress herself several times: for it will come out with a slight effort.
The exit of twins or multiple fetuses. Know that twins are often born: and sometimes three, and four are born. However, that is unusual, and rarely happens.
Five is beyond nature, and they do not live at all: and a single afterbirth contains them, although they multiply, separated by a membrane, distinguishing the tied umbilical cord of each of them.
And sometimes they exit like a single fetus does in a natural, easy birth: and they exit in an unhonorable manner, as we have described.
If some of them are difficult at birth, and they reach what we have said about unnatural forms, then treat them as we narrated: and let it be by a subtle midwife, and she does what is done with ease and slowness, and adapts according to every form with what is prepared for her, guided by skill leading to health.
Remember what is formed in the womb from embryos and is aborted.
Sometimes one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, and more than ten are formed in the womb: and it has already been verified by me that a woman aborted seven, and another fifteen, all formed.
That which was done by the measurement of the glorious wise man.
Therefore, all of this must be known by the obstetrician. For perhaps she may encounter something similar to that; therefore, let her oppose it with what is necessary.
Chapter LXXVI.
Regarding the extraction of a dead fetus.
When you treat a dead fetus with what I have said in the division on medication, and it does not exit, and you are compelled to use manual operation, then you must consider.
If therefore the woman is of sound health, and is not affected by any of the conditions from which loss is feared for her: then the woman must be placed on her back on a bed, with her head inclined downwards and her legs raised: and an assistant should hold her on both sides, or she should be tied to the bed, so that her body is not pulled during the extraction of the fetus.
Then moisten the mouth of the matrix with wet oils mixed with marshmallow, and fenugreek, and flaxseed.
Then the midwife should anoint her hand with these oils and mucilages; then she should insert it into the matrix with ease. Then she should seek with it the place where she can fix the hooks into the fetus, and the suitable places for that.
Consider then if the fetus is prepared to descend headfirst: then fix the hooks into its eyes, or into its neck, or into its mouth, or into its palate, or under its chin, or into its collarbone, or into places near the ribs, and under the hypochondria.
If, however, the descent is feetfirst, then into its hips and its middle ribs.
And it is necessary that she hold the hook with her right hand: and place its curvature between the fingers of her left hand: and insert it with ease, and fix the hook in one of those places which we have mentioned, until she reaches the empty space.
Then she should fix another hook opposite it, or a third one if needed: so that the contraction is equal, and does not lean to one side.
Then it should be extended with equal tension, and not only in a straight line, but it should be moved in all directions to ease its exit: as is done with a tooth during its extraction.
And it is necessary that in the area between those parts, the tension be softened. If any part is retained, then it is necessary for the midwife to anoint certain fingers with oil and insert them so as to turn with them what is retained.
If therefore a part of the fetus comes out, then change the hooks to a higher place: do this until the entire fetus comes out.
If therefore the hand comes out first and it is not possible to reduce it due to its constriction: then it is necessary for a cloth to be wrapped over it. Then extract it until it comes out entirely, cut it either at the ankle joint or at the elbow: and thus you should do with the other hand and with both feet.
If however the fetus's head is large, or it encounters constriction upon exit, or there is water collected in its head: then it is necessary to insert a spathile with spikes between the fingers, and split open the head with it, and draw out the water: or break it with an instrument called Almisdac: whose form comes with the forms of the other instruments in the chapter that follows this.
Similarly do if the fetus has a large head, then it is necessary to cut with an algengematu: or extract it with a misdach, as we have said. Then attract the bones with forceps.
If the head comes out and is constricted at the forking point: then it should be split open until the moisture in the chest is released.
If however it does not become unentangled and does not obey the exit: then cut the head piece by piece, according to what is possible for you.
If there are abscesses in the lower part of the belly, or if there is dropsy in it, then you must pierce it until the fluid flows out.
If the fetus is on its feet, then its extraction is easy, and its orientation towards the maternal canal is simple.
If it is constricted at the belly or chest, then you must extract it with a cloth which you wrap over your hand, and cut open the belly or chest until what is inside flows out.
If the other limbs are removed and the head returns, then the midwife should insert her left hand. If the maternal canal is open, then she should insert her hand deeply into the womb and seek with it the head, and pull it with her fingers until the head reaches the opening of the womb: then insert one hook or two hooks into it, and pull it with them.
If the maternal canal is constricted due to a warm abscess that has occurred in it, then one should not labor over it. Instead, one should administer a flow of moist and fatty substances, and apply plasters, and sit in waters that soften and moisturize.
If the fetus is on its side, then it is possible for it to be aligned: then administer what we have said for a living fetus.
If it is not possible to do that, then it should be cut piece by piece and extracted.
And you must not leave any part of the afterbirth inside at all.
When therefore you have completed your operation, then administer what we said about hot abscesses which occur in the wombs.
If a flow of blood should occur, then bathe in astringent waters, and administer the rest of the treatment.
And I indeed have seen a woman whose belly contained a dead fetus; then she conceived another one over it; afterwards, another fetus also died. Therefore, after a long time, an abscess occurred in his navel, and it swelled until it opened, and began to discharge pus.
I was called therefore for his treatment, and I treated him for a long time: and the wound did not heal.
I therefore applied to it some strongly attracting plasters: and the bone came out from the place. Then after some days had passed, another bone came out. I was therefore amazed at this, since there should not be bone in the belly.
I therefore thought that they were from the bones of the dead fetus.
I therefore examined the wound and extracted many bones, with the woman being in better condition: and she has lived thus for a long time, and discharges only a little pus from the place.
And I did not establish this foreign matter here unless there is knowledge in it, and assistance for what the skilled physician administers by hand in treatment.
Chapter LXXVII.
On the forms of necessary instruments in the extraction of the fetus.
The form of the end by which the matrix is opened.
Here below is the form of the Tightener, with which books are bound, having two equal ends at the extremities of two pieces of wood. However, this end should be finer than the tightener: and it should be made either of ebony or of buxus wood.
And let the width of the entire wood be almost two fingers: and the margin of each of both is almost one finger, and the length of each is a palm and a half: and in the middle of the two pieces of wood are two additions of the same kind of wood, which are already fixed in both, whose length is a half palm and a little more: and the width of each is almost two fingers, or a little more.
And these two additions are inserted into the mouth of the matrix, so that it may be opened with them when you turn the two ends.
Another form similar to that one, finer and lighter.
Let it be made of ebony wood or buxus wood, according to the likeness of forceps. However, at its end there should be two additions, as you see here above: and the length of each addition is almost a palm: and the width of each is two fingers.
Therefore, when you wish to open the matrix with it, then have the woman sit on the bed, with her feet hanging down, and with what is between her legs exposed. Then introduce these two connected additions into the womb: and you are holding the lower end of the instrument between her thighs. Then open your hand with the instrument, as you do with scissors, equally according to the amount you wish from the opening of the womb's mouth, until the midwife does what she wants.
The form of another vertigo which the ancients called the form of the impeller, by which the fetus is propelled.
The form of Almisdac, by which the large head is crushed: and it resembles a forceps, which has teeth at the end, as you see.
And sometimes it is made elongated, like forceps in this form, as you see, which has teeth like the teeth of a saw, by which it cuts and crushes.
The form of a hook having one spine.
The form of a hook having two spines.
The form of a spatula having two ends for cutting off the head.
The form of two broad spatulas.
All these instruments are used, and the more their types are multiplied, and they are prepared by the artisan, the quicker they are for their operation, and they are more esteemed among people because of their quantity.
Therefore, do not disdain any of them so that an instrument may be prepared for you. For the necessity of them is inexcusable.
Chapter LXXVIII.
Regarding the extraction of the afterbirth.
When the afterbirth is retained during childbirth, then you must instruct the patient to hold her breath. Then make her sneeze with condisi: and place your hand over her mouth and nose. If it exits through this method, it is good.
If not: then take a pot and pierce a hole in the cover. Place herbs that open the matrix os in it, such as reed, rue, dill, chamomile, savine, lign aloes, and centaury. Take all these herbs or some of them, submerge them in water, and place them on fire.
Then place a reed tube over the hole in the pot's cover, and put the other end in the os of the matrix: and hold it until the vapor reaches the cavity of the matrix.
Then make her sneeze, as we have said. For the afterbirth will exit with ease.
If it remains after this treatment and does not exit: then instruct the midwife to dip her hand in sesame oil or marshmallow mucilage. Then insert into the wound, and seek with it the second. When therefore he finds it, then let him take it and stretch it out gradually.
If however it is attached deep in the womb, then let him insert his hand as we have described, until he finds the afterbirth, and extract it gradually in a straight line so that the womb does not fall due to forceful pulling: rather it must be shifted with ease to the right and left sides; then increase the amount of pulling. For it obeys then, and is preserved, and escapes from adhering.
If the mouth of the womb is constricted, as we have already mentioned: treat it with sneezing and with the medication of a pot with herbs.
If however it does not come out with all that we have mentioned, then beware lest you fatigue yourself with repeated attempts at extraction.
But it is necessary that what comes out to the mouth of the womb from it, you tie to the woman's thigh. Then cleanse her with an ointment of tetrapharmacum. For it will腐烂它几天后，溶解并排出。(Note: The translation was supposed to be in English, the last part was mistakenly translated into Chinese. Here is the correct English translation.)
However when it becomes putrid, a bad smell rises to the stomach and head, and it harms the weak one. Therefore, appropriate fumigations should be administered for that.
Some of the ancients have already experienced the fumigation of mustard and dried figs.
The form of the instrument used for fumigating a woman in cases of retained afterbirth and menses.
Let it be made from a vessel like alcama, or from horn: and the wider end should be placed over the fire: and the fumigation should be placed on the coals: hold it until that fumigation is consumed: and repeat with another.
Chapter LXXIX.
Regarding the treatment of an unperforated anus.
Many children are born with anunas that are not perforated, which can be opened with a fine probe. Therefore, the midwife should perforate it with her finger: and if not, she should pierce it with a sharp spatula: and she should be careful not to touch the nerve.
Then place wool soaked in wine and oil on it. Then treat it with ointments until it heals.
If you fear it may close again, then place a lead tube in the opening for many days, and remove it when the child needs to defecate.
And it also happens that the anus is blocked due to the healing of a wound or an abscess. Therefore, that consolidation must be cut, then it should be treated with what we have said about treatment and lead.
Chapter LXXX.
On the treatment of fistulas which occur in the lower part.
Fistulas which occur in the lower part are Nodulation and Swelling which happen near the anus externally: or in the space of one part: and it is one Fistula or multiple.
When that nodulation becomes old, it opens, and a watery white moisture or thin pus runs out of it.
And sometimes these fistulas are penetrating. Therefore, penetrating ones are recognized by what exits with excrement and flatulence, when the patient has a bowel movement: and perhaps worms may exit from them.
And among these are fistulas when they are in the space penetrating as far as the bladder, and as far as the urethra. And among these are those that penetrate as far as the hip joint, and as far as the coccyx.
From which it is known that a penetrating fistula reaches the anus, and differs from a non-penetrating one, is to insert your index finger into the anus: and to insert a thin probe made of air, or iron, into the fistula when there is no tortuosity.
If there is a twist in it, then insert into it a thin thread of lead or a hair from horses' mane until you feel the thread or hair with your finger.
If you do not feel it thoroughly, and nothing comes out of the opening from discharge, nor gas, nor worm as I said: then know that it is not penetrating: therefore hurry to the treatment.
And when the fistula penetrates to the bladder or to the urine passage: then its indication is the discharge of urine from it, and the prevention of consolidation of the area with medicines.
If it penetrates to the hip joint or to the hip bone: then the sign of this is that the probe reaches there, if there is no twist up to the bone: and the discovery of pain around the part, and that pus always comes out from it: and that treatment is not effective, nor does it consolidate with ointment.
And in all these penetrating fistulas there is no cure at all: and the treatment of them is labor and vanity for him, by foolish doctors, upon whom it is formed.
In that which is not penetrating and not old, healing is hoped for with a scalpel: according to what I narrate to you, and I have already tested: and it is that the patient lies on their back under your hands: and lift their legs up above their hips, and their hips should be inclined towards their abdomen. Then insert a thread of lead or brass if there is a twist in the fistula until you know where the thread reaches.
If however he feels it weak around the anus, then you must insert your index finger into the anus.
If therefore you feel the thread has already penetrated by itself through the detected area, besides what you feel between your finger and the surface or the flesh: then therefore you know certainly that it is penetrating: do not therefore labor over it, for its healing is not possible, as we said.
They said, however, that the flesh is healed in some men and from the treatment in which hope of help lies is to ignite a fine cauterium according to the width of the fistula, as mentioned before, and insert it ignited into the fistula until it reaches around the anus. Then do this again twice or three times until you know that all those additional filtered flesh parts, which are like the hollow tubes of a bird's feather, have been burned away.
Then treat it with lint wrapped in butter until the burned flesh comes out: then treat it with ointments that generate flesh and strengthen.
If therefore it is healed, it is good.
And if not, then it will never be healed with any other treatment.
And if the thread comes out and does not reach your finger which is in the anus, and there is a thick veil of flesh or membrane between it and the thread: and you see the fistula following the surface of the skin, then cut the skin from the beginning of the fistula, and you go cutting with the thread that is in the fistula until the incision reaches where the end of the thread is, and the thread is freed and falls out.
Then clean those filtered flesh pieces which resemble a bird's feather tube so that nothing remains from them.
If the blood overcomes you and separates you from your operation so that you cut those flesh: then it is better and quicker to heal by cauterizing it with fire or with sharp medicine.
For the cautery with fire brings good properties, the burning of those added flesh, and the cutting off of blood, and the drying of moistures.
Then treat it with lint wrapped in butter, or crushed fat, until the place emits pus, and those burned flesh come out with the pus.
Then treat the wound with consolidating ointments, producing hard flesh: and there are medicines that have astringency and drying properties.
For when they are restored, then it is already healed: and you do not fear repetition.
If however the fistula has already reached deep into the anus, and extends from the excess of the body: then insert your finger into the anus, and explore with it.
If therefore you feel a tent, and between you and it there is a veil of sinew or flesh, and it is close to penetration: then there is no operation in that place unless according to the way of confidence and hope.
Which means that one of the three methods is applied to it: either you cauterize it as we said: or you cut it until you reach its concavity, so that it is possible for you to insert lint and apply treatment close by. And do not proceed much with the cutting so as not to cut the tendon containing the anus, and involuntary loss of stool occurs in the patient. Then treat it with what we have said.
For it may be healed: or you may remove the covering itself, and clean it after you cut it close to the anus, as we have said, either with a probe, or with another instrument of sharp end. Then clean the filtered flesh that is in the incision as far as you can with probing.
Then attempt the restoration of the entire wound with the incision, and the upper opening where it is consolidated: and the fistula remains open on the inner part of the anus, and it will be milder for the patient.
And sometimes the fistula is sutured in this manner: and it is when you insert a probe into the fistula: and it is on the side of the anus near the surface of the body with the skin and margin of the anus: then take a probe with a perforated end, which is like a tanner's needle, that is, of those who prepare hides, in this form. And insert into it a thread wrapped from five threads, and around it. Then insert the probe with the thread into the fistula until it reaches its concavity.
If it penetrates into the inner margin of the anus nearby, then pull the thread out from that opening: so that you insert your finger into the anus and pull out the end of the thread, and bring both ends together: and hold both tightly, and leave it for one day, or two days: and the more the thread cuts into the flesh, hold it tight until the flesh between the two ends of the thread is cut and falls off: then treat the wound until it consolidates and heals.
If however the opening of the fistula is not penetrating then make it penetrate in whatever way is prepared for you unless it is very deep. For it is not in you to do that because of the flap, so as not to cut it.
Then do with it as we have said until it heals.
The form of the thorny spatula with which the fistula is split, whose curvature is very sharp, and the other part is not sharp, so as not to cut what is not necessary, as you see.
Chapter LXXXI.
About the suturing of hemorrhoids, from which blood runs from their incision: and the treatment of fissures.
There are hemorrhoids in two ways. For they are either inside the anus, resembling coal sacs or ember sacs, or they are like individual grape grains. And among them there are small ones and large ones: and blood runs from them always, and there is one, and there are many. And they are outside the anus, and at its extremities.
However, those which are outside the anus are mostly lacking in moisture, from which yellow water or a little blood runs continuously: and they are according to the color of the body.
And the treatment of that which is inside the anus is to instruct the patient to dilate: and to express until the anus protrudes, and the hemorrhoids appear to you. Therefore, hang them with hooks: or hold them with your nail. Then cut them at their roots.
If however they do not hold the hooks, because of their moisture and softness: then take them with a coarse cloth, or with a mitten made of woolen material, and pull them out with your fingers. Then cut them, and sprinkle on them after the cutting certain hot powders, to serve in place of a cautery. Or cauterize them according to what preceded in the chapter on cauterizing. Then care for them with the rest of the treatment until they heal.
If the anus does not obey evacuation, then administer an enema to the patient that contains a slight irritant, so that it cleanses what is in the anus and obeys evacuation quickly when the patient expels it.
If however the growths are external to the anus, then their treatment is light and easy: it is as you take them with your nail, or you take them with a hook, and cut them. Then care for them with what we have said until they heal.
And for those who shrink from incision with iron, then it is necessary to administer their stitching according to this method. Take the wrapped thread and insert it into the needle. Then pull the growth upward, and make it penetrate with the needle at its root from the other side: and wrap both ends of the thread around the lower part of the needle, and let them be horizontal: and bind the growth with a strong tie. Then tie the thread, and remove the needle.
Do this with all the athelil, and leave one of them untouched: do not heat it, so that the excess blood may flow from it.
Then place a cloth soaked in rose oil or cerote over the anus, and put it on the anus: and instruct the patient to rest. Then leave it until it falls.
When the athelil fall, care for them with ointments and the rest of the treatment until they heal.
Regarding the treatment of fissures. For they often occur from the dryness of the stool and the constriction of the bowel movement.
When they become old and medicine does not heal them, then it is necessary to scrape with the edge of a scalpel or with your nail until they become moist, and remove the outer layer that prevents them from healing. Then care for them until they heal as necessary.
If they do not heal, then scrape them more vigorously than before until they bleed heavily, and remove the outer layer; then care for them until they heal.
Regarding the treatment of inverted and non-inverted almirmar, and dry athelil, and ants.
Chapter LXXXII.
Know that almirmar is nothing but a round knot according to the color of the body, similar to the head of a nail: and it occurs throughout the body, especially in the lower parts of the feet and toes: and pain occurs from them while walking.
Therefore, what is around the nail should be cut and held with scissors or with a hook and pulled out from its root.
Then care for it: and if you wish, cauterize it according to what has been precedented in its chapter.
From the dry athelil there is a small prominence, rough, filtered, round on the surface of the body. And they often occur in the hands of children.
And the treatment is to stretch the athelil and cut it, or tie it with silk thread, or with hair until it falls. And if you wish, cauterize it according to what has been mentioned with fire or with sharp medicine: and now the athelil are eradicated, both inverted and not inverted with the instrument that I call.
The formica is also a small, filtered, thick prominence on the surface of the body, going very deep: and when cold encounters it, it feels like an ant bite, and it occurs throughout the whole body: and it mostly happens in the hands.
And the treatment is to take a tube from a goose feather or a strong vulture feather: and place that tube over the formica until the circle of the tube contains parts of it. Then turn your hand with the tube until you cut what is around the formica: and place it deep into the flesh, and pull out the formica from its root.
And if you wish, do it with a tube of brass or iron, according to this form.
Let the upper part of the cannula be drawn up high and wrapped around, so that its grip on the finger may be eased and its rotation.
And if you wish to cauterize the Ant as mentioned in the cauterization of Athelil in the chapter on the cautery.
Chapter LXXXIII.
Regarding the forms of instruments used for enemas in diseases of the anus, and for relief of the bowels, and colic.
Sometimes an enema is made of silver, or brass, or cast metal, or hammered metal.
And sometimes these instruments are made small and large according to those in which they are used.
Therefore, that which is used in the treatment of small children should be small: and for those whose anuses are weak or painful, their enemas should be so as well.
Large enema.
Its tube, that is, the upper head where the bag is tied, should be wide in this manner: and it should have a distinct part where the bag is tied as you see, and its lower end which is inserted into the anus should be closed, that is, not open, very soft, tapering to fineness: and on one side there should be two holes, and on the other side one hole.
And the width of the hole should be according to the thickness of the rays and a little thicker, and the bag in which the medicines are placed should be made of an animal's bladder: or of sheepskin, which should be in the shape of a small asofrati: whose base is one palm.
And it should be pierced with many holes as it is turned, and let the space that is between every hole be the thickness of a finger. Then insert into those holes a strong thread made of raw silk, which should be composed of ten threads, or about that number, and join it with the skin like asofrati. When the skin is placed on it, it should be tied tightly around the head of the enema between two distinguishing constrictions. Then administer the enema with it.
And this is the form of the circle and the holes depicted here with the skin.
The quality of administering the enema with it is as follows: fill the skin or bladder with medicine that is warmed according to the quantity tolerated by the patient: and beware that it is not too hot or too cold.
Then the patient should lie on their back, and raise their legs upwards: and place under them a mat, that is, skin or cloth on which people lie, or a linen sheet.
Then anoint the end of the enema with oil, or with egg white, or with fenugreek mucilage, or similar substances. Then insert it into the anus easily. Then the administrator should take the skin with both hands simultaneously, and squeeze it vigorously until all that is in the enema is emptied into the intestine.
Then remove the enema, and let the patient raise his legs against the wall.
If medicine drives him to an end, then let it hold as much as it can. And if he sleeps with her the entire night, it is more ultimate in healing.
If you give him an enema for intestinal ailments, and its effect is swift: then repeat the enema until he is healed.
If there are hemorrhoids or painful abscesses in the anus, then let the enema be very fine and gentle, such as those with which children are given enemas.
And this should be the form of a fine enema for which the skin is tight.
Chapter LXXXIV.
I have already said in the division regarding the treatment of wounds what was appropriate for the book, and I will now speak here of their treatment with the hand and with medicines according to completion.
I say, therefore, that wounds differ according to the instrument by which they are inflicted and according to the place where the wound falls.
The things by which wounds are caused are often various, such as being hit by a stone, or cut by a sword or dagger, or struck with a lance, wood, or arrow, and similar objects from many other things.
Wounds that are inflicted according to the parts of the body are, for example, a wound that falls on the head, or neck, or chest, or abdomen, or spleen: and similar ones from other limbs.
And I am telling the treatments of some wounds, so that I may set forth that reasoning and rule on other wounds.
And I will begin with simple head wounds: because the mention of compound wounds will come at the beginning of the third chapter.
Therefore, I say. When a simple wound occurs on the head, and there is no fracture of the bone: then consider if it is from the throw of a stone or similar objects, and has only broken the skin: and the wound is large, and you fear an unfavorable outcome of hot abscess: then hurry and immediately perform phlebotomy on the cephalic vein: and do not delay this: and withdraw blood according to the strength of the patient: if there is nothing prohibiting phlebotomy, especially if little blood is coming out from the wound. And let the phlebotomy be performed on the opposite side of the wounded area.
And let the phlebotomy be performed on the opposite side of the wounded area. And let the patient beware of excess, and wine, and heavy foods.
If however something prohibits bloodletting, then let the diet be reduced, and let no meat or wine be approached.
And apply to the wound, if a hot abscess occurs, lint infused in rose oil alone, or with wine that has astringent properties.
If however you are certain there will be no hot abscess, then apply to the wound, if it is fresh with its own blood and has not been altered by air, the powder which I will describe shortly: and if it has already been altered by air, then apply some ointments until it heals.
If the wound is large, or from a sword cut, and the like: and its edges do not come together with small pins, then bring them together with stitches, as I will narrate concerning wounds of the belly regarding their stitching.
If the wound is already separated from the bone, and hangs loose, and there is no retention of it except with a small sling: then cut it off. Then treat the wound with medicines, and restore hard flesh instead of skin, and advise the patient to nourish themselves with foods that are thickening, such as heads, and cooked wheat until it is like porridge: and things similar to these.
If you find putrefaction in the skin, and it does not adhere to the bone: then cut out all the putrefied part and discard it: then treat it.
If in these wounds there is an artery or vein from which blood flows: and it is not stopped by medications, then apply pressure on the artery. If you find it uncut, then cut it with a scalpel, or tie it off. If necessity demands that what we have said cannot be accomplished, then cauterize it until the blood is stopped.
If these wounds are small and simple, then their treatment is easy and light: so that you may sprinkle this powder on them: for it consolidates them before the air alters them.
Method of the Flesh-forming Powder. Take one part of oil, and two parts of dragon's blood, and three parts of unslaked lime: grind the whole much, and sieve it: and fill the wound with it, and bind it well, until it adheres to it well, and coagulates with the blood.
Then bind it with bandages from above, and leave it, and do not loosen it as long as it remains, so that it does not become swollen. For the medicine is not removed from it until it is healed.
And sometimes the lime alone does it, when you do not have oil and dragon's blood at hand; and dragon's blood also performs the same operation on many large wounds, when it is appropriate to put it on them and bind them, and the wounds are fresh with their own blood which has not been altered by air.
If the air has already altered them in some way, especially when it is summer, then this powder's intention is not effective: so care for it with what we have said, placing some digestive ointments on them; or put on them poultices made from barley flour mixed with water and honey, until they discharge pus. Then care for it with the remaining treatment until it is healed.
If a fracture in the bone occurs with the wound and it is small, then extract it with a probe: and I will now speak of the treatment for fractures of the head in what is to come.
Regarding wounds of the neck.
If a wound occurs on the neck, then there is no difference in its treatment, and for a simple head wound.
If the nerve or artery of the neck has already been cut: then if it is a nerve, there is no skill in it except to treat it with something that causes strong styptic effect, such as ziniar, and zegi, and things similar to these. For they harm the nerves and contract them.
And you shall not apply anything cold at all to the wound: for the substance of the nerves is cold, and its continuation is with the brain, which is the noblest part of the members: and let that with which it is cured be mild from medicines, such as lime washed several times with sweet water mixed with oil, or with rose oil, and turpeth mineral, when it is also washed with sweet water: and the other mineral stones in this manner, and moist ointments.
If the wound is large, then apply sutures: or bind its edges with compresses. Then treat it until it heals.
If the wound has depth, or a sinus has formed in its lower part where pus has already collected, then puncture it at the most depressed place in it.
If an artery has already been cut in the wound and its flow of blood has started: then separate or cut it and ligate it: or cauterize it if the necessity calls for it.
If the windpipe or its entirety has been cut, but the alae nasi are saved: then approximate the skin edges with sutures over the windpipe, and do not touch the windpipe, rather level it and reduce it to its natural form. Then bind it with a proper bandage, and leave it for several days. Then treat it with ointments that have astringent and drying properties until it heals.
If the wound has already made an impression on the bone, then examine it: then if there are fragments of bone in it, remove all of them, or as many as you can: and what does not prepare, leave it until the wound putrefies, and it separates and its discharge is alleviated.
If the wound is fresh, then sprinkle on it the powder I mentioned. If bone appears in the wound and a fistula forms, then treat it with the method mentioned in its respective chapter.
Regarding the wound on spatulas.
If there is a stab from a lance or a knife, and you see its depth, then examine it. If wind or gas exits the wound when the patient breathes on it, then you know that the wound is mortal.
If it does not have depth and is fresh with its blood, then do not apply powder to it right away or bind it, so that blood does not remain in its depth and return to the heart, killing the patient: instead, apply a drawing ointment to it and unbind it twice a day.
If ointment is not available, then place an old piece of wool on the wound's opening to absorb what comes out from its moisture: and have the patient lie down on the wound so that what accumulates in it can flow out.
If however three days have passed since the wound, or more, and spasms do not occur to the patient, nor bad palpitations of the heart, nor constriction in breathing, and you see his other conditions good: then know that the wound is safe. Treat it therefore with rue and other treatments until it is healed.
If however its healing is hindered, and it is now always open, then know that it has become a fistula. Treat it therefore according to its chapter.
And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it is simple on the surface of the chest or back: then treat it with what precedes regarding suturing, if it is large; or with powder, if it is small.
And if it has already made an impression on the bone and fragments have broken off: then examine the wound and quickly remove those fragments, if they are separated. If however they are not separated, then leave them until the wound becomes putrid, for their extraction is eased then.
The judgment in the treatment of other wounds occurring in other limbs is the same as what we have said.
About wounds of the abdomen, and the protrusion of the intestines, and their treatment.
The disruption that occurs in the abdomen is major, medium, and minor.
Sometimes therefore the intestine or a number of intestines protrudes from the large one.
Therefore, their insertion and their suture are more forceful and difficult.
And even a small rupture becomes difficult in another way. Therefore, it follows that their reduction is more difficult if you do not promptly return them to their place immediately: because they inflate, open up, and swell: hence their entry becomes difficult.
Therefore, the moderate rupture is better: because with it, the reduction of the intestine is not difficult, as it is difficult in those two types.
Know that the suture of the abdomen is according to four methods.
Two common sutures are used for the suture of the abdomen and for the suture of other wounds of the body: and two other sutures are specifically used for the other wounds. However, they are more specific for the suture of the abdomen: and I will tell you each one with an explanation and description.
I say therefore, that when the wound is small, and something of the intestine protrudes from it, and it becomes difficult to reduce it: then this is because of one of two methods. Either because of the smallness of the rupture, as we said: or because there is swelling in the intestine due to the cold air.
Therefore, when it is thus, then you must warm it, so that you soak a sponge or a wet cloth in warm water alone. Or boil in water squills, and cyperus, and spike, and bind with it the intestine until the swelling dissolves.
Sometimes he makes it with wine in which there is astringency: and it is better than water alone in resolving the swelling.
When you see that the swelling has already dissolved, then moisten the intestine with water in which althea or mallows have been boiled. For by that means its entrance is alleviated with a small object.
If, however, the return of it occurs after this treatment, then find and cut slightly in the area of disruption with the instrument used to cut hemorrhoids.
And the first treatment is better when prepared than cutting; and there should be no compulsion to cut after necessity and lack of instruments.
Let one part of it be twisted, sharp, and the other part not sharp, and the end should be fine but not as delicate as a spatula, rather somewhat blunt: and it is that which resembles a probe, as you see.
When the wound enlarges and enters the intestine, then it is necessary to reduce it according to its natural form in its proper place if possible: for that is better.
When the disruption is wide in the lower part of the abdomen: then it is necessary to have the patient lie on their back, and place their legs higher than their head. And if it is in the upper part of the abdomen, then place his head and chest higher than his lower parts.
And similarly if there is a disruption in one of the two parts of the abdomen, then place your attention and your consideration always on this, that the part in which there is a wound be higher than the other part.
And thus you should apply it to large wounds and medium wounds.
In small wounds, apply it according to how it is prepared for you.
Then make sure that a faithful attendant is present at your side, who will hold the entire disruption with his hand: and bring together its lips. Then uncover it for the one who follows the suture, piece by piece: and this is the method of a common suture.
And it is such that you take a needle, or a number of needles according to the quantity of the wound's size. Then leave a quantity of one finger's width from the end of the disruption, that is, the doctor's: and insert one needle with thread at both ends of the skin, passing through the sifac which is under the skin from the inside, until it penetrates from the other side, and you have now brought together two ends of the skin, and two ends of the sifac: and there are four layers.
Then tighten with double thread around the needle several times from both sides simultaneously, until the two lips of the wound are brought together with a proper approximation.
Then leave the thickness of another finger, and insert another needle into it: then tie it with thread as you did with the first needle. Therefore do not cease to do that with what you need from the linen until you complete the constriction of the whole wound.
And let the needles be of medium thickness between thick and thin: for very thin needles cut the flesh quickly: and thick ones have difficulty entering the skin: therefore they must be of medium thinness and thickness.
And it is not appropriate for the needle to be fixed at both ends of the skin that are very close: so that the flesh is not cut quickly, and the wound is opened before its consolidation, and they are not stretched even with the suture, so that the wound is not prevented from consolidating.
Then cut the tips of the needles so they do not harm the patient during their sleep: and place small pieces of cloth from clothes on all sides to hold the tips of the needles: and leave them until you know that the wound is already consolidated.
And this type of suture with needles is more suitable for small wounds. For one needle, or two, or about that number is sufficient for their suture.
The second common suture is to join the four ends together: two ends of the skin and two ends of the sifac alternately, with a needle on which is wound thread equal in thinness and thickness.
Then when you have penetrated these four ends with the needle, withdraw the needle from the side where you started, so that the thread falls back from the upper part of the wound: so that the suture is like the suture of cloth by which cloths are drawn together, and place between each suture the thickness of a little finger.
Men know this suture.
And with this suture I treated the wound that had occurred to a man in his belly, who had been wounded with a knife, and the tear of the wound was more than one palm: and about two palms had come out from the middle intestine, and there was a tear in the middle of the belly.
I therefore replaced it after his intestine had been outside the wound for twenty-four hours.
The wound thus healed within about fifteen days: and I treated him, and he was healed: and he lived for many years afterward, in his usual condition.
And the doctors had judged that he would not be healed.
And it was a miracle that I did not treat it with an ointment. For I was in a place where no ointment could be found, nor any other medicine. I therefore placed old dung on the wound twice a day, and continually washed it with honey water until it was healed.
I will now speak of two types of sutures according to the account of the discussion.
And it is to begin with a sharp suture: and insert the needle from the outer to the inner part.
When the needle penetrates the skin, and goes into the flesh according to the length and breadth of the whole body: leave one end as you inserted the needle on the side where you introduced it, and make it penetrate to the other end from the inner part to the outer part on the opposite side.
When therefore you make it penetrate, then make it penetrate according to this at the same end of mirach from the outer part to the inner: and leave the end of sifac which is on this side, and make the needle penetrate to the other end from the inner part to the outer: and make it penetrate with your penetration by which you make it penetrate in the end of sifac at the mirach which is on its part, until it penetrates into the whole of it.
Then begin again from this same side, and sew it with the end which is from sifac on the other side, and pull the needle out from the skin which it penetrated.
Then bring it back to that skin, and sew the end of sifac which is on the other side with this end of mirach: and pull it out from the skin which is on its part, and do this alternately, one after another: and do this turn by turn until you sew all around according to this example.
And the aim of this stitching is to sew the sutures of the skin flaps in such a way that you sew sifac alternately from one side of the skin end: and leave it alternately from the other side until you complete it.
The second type of proper suture, which Galen mentioned.
This his method is described so that you sew it according to the manner in which some of the physicians sew them, aggregating each part to its corresponding matching part by nature: and they apply one end of sifac to its other end, and one end of mirach to the other end of it. And it is done according to what I tell you.
You must fix the needle at the end of the bandage nearest to you from the outer side, and make it penetrate to the inner side at that point only: and leave two ends of the suture. Then turn the needle and make it penetrate from the outer side to the inner side at two ends of the suture, that is, on both sides.
Then turn both, also make both penetrate from the inner to the outer side, at two ends of the bandage which are on the opposite side.
And this method of suturing is better than the common easy suturing, and it is the suturing that has been previously mentioned.
This is therefore the teaching of Galen as well.
And some have said. The abdominal suture is corrected with two needles. Which means you insert one thread into both: and begin with the insertion of the needle, from the part that is nearest to you, and make it penetrate all the way to the other side, according to the suturing of those who sew the skins evenly.
And you should know that when the rupture is in the middle of the abdomen: then its suturing is more difficult than that of other parts of the abdomen.
The judgment of the treatment of a wound is the judgment of other wounds.
Which means that when you encounter a fresh wound with its blood before the air alters it: and you reduce the intestine, and return it to its place, and adjust it: then apply pulverized incarnative over it.
If the air has already altered the wound: then apply some ointments that are available to you until they cause pus to form: and let the threads fall out, and the sinews consolidate and heal. Then care for it as you would treat other wounds until it is healed.
If the medicines are not available to you, then apply old dung immediately when it starts to emit pus: and change it twice a day, as I have taught you, until it is healed.
For you do not need other medications in most cases when the wounds are simple.
If you fear that the wound may spread to the principal members in the injury, then it is necessary to soak a soft wool in oil of moderate heat, or in rose oil: and apply it around the areas between the groin, and under the armpits.
If he feels pain, or pricks, or putrefaction in his intestines (for this often happens), then cleanse him with a styptic, black, warm wine enema: especially if the putrefaction has already reached the intestine and caused a discharge penetrating to its concavity.
And know that what comes from the large intestine is easier to heal: and what comes from the small intestine is harder to heal.
However, the intestine known as the Jejunum does not accept healing from a wound that occurs in it at all: and this is due to the abundance of its veins, and their size, and because of the fineness of its body, and its closeness to the nature of nerves.
If however that which comes out from the wound is flesh, and you catch it fresh: reduce it according to your reduction, by which you equally reduce the intestines.
If however the time has passed, and it has already turned green or black: then it is necessary to tie it with a thread above the place which has been darkened by it, so that blood flow does not occur. For in flesh there are veins and arteries.
Then cut what is beyond that ligament, and place the two ends of the thread hanging from the lower part of the wound outside it: so that the pulling of it is eased for you, and its extraction in case of flesh detachment and pus discharge from the wound.
Reminder of the wound that occurs in the intestine.
When a rupture occurs in the intestine and it is small: then it is possible for it to be restored in some people: therefore, because I have seen someone who was wounded in his belly with a lance strike, and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and the wound was old: and it became a fistula, and excretions and flatulence came out from it.
I therefore applied treatment until I was no longer confident in his healing: nor did I cease to care for him carefully until he was healed and the area was strengthened.
After I saw the area already strengthened, I was concerned about the patient, that a bad accident might occur in his belly: and no such bad accident happened to him. And he remained in better dispositions, eating and drinking, and having intercourse, and entered the bath, and exercised in his diets.
And some of the experimenters have said that when a small wound occurs in the intestine, then it must be tied according to this method. And it is that you take ants with large heads. Then bring together the two lips of the wound, and place one of the ants which have an open mouth over the two lips of the wound. When therefore it bites on them and closes its mouth, cut off its head, for it adheres and does not loosen.
Then place another ant near the first one, and do not cease to do this with each ant after the other according to the extent of the entire wound.
Then reduce it, and sew the wound. For those heads remain attached to the intestine until the intestine is nourished and healed, and no harm befalls the patient thoroughly.
And now it is possible to suture the intestine even with a fine thread: which is cleaned from the intestine of an animal, attached to the needle after it is inserted.
And it is that you take the end of this thread from the intestine, and clean it thoroughly. Then tie a fine linen thread at its end tightly. Then insert that thread into the needle, and sew the intestine with it. Then replace it in the wound.
And this method of sewing with ants and intestine is only according to the way of confidence and hope.
Know, a wound that is large, wide, especially if it is in one of the thin intestines: then there is no remedy except for narrowing, and there is no healing of it at all.
On the treatment of Zuchemen and Fistulas.
Know, that every wound or abscess when it becomes old and aged, and turns into an ulcer, and does not heal, and constantly emits pus, and does not cease: then it is universally called a Fistula wherever it may be in the body, and we name it Zuchemen.
And the Fistula indeed is according to truth a hardened, white, filtered knot: with which there is no pain, and it has the concavity of a bird's feather: and because of this some name it Risati, that is, feather.
And at certain times it is moist, emitting pus. And perhaps the moisture splits at certain times. And sometimes this moisture is abundant, and at other times it is scarce: and it is thick, and it is thin.
And I have already mentioned in the division when I said wounds, that every ulcer that does not heal, and in which flesh does not grow, is not so except for one of nine causes.
One of them is either due to the scarcity of blood in the body; or due to the bad quality of it; or because there is hard flesh between it and its lips, preventing the birth of flesh; or because it is full of dirt and filth; or because the ulcer itself is putrid, and the material discharged from it is of poor quality; or because the medicine used for its cure is unsuitable; or because the corruption falling in the region is a type of pestilence, or due to the characteristic of the region, as happens in Caesaraugusta: where the digestion of diseases becomes difficult, and the healing of abscesses by nature is delayed there; or because it has one bone or a number of bones.
And I have already shown all these causes and their signs, and their cures with medicines in the division: and it is necessary here that I make you know the cure of Fistula and Zukens, which is done by the way of surgery with the hand.
Know therefore, that Fistula occurs in all the members of the body. For from these are the Fistulas that reach the large veins and arteries, or nerves, or spine: or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to any of the ribs: or to any of the vertebrae of the back, or to any of the compound joints: such as the hand, and foot: and from these are those that go to the proximity of the principal member, and similars.
Therefore, among these Fistulas, those that occur in this manner are of difficult healing and do not accept treatment, and dealing with them is labor and ignorance.
If there is any Fistula whose depth does not reach the places I mentioned: and you hope and have confidence in its cure, and wish to understand it, then take a probe of metal or iron, if the Fistula extends in a straight line, and examine it with it.
If however there is a winding in the fistula, then investigate it with a thin lead probe. Because lead, with the softness of its body, is lightened and curved around the winding.
If the fistula has many openings, it is not possible for you to indicate on it with a probe. Therefore, choose one opening from its openings for enema.
For the moisture with which you perform the enema goes towards the other openings and runs out from them.
Then carefully investigate in whatever way is possible for you: to know whether there is an opening or a nerve, and whether the Fistula's cavity is far or near: or whether it is one Fistula with many openings, and stand over all of this with the utmost strength of your inquiry, with your questioning of the patient, and by finding pain upon pressing with your hand on the area, and similar indications and causes leading to the formation of an abscess.
Therefore, when you have stood at all those true stations, then proceed to the cure with confidence: and this is to consider whether the Fistula is a near one that appears, or in a safe place far from the joint, or from the nerve, or artery, or vein, or one of the places I told you about: then cut the Fistula as mentioned in my narrative, and remove what is in it from filtration, and corrupted flesh, which grows at its opening from the flesh, or thelul, and similar things: and care for it until it heals.
If however the Fistula is of deep length and is straight: then it is necessary to cut it deeply as much as possible for you. Then cleanse it from all its corrupted flesh.
Then apply licinia wrapped in sharp medicines: and insert it until the concavity of the fistula you grasped with iron: do this several times with it, until the sharp medicine corrodes all that remains in the concavity of the fistula from the corruption.
Then restore it with ointments that generate healthy flesh until it is healed.
If however it does not heal through that, then cauterize it according to what we have mentioned.
If therefore the cause of the fistula is bone, and it is confirmed to you: then seek it out, and cut it according to what I have told you: unless something prevents you from doing so by a vein, or nerve, or principal member, as we have said.
If therefore the bone is revealed to you, and there is something of corruption and blackness in it: then scrape it until all its corruption is removed. Then treat it with what causes flesh to grow on it until it is healed.
If it does not heal and discharges pus as it did before: then you know that you have not achieved the complete eradication of the corruption.
Reveal it again, and carefully examine it and cleanse it with all your strength.
Then restore it. If it heals, that is good: and if not, then you know that the corruption is in a deep part of the body, which you have not reached. Therefore, there is no ingenuity for you in it, except to leave it to nature.
If a small bone is corrupted, and it is possible for you, pull it out with subtle scissors that are suitable for it.
If there are many bones, then carefully perform the extraction of all of them, and do not leave any of them with your strength.
If something from the humors opposes you, and there is no fear or mistake in cutting them: then cut those humors and flesh, if they are there, and free the bones.
If you are not prepared to remove the bones at your time, then apply something to the wound that will cause it to rot: and leave it until what surrounds those bones from flesh and humors putrefies.
And guard the wound so that it does not heal. And let the incision which you made in your operation be constricted. Rather, apply to it, if you fear, tow soaked in ground sulfur with oil: or tow soaked in Egyptian ointment, or some green ointment.
For when those humors putrefy and the bones separate from them, the removal of them is alleviated, and their extraction.
If there is one large bone, such as the bone of the leg, or the bone of the hip, and similar to these, and what is corrupted in it is a large part: then scrape it with the finest scraper until that blackness and corruption are removed. Then restore the wound.
If however what is corrupted in it is a large part, and the corruption has already reached the marrow of the bone, then it is necessary to saw through it, and cut it entirely until the place where the corruption reaches: then treat it until it consolidates.
And I tell you a story that happened to a man in his leg: that you may set it as an example and aid for your operation.
There was a man of about thirty years of age, to whom pain occurred in his leg, caused by something moving within his body, that is, from the interior, until the matter reached the leg and formed a large abscess: and he did not have an external cause.
Therefore, time was wasted with the error of the physicians until the abscess was opened, and a great deal of matter came out with it. And his treatment was delayed until the leg became fistulated, and many openings were formed in it: all of which discharged pus and bodily fluids.
Therefore, he was treated by a multitude of physicians for about two years, and there was no skilled hand in the art until I was called, and I saw his leg, and the matter flowing from those openings in great abundance: moreover, the whole body of the man had already wasted away, and his color was yellow.
I therefore inserted a probe into one of the openings, and the probe reached the bone.
Then I examined all the openings: and I found them to connect with each other from all parts of the leg.
I hurried therefore, and cut above one of those orifices, until I exposed part of the bone: and I found it corrupted: which was already corroded, and blackened, and had putrefied, and was perforated, until it had penetrated as far as the marrow.
I sawed therefore what was revealed to me and prepared from the corrupted bone.
