And I cut away so that there would be nothing in the bone except that corruption which I severed and sawed. And I had already eradicated it.
Then I placed the restoration of the wound with consolidating medicines for a long period. And it was not consolidated.
Then I tried and exposed above the second bone beyond the first exposure: and I found continuous corruption with the bone: and I sawed what appeared to me also from that corruption.
Then I attempted its restoration. And it was not restored.
I exposed it again and did not cease to cut the bone bit by bit, and attempted its restoration: and it was not restored, until I cut about one palm from the bone, and extracted it with its marrow.
Then I restored it with medicines, and it was consolidated quickly, and healed: and this repetition in its operation and section was not necessary, except due to the disposition of the patient's weakness, and the lack of his tolerance, and my fear for him of death: for he was fainting at all times from an excess of evacuation.
He was therefore healed completely: and hard flesh formed in place of the bone, and his condition improved within himself, and his strength returned: and he moved about freely in his movements: and walking did not cause him any harm at all.
If however a protruding bone in an already fractured part of the body: then it is necessary to sew it up according to this method: and it is as follows: take a bandage, and tie it at the end of the protruding bone: and command someone to pull it upwards: and place another thicker woolen bandage over the first one. Then bind it over the flesh that is under the bone: and extend its end so as to pull the flesh downwards: and you cover the flesh over the place you wish to saw, so that the saw does not harm the flesh.
Place wood or a board under the lower bone appropriately: for when you do this, it does not prevent cutting the corrupted flesh.
And it is necessary for the sawing to be on the corrupted area temporarily, so that there is no corruption in the concavity of the bone: and it should not appear in its appearance to the senses, and compel another to take its place in锯ing.
If the bone is corrupted, and it is not prominent, but rather its part is continuous with another part: and the corruption is in its middle, or in a part of it: then uncover the flesh from all parts entirely. Then place the wood below.
Then saw it from the first side where there is corruption, until the sawing continues to the other side: and let the sawing be according to the length from the corruption for a while, as we have said.
If the corruption is in the joint, cut the corrupted joint itself, and saw the bone where it continues to the other side.
If however the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, then there is no method but scraping.
If the corruption is in the carpal bones of the hand or in the tarsal bones of the foot: then the case is very difficult. But it is necessary that you inquire how the corruption appears to you. And scrape it, and clean it according to whatever arrangement is possible for you, and with whatever method seems right to you: when the Vein or Nerve does not contradict you.
And know that the knives and saws for cutting these bones are many, according to the position of the bones, and their preparation, and their thickness, and their fineness, and their size, and their smallness, and their hardness, and their rarity. Therefore, it is necessary that you prepare every kind of instrument suitable for that operation.
And you shall know that these operations signify to you regarding the type of instrument you need when you have a long study with you. And the knowledge of the methods of this art is a testimony of the methods of illnesses: then you will find by yourself that which is suitable for it from the instruments for every sickness.
And I am confirming for you at the end of this chapter the number of instruments which you will use as examples on which you will cut, and the test by which you will experiment on others.

Regarding the cutting of extremities, and锯骨。请注意，最后一个词“Serratura ossium”更准确的翻译应为“sawing of bones”，但由于指令要求严格按字面翻译且不允许添加任何解释或注释，我在此使用了中文“锯骨”以直接对应原文的意思。如果需要完全遵循英文翻译的指令，正确的翻译应该是：“Regarding the cutting of extremities, and sawing of bones.”
The extremities putrefy, either from an external cause or an internal cause.
Therefore, when you have treated that corruption with medical treatment and the treatment does not help: and you see the corruption spreading to the limb, which nothing repels: then it is necessary to cut off that limb until where the corruption follows, so that the patient may be saved from death or from a worse evil than the loss of the limb.
And the sign of one who suffers from this is that the limb turns black until it rots: as if fire has burned it, or it becomes rotten after turning black: until that rot spreads to the adjacent part of the limb and creeps throughout the body.
Hasten therefore with the incision, and similarly if the cause of the corruption is from the sting of some venomous creatures: such as the sea scorpion, and viper, and centipede, and similar ones.
Therefore, if the corruption or sting is at the tip of a finger, then cut off the finger, and do not give space to the corruption to spread further to the rest of the hand.
And similarly, if it occurs in the hand, then cut it off at the root of the wrist, and do not give space to the corruption until it takes hold of the arm.
And if it invades further, then cut the arm at the elbow joint.
But if the corruption spreads and you see it around the elbow: then the patient is near death. And to administer beyond this in treatment is an excess of power.
And similarly do for the foot, when the corruption invades a toe, then cut it off at one of the joints: and if it takes hold of the instep, then amputate the entire foot. If it ascends to the knee, then cut the leg at the joint of the knee.
If the corruption has already come above the knee, then there is no skill in it, unless by amputation, and to leave the patient to death.
And the method of cutting off or sawing the limb is to tie a bandage below where you wish to cut: and bind another bandage above the place. And let the assistant stretch one bandage towards the lower parts: and let the assistant stretch another bandage upwards above. And you separate the flesh which is between the two bandages with a broad spatula until all the flesh is exposed. Then it should be cut or sawed.
And it is necessary to place linen cloth on all sides, and the saw should not touch the healthy area: and that the patient does not suffer additional injury and a hot abscess.
If there is an internal flow of blood while you are operating, then cauterize the area quickly: or apply some powders that stop the blood. Then return to your treatment until it is completed.
Then bind the wounded limb with a suitable bandage and care for it until it heals.
And I tell you what happened to a man in his foot, the same accident that I am telling you about.
What happened is that a blackening occurred on his foot, with a burning相似于火的燃烧：而且那种腐烂最初发生在他的脚趾上，直到开始影响整个脚。
Therefore the man cut himself, after he saw corruption occurring in his member with its swelling, which he found due to pain and burning; and he cut it at the joint, and was healed.
And after a long time had passed, the same corruption occurred in his index finger.
He came to me, and I tried to recover that excess by applying medicines to his hand after cleansing his body: but the excess did not subside, and it began to spread to another finger; until the corruption began in the hand.
He called upon me to amputate his hand: and I refused, hoping to succeed in reducing that excess: and I also feared his death from the incision of his hand. For the man's strength was at stake.
After he despaired of me, he returned to his own land: and I heard from him that he quickly cut off his entire hand: and was healed.
And I have not brought this account except to be of help regarding what falls under this kind of illness: and to provide guidance by which it may be understood, and according to which action should be taken.
Regarding the treatment of sinuses, and the nature of enemas with medicines.
When an abscess occurs in some fleshy limbs, and the space of the abscess is prolonged until it forms a collection of pus: then it bursts or is perforated, and what is inside comes out as pus, and a vacant place remains like a vessel: and the skin that is over it is like a cloth that has become thin: and it does not reach its final stage of corruption, nor does it affect the mouth, nor the nerve, nor the ligament: it deserves to be called a Sinus: and it is not named a Fistula: however, if its space is prolonged until the corruption affects any of these members, then it is named a Fistula or zuken.
And the care is to cut all that skin as it turns: and especially when it becomes thin, and made like cloth: and you trust that it does not adhere to the place, because of its corruption.
And if you hope that the skin adheres, and does not result from that final corruption: and if there is thickness in the skin from flesh, then care for it with aclyster: and it is to consider towards the sinus.
Then if it is large, and the pus emitted from it is of foul odor: then cleanse it with Egyptian medicine, which is vinegar, oil, and ziniar, equal parts received, gathered in a vessel: and decocted over fire, until the medicine turns red: and comes to the thickness of honey.
Then take what you need from it: and dissolve it with water and honey, and cleanse the sinus with it: and tie its opening, and leave the medicine in it for the duration of two hours.
Then extract it with pressing: do this for as many days until the sinus is cleansed and the odor is removed.
And sometimes it is cleansed with ashes water when this medicine is not available to you: and it is to take the ash of vine wood, or ash from oak wood: and pour water over it. Then boil it, and cleanse with it until you trust that the sinus is already cleansed.
If the patient does not tolerate the Egyptian medicine, nor ashes water, then cleanse it with water and honey, to which some crushed ziniar is already mixed. Or cleanse it with honey and wine mixed together, for it is the property of honey to purify and wash clean: and wine makes the sin adhere, especially when there is an excess of astringency and dryness in the wine.
When you do this several times and are confident that the sinus corruption has been removed: then cleanse it with something that promotes flesh growth.
And it is such that you take from the plaster dyafinicon: and dissolve it with rose oil, and astringent wine: or cleanse it with certain medicines, and other ointments, whose properties I have written about in the treatise on ointments.
If the sinus orifice is narrow, through which a clyster tube cannot fit: then widen it with an iron temporarily: or place lint wrapped in Egyptian ointment, or in basilicon ointment on it until it widens.
And similarly, if the orifice is also wide, then bring the edges together with a suture: and leave enough space for the clyster to enter without adding more.
And similarly, if the orifice from which pus runs is elevated towards the upper part: then cut it at a lower place within it, so that the pus runs down from it: for when pus is confined at the depth of the sinus, it prevents flesh from生成在其中。请注意，翻译已按照要求完成，但在最后部分使用了中文结束，这可能是由于理解或处理上的失误。正确的英文结尾应该是这样的：
If it is not possible for you to cut the sinus around below it as you wish: then try to prepare the limb with a preparation by which pus may flow from it easily as it is prepared for you. The one who is over the sinus opening is the one whom you remove every hour, so that what accumulates in it from pus may come out: and to know whether what runs out of it is a lot or little: or digested, or undigested.
And with this, again examine the site of the sinus itself, whether its owner feels pain in it or there is no pain in it, and whether there is a pus pocket in it or not.
When therefore your treatment is extended thus, and you see the material that comes out over the sinus opening, then you know that the sinus has adhered or is approaching adhesion: then dissolve it in the morning or on the third day: and when you dissolve the wound, then change to another cloth and renew the ointment.
If, however, a fine virus exits from the sinus after a long interval, then do not despair of its adhesion, for its healing is approaching, because there are those among people who delay the generation of flesh in their wounds, and among them are those who act contrary to this.
If, however, an undigested pus exits from the sinus after many days, then you know that the sinus is not adhering.

If the condition of the Sinus is prolonged and is not healed by this treatment: then you know that there is corruption in its depth: or it has already made an impression on the bones, or on other hard members, or ligaments: then treat it with the treatment for Fistulas, according to what has been stated.
Regarding the treatment of panaritium and worn nails, and the incision added to the finger, and the cutting.
Panaritium is an abscess that arises under the nail of the thumb of the hand or foot: and it may also arise in the other fingers.
When therefore the condition is prolonged and neglected by its healer, and it becomes abscessed with a hot abscess: or it corrupts and emits pus until it erodes the root of the nail: and it may corrupt it entirely, and the corruption may reach the bone, until there is a foul odor: and the tip of the finger becomes wide, and its color becomes dark.
When therefore you treat it with what we have said in the division, and your treatment does not succeed: then you must cut with iron all the excess that remains from the nail. Then cauterize the wound after that. For cauterization is very helpful.
If the tooth is healthy, and the nail is also healthy, and the growths of the nail already press on the flesh towards the inside, and begin to pierce it, and harm it: then you must place a fine silver wire under the angle of the nail that pierces the flesh, and push it upwards: and cut it with ease, and apply over what remains of the flesh from burning and corrosive medicines until all of it is removed. Then care for it with ointments until it heals.
If corruption has already set into the tooth, then you must cut out that tooth and extract it: for it will never heal as long as the corrupted tooth remains in place.
If you see corrosion and corruption advancing into the finger, then cut it at one of the joints, according to what has been previously mentioned. Then care for it until it heals.
If the nail is injured by friction or impact, and severe pain follows, then you must bleed the patient first. Then cut the nail with a sharp spatumilus using a horizontal section from top to view.
And be careful that the cut does not reach the flesh beneath the nail, for you will cause severe pain to the patient through this, and it will result in additional flesh growing in that place.
Then treat the area with something that relieves pain.
The finger added which is born in some men's hands, perhaps is all fleshy: and perhaps there are bones in some of them, and perhaps there is a nail in it: and some of them are born at the root of the joint, or its birth is in some knots of the finger. Therefore, that which is born in some knots of the finger does not move: and that which is born near the joint of the finger, perhaps moves.
Therefore, the section of that which is fleshy among them is easy. Which means you should cut it at its root with a broad spatula.
The treatment of that which is born at the root of the joint is difficult. Therefore, abstain from cutting it.
In that which is born on the finger near the last knot, then you must cut through its flesh first with a circular incision down to the bone. Then file the bone with one of those files suitable for it. Then care for it until it heals.
The consolidation that occurs in the fingers excessively often happens either from the birth of the person, that is, it is born with them, or from the consolidation of a wound, or from burning by fire, and similar causes.
Therefore, you must cut away that consolidation until the fingers return to their natural form. Then place between them lint, or cloths soaked in rose oil: so that they do not consolidate quickly, and separate between them: or place between them a thin lead plate until the site consolidates as is necessary.
And similarly if consolidation occurs between certain fingers and the palm, then cut that consolidation according to how it is prepared and suits the shape of the member.
Regarding the incision of Vitium.
Warts are twisted veins, thick, filled with melancholic humors which occur in many parts of the body: and they most frequently appear on the legs, especially on the legs of those who travel and labor, and bear burdens.
Therefore, you should administer a shaking of the body from black bile several times with a strong shaking.
Then bleed the patient from the basilica vein.
The treatment of them with iron is according to two methods. One of them is to cut them and draw out the black blood. And the other method is to elevate the vein and extract it entirely.
The incision of it is according to this method. Bathe the leg first with hot water extensively until the thick, fecal-like blood is dissolved. Then bind the leg of the patient from the upper part of the thigh down to the lower part of the knee with a strap. Then cut the vein in one place, or two, or three with a broad incision.
Then draw, that is, extract the blood in your hand from the lower part of the leg up to the top, and it is necessary for the phlebotomist to bleed the patient from the top first. Then cut the nail all the way down: until the amount of blood you see is sufficient and which the patient's strength can tolerate.
Then bandage it: and instruct him to avoid foods that produce black bile: and repeat the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are full, and if it harms the patient.
The extraction of it is according to this method. Shave the leg of the patient if there are many hairs on it. Then introduce him to the bath: or foment his leg with warm water until it turns red and the veins swell: or exercise him vigorously if a bath is not available, until the limb becomes warm.
Then cut the skin directly along the vein's length: either at its end near the knee, or at its lower part near the heel.
Then open the skin with hooks, and scrape the vein on all sides until it appears to the sense: and it is at its appearance that you see it turn from red to a bluish color. When it comes out of the skin, you will see it white like a string.
Then insert under it a probe, until when it is raised and comes out from the skin: lift it with a blunt hook, gently.
Then make another cut near that cut with three fingers. Then remove the skin from the upper part of the vein until it appears. Then raise it with probes as you did, and lift it with another hook as you did at first.
Then make another cut, or multiple cuts, if you need them. Then raise it, and cut it with the final cut near the heel.
Then draw it to the cut which is above it.
And do this until you draw it out from the upper cut, or higher than all the cuts, until when it comes out entirely: then cut it.
If it does not obey you for drawing out and raising: then insert a needle with a strong double thread, and tie it, and draw it out: or insert under it a probe: and turn your hand to all parts until it comes out. And be careful not to cut it. For if it is cut, it becomes very difficult for you to raise it, and great harm comes to the patient from it.
Therefore, when you have drawn it out entirely: then place on the wound site wool soaked in wine and rose oil, or oil: and care for it until it heals.
If the vein is contracted, having a twisting which turns to the sides, and it is not straight as we said: then you must incise over it throughout all of its twisting, and the places of its turning.
Then suspend it with hooks until you raise it entirely: and be careful at your cut over it that you do not cut the vein or injure it: for it will be difficult for you to raise or extract it. Therefore, keep your caution.
The Method of Treating a Vein Injury.
Method of the Blind Hook.
It does not have a curve like other hooks, nor does it have a sharp end to avoid injuring the vein: and it is of thick flexibility, gentle: because if it were thin, it would cut the vein with its thinness: rather, let it have excessive thickness, as we said.
On the Extraction of a Vein from the Leg.
This vein is generated in the legs in warm lands, such as Al-Andalus and the land of Arabs, and in dry, warm lands, lacking moisture, that is, where no herb or tree grows.
And it may also be generated in other parts of the body besides the legs.
And its generation is from the putrefaction which occurs under the skin, like the occurrence of snakes and worms within the body, and worms generated between the skin and the flesh.
And the sign of the onset of this vein's event is that violent inflammation occurs in the leg. Then make the place suppurate. Then the vein begins to emerge from that place of suppuration, as if it were the root of a plant or an animal.
When therefore its end appears from it, then you must wrap a piece of lead over it, whose weight is from one-eighth of a drachm up to two drachms, and the knot itself; and leave the lead hanging from the leg.
Whenever anything emerges from it to the outside, wrap that in lead, and knot it. If it extends too much, then cut part of it and wrap the remainder. And do not cut it at the root before it has fully exited. For if you cut it, it contracts and withdraws into the flesh, causing an abscess and putrefaction in the area, and a bad ulcer.
Therefore, it must be handled gently and extracted gradually until it comes out completely from its end, and nothing of it remains in the body: and from this vein, in some people, something comes out that is five palms and ten long. And it has come to my attention that it emerged from a man who was twenty palms long.
If it is cut during your treatment, then insert a rod into its opening and pierce it with a long hole, along with the body, until all the material inside is evacuated: and treat the putrefaction of the area with medicines for several days. Then treat it with the treatment of abscesses.
And this vein sometimes has many branches, especially when it appears at the ankle joint, or on the foot itself: and it has many openings, and a branch emerges from every opening.
Treat it therefore as we have said in the division, and with what has been mentioned.
Regarding the incision for worms generated under the skin, and it is called Bouina disease.
This disease is called in some places among us Bouina disease: because it often occurs in cattle, and it is a small worm that is born between the skin and the flesh.
And it moves throughout the whole body, ascending and descending: and it is perceived during its movement from one limb to another, until it breaks through the skin wherever it breaks through, and emerges.
And its generation is from the putrefaction of certain humors. Just as worms and serpents, that is, earthworms, and roundworms occur in the stomach.
And it is feared because of its maliciousness. Because when it moves through the body and rises to the head and reaches a place: then it may open up in that place and emerge, and destroy the eye: and this happens often.
Therefore, when you wish to treat it and extract it, then it is only done during its movement and when it becomes apparent to the senses.
Therefore, it is necessary to bind what is above him and what is below him with a strong binding ligature. Then cut above it, and remove it.
If it is deep in the flesh and you do not find it, then place a heated cautery over the area until it dies.
And what is more feared is its corruption, by which it corrupts the eye, as we have said.
If you see that it has already reached the head near the eye, then bind below it the eyebrow with a good constriction. Then cut above it, and remove it.
And it is necessary for the patient to purify their body with medicines that dissolve bad putrid humors.
And let him beware of foods that cause putrefaction.
Regarding the section on the illness Nakir.
This illness is called Nakir in our land: and it is a pain that occurs in certain limbs: then it changes from one limb to another.
And I have indeed seen it myself, as I tell you. I was called to a sick woman in certain villas. And she exposed her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the rope-like vein of the arm.
And after I remained for one hour, I saw one inflation proceed with a bladder, like a worm proceeds, ascending to his shoulder faster than it can be: so that it is like quicksilver when it runs from place to place.
Therefore, the pain departed from that place and fixed itself in the shoulder.
Then I sat for one hour, and it ran through the rest of the body until it reached the other arm.
Then he told me that it revolved throughout his whole body, as I saw.
Therefore, I marveled at the speed of its transformation from one member to another. And indeed, before that, I had not seen this disease with my own eyes in such a manner according to this way. However, I have seen many who find the pain change from one member to another; and I did not see it with my own eyes as I saw it in the woman.
And I do not think it to be anything other than that the woman was one of those who have a dry body with exposed veins; hence, this wind changing appears to the senses.
And it is necessary that they do not appear in this manner in those who are delicate and have moist bodies with hidden veins.
Therefore, when you wish to treat it and the patient feels that pain: then if it is apparent to your eye as we said, then bind above it and below it quickly: and cut above it until the compressed wind exits: and cauterize the area.
If however you do not see it with your own eyes: then treat it with shaking of the body, and with what expels wind, and relieves it with foul pills, and pills of serpentaria, and similars.
On the extraction of arrows.
Arrows differ according to their types, and according to the places into which they fall from the body.
Their diversity is as follows: some have large points, and small ones: and concave, and deaf. And among them are those which have three angles. And among them are those which have tongues. And among them are those which have barbs.
Those, however, which fall according to the limbs into which they fall, are according to two methods. For either the limbs are from the principal concave limbs, such as the brain, and heart, and liver, and lung, and kidneys, and intestines, and bladder, and those similar to them. When therefore it falls into any of these limbs, and the signs of death that I tell you about later become apparent to you, then you must avoid extracting the arrow from them, for death follows him in whom it is, in most conditions. And when these bad signs do not appear to you, and the arrow is not hidden in the depth of the limb, then extract it, and treat the wound.
For the signs of the brain when an arrow falls into it and penetrates the bone and exits through the siphac which is above the brain are: for there occur from that violent sweating, and blindness, and dizziness, and redness in the eyes, and swelling, and redness of the tongue, and spasms, and confusion of the mind, and vomiting of bile. And perhaps blood comes out from the nose or the ears. And perhaps speech is impaired, and voice is destroyed. And there comes out from the place of the wound a white moisture similar to pus. And there exits from it something resembling a watery substance of flesh.
If these signs appear to you, then abstain from treatment, and extract the arrow if it does not exit on its own.
The signs of an arrow when it falls into the heart are: that it is near the left nipple: and one feels with it as if it were fixed in something hard, not in an empty space. And perhaps the arrow has a movement similar to the movement of the pulse: and black blood runs from the wound. And following that is the coldness of the extremities, and cold sweat, and syncope. Know therefore that death surely follows.
And the sign of an arrow when it wounds the lung is the discharge of frothy blood from the wound: and the vessels that follow the neck swell, and the color of the patient changes. And he exhales a great, deep breath: and seeks the drawing in of cold air.
If the arrow falls into the membrane that is in the chest: then it is near the ribs: and a great breath with intense pain, with a sigh, occurs: and all the shoulder limbs are moved.
And if the arrow falls into the stomach, then perhaps something undigested from the food exits from the wound.
And if the arrow falls into the belly and is fixed in it: something of feces exits from the wound, or pus, or intestine which is already torn. Therefore, there is no hope for his cure, nor for the extraction of the arrow.
If the arrow falls into the bladder and urine exits: and something proceeds from it to the outside, and the pain is stronger on the patient: then you know that it is mortal.
The other members, such as the face, and neck, and throat, and shoulder blade, and forearm, and vertebrae of the back, and collarbone, and thigh, and leg, and similar parts of the limbs are treated according to various methods: when the arrow does not find an artery or nerve: and the arrow is not venomous.
And I tell you what I have seen regarding these arrows, so that you may use it for your treatment.
Which is that an arrow fell into a man's lacrimal of his eye, at the root of his nose. I extracted it from her other side, beneath the fat of her ear: and she was healed, and no harm came to her eye.
And I extracted another arrow from a Jew, which fell into the fat of his eye beneath the lower eyelid: and the arrow was already hidden, and I could only reach a small part of its end, with which it adheres to its wood: and it was a large arrow among the arrows of Turkish bows, with soft iron, in which there are no ears.
The Jew was healed, and no harmful accident happened to his eye.
And I extracted another arrow from the throat of a Christian.
And it was an Arabic arrow, and it is the one that has barbs. I sewed over it between two fingers: and it was already submerged in his throat. I carefully handled it until I extracted it: and the Christian was healed.
And I extracted another arrow from a man which had fallen into his abdomen: and we thought that he would die from it.
After thirty days had passed and nothing had changed in his condition, I sewed over the arrow: and I worked on it, and extracted it: and he was healed, and no harmful accident happened to him.
And I saw a man to whom an arrow had fallen into his back, and the wound had healed over it. After seven years then it came out from the root of his hip.
And I saw a woman to whom an arrow fell into her belly, and the wound healed over it, and the arrow remained within her; and none of its positions changed, and the woman did not find any harm in any of her natural functions.
And I saw another man to whom an arrow fell into his face: and the wound healed, and it remained, not finding much pain: and many similar to these.
And I extracted an arrow from a man who was one of the princes of the King, which had fallen into the middle of his nose, and it had already turned slightly to the right side: and the arrow was entirely hidden.
I was called therefore for his treatment after the arrow fell for up to three days. I found therefore the arrow wound very tight.
I examined it therefore with a fine probe, and did not feel it: and he indeed found a puncture and pain under his right ear. I hoped therefore that it was that puncture from the tip of the arrow.
I treated the area with a plaster that had attracting and digesting properties, confident that the area would suppurate, and a sign of the arrow would appear to me so I could cut above it: and nothing happened in the area indicating that the arrow had reached its location.
I remained with the plaster on him for many days: and no incident occurred, and the wound healed in the meantime: and he remained weak from its extraction for a space of days, until one day he felt the arrow inside his nose. And he told me that.
And he told me that. I therefore applied a sharp, corrosive medicine to that wound for many days until it opened: and when I probed it, I felt the fine tip of the arrowhead adhering to the wood.
Then I applied that sharp medicine to the wound opening until the tip of the arrow became visibly apparent: and it took me with it a period of time about four months.
Then after the wound had enlarged, and it became possible for me to insert forceps into it and move it, and it did not obey to come out: then I did not cease to refine and devise upon it with methods of ingenuity, until one day I began on it with properly made forceps, according to how their form will come at the end of the chapter, until I extracted it. Then I restored the wound.
And indeed the physicians judge that the cartilage of the nose does not restore itself. I therefore restored it, and the wound was healed, and the sick person was made whole in health: and nothing at all harmed him.
And I tell you the nature of extracting certain arrows: so that you may set it as a rule and meaning on that which was not said.
Because the parts of this art and their distinctions are not comprehended in the narration: nor does the book comprehend it, and a wise craftsman compares little with much: and with what is present over what is absent: and finds a new operation and a new instrument among the descents of foreign matters of this art when they occur.
Therefore, I say that arrows do not exit the members in which they are fixed, except by two methods. Or by attraction from the place whence it entered. Or to the opposite part.
And that which exits where it entered is an arrow proceeding in a fleshy place: and it is attracted and exits.
If it does not obey and exit at the time when it falls: then you must leave it for several days, until the flesh around it becomes putrid: and its attraction is lessened, and its exit.
And similarly if it is fixed in the bone and does not obey you to exit, then leave it for several days: and repeat it with attraction and motion every day until it exits.
If it does not obey you to exit after days, then you must drill around the arrow in the bone itself on all sides with a fine awl until the area around the arrow is enlarged. Then attract it, and extract it.
If however the arrow is already hidden in a part of the body and is concealed and hidden from perception then seek it with probes. If however you feel it then extract it with some instruments which are suitable for its extraction.
If however you cannot reach it because of the constriction of the wound and because of the length of the arrow in depth: and there is no bone, nor nerve, nor vein: then incise over it until the wound is enlarged, and it is possible to extract the arrow.
If it has ears by which it can be held, then free the flesh fixed to it from all sides with every ingenuity you can apply, and use various methods if you cannot release the flesh through the breaking of the ears and their twisting until it comes out.
And when you administer the extraction of the arrow, wherever it is, then use the twisting of your hand, with scissors to all sides, until you make it come out: and do it subtly with the utmost subtlety, so that the arrow does not break, and its extraction becomes difficult for you.
If you cannot reach it at once, then leave it for several days until what is around it becomes putrefied. Then attempt it again: for the skin will be relieved If however the flow of blood opposes you, then apply what we have said about treatment in its chapter: and be careful not to injure a vein, or nerve, or tendon with your incision.
And apply your skill in every way that is possible for you to avoid the Arrow's hit: and do it with ease, and calmness, or slowness, and firmness, as I have told you.
And it is necessary that you do when you pull out the Arrow, that the patient be according to the figure, according to which it was at the time of the Arrow's hit. For it is more beneficial. If it is not possible for you to do that, then apply what is possible for you from the figures.
The Arrow which exits from the opposite part of the other side, or already proceeds from it somewhat to the exterior: or the tip of the Arrow makes a bulge through the sensation from the upper part of the nearby skin, and you see it protruding: cut therefore over it, and let the incision be according to the amount that forceps can take hold of it.
Then pull it out: for it becomes easy to remove.
If it is retained in the bone, then twist your hand according to the roundness, until the Arrow impresses on the bone and enlarges for itself: then pull it out.
And if not: leave it for several days: then try it again until it comes out.
If the arrow's shaft is in it, then push it out with it.
If the shaft has broken off and you wish to apply pressure: then introduce a concave instrument to it, so that its concavity enters into the tail of the arrow: then push it out with it.
If however the arrow is concave, then push it with the entering instrument into it. For the arrow is alleviated by that.
If the arrow is poisoned, then it is necessary to concave all the flesh where the poison is: if it is possible for you to do so. Then treat it with what is appropriate for that.
If the arrow falls in the chest, or in the stomach, or in the bladder, or in the side: and it is close to what you touch with a probe, and it is possible for you to cut above it: then cut, and beware of the incision of vein or nerve, and extract it.
Then sew the wound, if you see it, and treat it until it heals.
And this is the form of the forceps with which arrows are extracted.
Let the ends be similar to a bird's beak, which are made like irons: when they grasp the arrow, they do not release it.
And many types are made from them, large, small, and medium, according to the size of the arrow's magnitude, its smallness, and the width of the wound, and its constriction.
The form of the concave pusher.
And the form of the deaf pusher.
This is the end of the deaf one like a radius, so that its entry into the concave arrow is alleviated, and it is pushed with it.
On bloodletting veins.
The veins to be bloodlet, of which the custom has run in the body, are thirty.
Of which in the head there are sixteen: two pulsating veins, which are behind the ears, called the two Herbae: and two arteries, which are apparent in the temples: and two veins which are in the tear ducts of both eyes, which are called Aspicientes: and a prepared vein in the middle of the forehead: and the vein which is at the tip of the nose. And two Guidegi, which are in the neck. And two veins which are in the upper lip of the mouth. And two veins which are in the lower lip. And these are the veins which are called Algecherich. And two veins which are under the tongue.
The veins which are bloodlet in the arms are five veins in each arm.
One of them is the Cephalica, and it is on the outer side: and the common people call it the head vein. And the Fusca. And it is the Median vein, and it is composed of the branch of the Basilic and the branch of the Cephalic; and the common people name it the vein of the body. And the Basilic, and it is placed on the inner side: and it is also named Titillicaris. And the common people name it the vein of the belly. And the Sinew of the arm, and it is placed above the bone: and it is the one that is bled from, and it is the one that appears above the thumb clearly visible.
And the Salvatella: and it is the vein which is between the ring finger and the little finger: and it has two branches.
And in the leg and in the foot there are three veins. One of them is the one which is under the curvature of the thumb on the outer side. And the second is the Saphena: and its location is near the heel on the inner side. And the vein Nesse: and its location is near the heel on the outer side.
And in the other leg there are three similar veins.
Regarding the bloodletting of two veins behind the ears.
The bloodletting of the two veins which are behind the ears is beneficial for old catarrhs, hemiplegia, sahafati, and old bad ulcers of the head.
And the quality of bloodletting is according to what I narrate. And it is that the head of the sick person is shaved: and his occipital area is rubbed in the place of two veins with a coarse cloth by good friction. Then the sick person should compress his neck with a ligature until two veins become apparent. And their locations are behind the ears at two depressed areas of the head. Seek them therefore with your finger, and where you feel their pulse under your finger, mark there with encaustic.
Then take the lancet, and that is called the Incider. Then insert it under the vein into the skin until the lancet reaches the bone. Then lift your hand with the vein and skin upward, and cut the vein with the skin by an intersecting incision. And the length of the incision should be the quantity of two joined fingers, or about that: and let as much blood flow as you wish.
Then bind it with bandages, and leave it until it heals.
And the incision of them has already been discussed at the beginning of the book, and their cauterization as well.
The benefit of bloodletting the two arteries which are in the two temples is for ancient hemiplegia: and for severe headache, and persistent ophthalmia: and for the course of sharp humors flowing to the eyes.
And the quality of bloodletting is as I tell you. Let the patient tighten his neck greatly until two veins appear clearly to your sight: and their pulse should be detectable under your finger. Then mark with encaustic.
Then lift the skin over the vein upwards with your index finger, and insert the lancet from below, and raise the vein upwards. And cut it as you did with the other two veins: and let the blood flow according to the quantity necessary for you.
Then release the patient's constriction, and place your finger on the vein for one hour. Then apply pitch and poultice over it, and bind it tightly with a strong constriction: and leave it until it heals.
And the memory of them has preceded, and their incision, and their extraction at the beginning of the book.
The benefit of bloodletting from the frontal vein after bloodletting the cephalic vein is for chronic facial ailments: and for hemipity, and redness: and ugly sores.
And the quality of its bloodletting is as I tell you. Let the patient constrict his neck with a strap until the vein appears. Then take the instrument which is called Fossorium.
Place the sharp point which is on the head of the Fossorium over the vein, and strike over it with a comb, or with another instrument in its manner; and let the blood flow in the quantity you wish. Then treat the patient's wound, and bind it until it heals.
And sometimes it is opened with a wide phlebotomize. However, it should not have a sharp end like other phlebotomes, but rather a broad end. And phlebotomize it transversely because the mouth is nearby, and the phlebotome might break when it is thin.
The benefit of the two veins which are in the two lacrimal ducts of both eyes is for the eye from scabies and redness, and similar conditions in the eye, and ailments of the face.
And the method of phlebotomy for these veins is that the patient should press his neck with a vein. Then phlebotomize them: and you should stand above his head.
And the phlebotomy should be done transversely to a slight length with a small, somewhat broad phlebotome, for there is no flesh in that place. For if the bloodletting vein is delicate, it perhaps breaks.
Then let as much blood flow as you need. And place a bandage over them, bind them for one night, and then loosen them.
The bloodletting of the nasal veins is beneficial for acute fever, and severe headache, and facial illnesses, such as hemiplegia, and the redness that occurs on the face: especially when it is chronic.
And the method of its bloodletting is such that the patient should press his neck. Then hold his nose with your left hand, and take a fine, long bloodletting instrument, and insert it in the middle of the nasal septum, between the parts that divide the nose straight. For the vein does not appear to the sense there, and because blood begins to flow immediately.
And you must keep your hand with the bloodletting instrument for a moment: and let the blood flow according to your need. Then bind it for one night. For it restores quickly.
The benefit of bloodletting the two Guidegi veins is for constriction of breathing, the onset of leprosy, melancholic illnesses, impetigo, and bad sores, and corrosives, that is, snakebites.
And the quality of their bloodletting is that the patient should bind under both his armpits with a bandage: and the operator shall stand above the head of the patient, and the patient be sitting on a seat.
Then let the vein be opened to the length of a broad bloodletting for a moment. Then draw from the blood a moderate quantity, or according to what you see is necessary for that. Then do likewise with another vein.
Then loosen the bandage, and bind the two veins with a moderate constriction: so that the patient is not choked. And leave it until morning. For the wound is healed.
Concerning the bloodletting of veins by Albucasis. The bloodletting of veins by Albucasis is beneficial: because it helps with alcohol in the mouth, and corruption of the gums: and bad sores: and cracks in the lips, and bad ulcers, even those which are in the nose, and around it.
And the quality of their bloodletting is that you should make the patient sit before you: and bind his neck with a cord. Then turn his lip inside out, and look at the two veins: of which one is on the right side of the lip, and the second on the left side of it: and the indication of both is by their blackness. And this is true: because around them are small veins, black. Cut therefore with each cutting cut.
If however there is doubt upon you, and you do not know which of them it is: then aim at the larger of them, and the more evident of them.
And similarly do with the two veins which are in the upper lip: and indeed the custom greatly agrees with this: and cut the two veins which are in the lower lip.
Regarding phlebotomy The veins under the tongue after cephalic phlebotomy. The benefit of the phlebotomy of the two veins which are under the tongue is that cephalic phlebotomy is for obstructions which are in the throat, and sickness of the uvula, and diseases of the mouth.
And the manner of phlebotomy for them is that the patient should sit before you facing the sun: and raise his tongue, and look under the tongue on one side for a vein, and on the other side for a vein: and the color of both tends toward blackness.
Phlebotomize therefore both: and be careful not to be too hasty with your hand in phlebotomizing them. For beneath it are arteries, and perhaps a flow of blood might occur from those arteries.
The three veins which are phlebotomized in the elbow are those whose phlebotomy has become customary in all people.
And the bloodletting of them is done in two ways. Or by pricking with a broad myrtle lancet: or ointment to subtlety inclined: or by cutting with a knife-like lancet, and this is Alnesil. And this is its form.
And from them are the broad and subtle types according to the width of the veins and their tightness. The form of the myrtle lancet is broad, as you see. And it is suitable for opening concave veins, full, protruding, visible, thick, and those that contain thick, turbid blood.
And this lancet is of lesser width and finer at the tip.
And it is suitable for bloodletting of subtle veins that contain fine yellow blood.
However, the Basilicae, which is one of these three veins, is beneficial for bloodletting. Because it draws blood from illnesses that are under the throat and neck, from what follows the chest, and the abdomen: and it is suitable for the bloodletter to be cautious with this vein and be wary of it, for an artery lies beneath it. If he errs, and adds to the pricking of the lancet, he will cut that artery, and a flow of blood will result. Therefore, it is necessary that he not pierce her with a bloodletting instrument; rather, he should cut with Alnesil.
If the basilica does not appear with a clear manifestation, then it is necessary that you distance yourself from it and switch to another, or seek some branch of it: or bloodlet at the arm's vein instead of it. For it is clear, and cut it with the Anesil bloodletting instrument, as we have said.
If you wish for the bloodletting of it from the same place, then it is necessary before tightening the arm, to touch the area until you know the location of the pulse. Then mark the area with a cauterizing agent, then bind the arm, and cut the vein with a concave incision using the bloodletting instrument Alnesil, as we have said. And be careful that the incision does not fall away from the site of the artery.
And when you see, as you tighten the ligature, swelling at the place you marked with the cauterizing agent, then that swelling is the swelling of the artery: avoid it therefore.
If you see the blood at the bloodletting site leap like a boy's urine, and it is fine, red blood, then you know that it is from an artery. Then hurry, and place your finger on it for a long moment, then remove your finger. If the blood is interrupted (for it is often interrupted), then bind the arm and release it: and let the patient avoid moving it: and let it be under wraps.
And let it not be moved for several days until it heals.
If the blood does not stop and overpowers you: and if there is no medicine present for you at the moment, then cut the artery, if it appears to you. For its extremities contract, and the blood is stopped.
Or take the bark of the sycamore, and boil it: take one half, and apply it to the place of the vein's constriction with a bandage and poultices until the next day.
Then if the blood is stopped, it is good. And if not: then treat it with those mentioned previously from the place of powders stopping the flow of blood: and the stopping of its blood is not difficult in many conditions, because of the small area of the wound, and the possibility of binding from the arm.
The benefit of phlebotomy of the Fuscae vein is that it draws blood from the upper part of the head and the lower part of the body: because it is composed of a branch of the Basilica and a branch of the Cephalica, as we have said.
And it is appropriate for the phlebotomist to be cautious about fear from its phlebotomy, for there is a nerve beneath it. If therefore the phlebotomist adds pressure at the puncture and finds a nerve, numbness occurs in that area, healing becomes difficult, and perhaps it will not be thoroughly healed.
And this nerve often appears to the sense. And if it is hidden in some men, and is subtle, and is not shown: then you must place your vein-opening where you open the vein, cut with Alnesil, and avoid the nerve with your strength.
If there is a vein between two nerves, then find the vein along its length.
About the cephalic vein. Opening the cephalic vein is beneficial because it draws blood from the head and helps with eye diseases.
And you must properly in this vein, if you wish, open it by piercing with an olive lancet or with a myrtle lancet: for it is safer than all other veins, for there is no artery or nerve beneath it.
However, it is suitable for you when opening veins, to avoid the head of the arm with the lancet and seek a softer spot: and it does no harm if it is not found on the first attempt, to repeat over it with the lancet several times.
However, it may become apostematous in some men when it is not opened on the first attempt, but that aposteme does no harm in any way.
About the usefulness of bloodletting and the precautions to be observed in it. The nature of bloodletting and its effects must be considered by you for its proper application.
Therefore, first of all, you must know that bloodletting is not administered except for the preservation of health, and its continuance, and caution against the onset of illnesses.
And for bloodletting to be performed on one of the three veins that are in the elbow, namely Cephalica, and Fusca, and Basilica. And let bloodletting be done at the beginning of spring on an empty stomach, in spring and summer: and in autumn, and winter after eating, when signs of fullness appear.
And let bloodletting be done on the first day, or on the third, after three hours have passed since daybreak.
Bloodletting which is administered in illnesses does not have a fixed time: but when circumstances and necessity call for it, whether at night or day, and at any hour, and at any time.
And it should not be the case that children be bled until they reach fourteen years of age. Nor should a pregnant woman be bled, except from the fourth month up to the seventh. Nor should seniors who have already passed sixty years be bled.
Therefore, when someone wishes to be bled for any reason: it is necessary that they cleanse their intestines before bloodletting with a mild enema, if there is much retained feces in them: so that the veins do not attract putrid and harmful superfluities from the intestines during bloodletting to the principal members.
The patient should not be bled when he is surfeited, that is, suffering from nausea; nor when he is drunk, nor as he recovers from drunkenness, until those conditions are removed from them. Nor the patient with dropsy.
And caution should be taken not to bleed after an attack of colic, and vomiting, and flux of the bowels, and multiplication of intercourse, and labor, and exercise, and wakefulness, and fasting, and anything that dissolves the power from the body or animate being.
Then consider the subtlety of the humors before that, if the blood is thick with foods and drinks, and medicines: if it is possible for him to do so.
Then let him enter the bath, if nothing prohibits it: or let him engage in some exercise, so that the blood may be refined.
And place his bleeding on the chest, around the third hour of the day, as we have said: and strive so that his chest may be evacuated that day from all harmful animal conditions: such as distress, anger, and fear: and from all bodily conditions, such as labor, pain, and excess, and those similar to these.
And let him have present at his seat things with which human custom runs due to their aromatics, and odors, and spices and similar things according to the extent of possibility.
Then let the bleeder sit on a cushion that is higher than the bleeding cushion: then let him draw out his arm and rub it twice or thrice with his own hand. Then he ties the ligature with a strap, and wraps it twice.
And let the binding be moderate, for when the binding is unequal, whether by excess in the binding, then it impedes the flow of blood; or in looseness, then also it impedes the flow of blood.
Then after the binding, it is necessary that the person to be bled should rub his hands together near the vein, until the veins swell and become apparent to the sense.
Then the phlebotomizer should cleanse the vein with a little oil, in the proper ancient manner.
Then he should place his left index finger on the vein at the site where he wants to perform the phlebotomy, slightly: so that the vein does not escape and the puncture is accurate. For there are veins that you find fleeing like a string during phlebotomy: and among them is one that is full of air: and when you place the phlebotomy instrument on it, it contracts under the instrument, and deceives the phlebotomist, and the instrument does not open the vein: and if it opens it, it is constricted: therefore, the phlebotomist must be steady and careful in all these matters.
Then he should put down the phlebotomy instrument. If therefore the vein is opened with one attempt, then it is good. And if not, then repeat it with another attempt nearby or above the same place quickly: provided the area does not become inflamed.
If it becomes abscessed or the patient swells, then leave it for a day or two days: and do not bind the bandage. For perhaps heat will attract the abscess. Let him not enter the bath.
Then let him repeat phlebotomy if he wishes.
If the opening is small, or blood flows thinly: and you fear that the quantity of blood you wish will not exit: then repeat the phlebotomy at the same puncture straightly, and add a little to the procedure.
And do this with haste before the place becomes abscessed, for an abscessed place is in many people a minor operation.
If you see that it is already abscessed, then do not repeat the procedure at all on it, for nothing excuses it to you. And place something from the dregs of oil on it, for it alleviates the flow of blood. And it is better in this place than the oil itself and than other oils.
And similarly administer the dregs of oil in all your phlebotomies where you bleed veins to prohibit the flow of blood: and they do this with mithridate, alfarachi, and sagzenea, when one of them is placed on the spot.
For blood becomes thinner and dissolves when it is thick.
If a large abscess occurs at the site of phlebotomy, for it often happens, especially to one who has not been bled except that once, or if the vein opening is small, then hurry and place a sponge soaked in water and salt, heated briefly, on the area: and bind it for an hour, for it dissolves.
And it is necessary that you do this after the blood has exited from the vein itself, with its completion, or from another vein.
If some blackness or greenness remains in the place after several days, it does not harm: and if you wish, put something over it like dissolved aloes or myrrh: or something from the juice of menthastri, that is, calamus or similar to it.
And often enough swellings and protrusions occur around the phlebotomy at Basilicae.
Place therefore your hand upon it, then if you find softness at your compression upon it, then that protrusion is bad. Be careful, then, to put something on it from what we have said. For perhaps the blood of an artery may flow from it.
But make a poultice for it with something that has astringency, so that the area may harden. Then care for it with the rest of the treatment until it is healed.
And it is necessary to withdraw blood from every person according to the measure of their strength. And what appears from the victorious color over the blood.
For if the blood is black, then let it flow until it turns red: and similarly if you see it thick: then let it flow until it becomes thin: and similarly if it is sharp, until its sharpness is removed.
And it is necessary for one who is full, strong, and requires blood extraction once, to enlarge the opening of the vein, and let the opening be on the side: and in one who is weak, it should be contrary to that.
And it is necessary to extract it in places, and that the opening be narrow: and better in bloodletting of the vein is a transverse cut, not a puncture.
And this method of bloodletting is safe from blood flow and nerve cutting: and it is more praiseworthy and safer than bloodletting across the length and width.
And for one who is accustomed to faint at bloodletting, it is necessary to eat slightly before bloodletting with bread infused in pomegranate juice or honey: or secaniabin, if it is heated: and extract from him blood in three places, or four.
And if it is of a chilled complexion, then let them take before bloodletting bread infused in honey syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices, or in fragrant aromatic syrup.
If fainting occurs during bloodletting, and the cause is a large loss of blood: then it is necessary for them to drink water with meat and subtle fragrant syrup: and use aromatics with algalia, and anoint their chest with it: and use the other things we mentioned in the division in the chapter on fainting from evacuation.
Who wishes to bleed his arm and release his blood a second time: it is necessary for one whose bloodletting is for significant evacuation and whose strength is weak, to release blood gradually according to the amount of strength over consecutive days.
Whoever wants to bleed his arm again, and his body is strong: then let him do it after seven or nine hours from his first bloodletting.
Whoever wants to draw blood from his body to the opposite part to which it leans: it is necessary that he be bled on the second day or the third.
In whose body there is already much heated blood, and it becomes sharp, and causes fever to occur: it is necessary that blood be let from him once, and a large quantity be drawn from him: and the incision should be enlarged until syncope occurs: after you have been preserving all the conditions of bloodletting: and place your hand on his pulse at the course of the blood, so that death does not occur instead of syncope. For it often happens that when the bloodletter is ignorant, negligence occurs.
And it is not appropriate when you want to bleed an arm again, and the vein's opening is already closed, and the blood's exit becomes difficult, to press on it violently, and to extend it quickly while bent. For that is very bad, indeed leave it until it is bled again.
Or remove with the sharpness of a bloodletter what has coagulated from the blood at the vein's opening, and place something dissolved salt in water on it. And place something from theriac alfaroch, or sagzenea on it, and apply it with gentle pressure until the blood flows out.
If however the vein is already an abscess, then leave it uncovered and do not cover it until the abscess settles.
If the necessity provokes to release blood a second time, and there is no excuse, then either perform phlebotomy at that same place or in another vein on the other arm.
The vein of the arm is phlebotomized at the location of the Fuscae and Basilicae, when they are not found and are hidden, because it is composed of them.
And the quality of its phlebotomy is such that the patient should insert his hand into warm water until the vein becomes red and appears clearly.
Then it should be bound above it with a bandage with slight constriction in the middle. Then phlebotomize across gradually, not widthwise, nor lengthwise: and let the opening be wide, and let your phlebotomy where you phlebotomize be at the joint of the hand for a moment.
If the flow of blood is prevented, then dip the hand again into warm water, and let the blood run into the water until you achieve your purpose.
If however you are in the summer days, then you are excused from dipping the hand in warm water. And it is placed most importantly that the flow of blood into warm water occurs during the winter time.
And the phlebotomy of this vein is safer than all other veins because there is no pulsating vein or nerve beneath it.
Indeed, the bloodletting of the right hand is beneficial for liver ailments.
And the quality of its bloodletting is to bind the wrist with a bandage, or with your hand, after you have immersed it in warm water, until the vein swells and is very apparent to the sense. Then puncture it transversely. And if you cut it completely, it will not harm it in any way.
And be careful not to leave your hand with the lancet at the end. Beneath it, the nerves of the fingers are exposed without flesh.
Then return the hand to warm water, and let the blood flow into it. For if you do not return it to warm water, the blood will clot at the vein's opening and be prevented from flowing.
Therefore, when you have extracted the necessary amount of blood, then place oil and salt on the vein so that it does not close quickly.
And similarly, you should do this with every tight branch.
The bloodletting from the left hand is beneficial for spleen ailments: and similarly perform its bloodletting in the same manner as you did for the second one equally.
The benefit of bloodletting from the saphenous vein is for ailments in the lower part of the body, such as ailments of the wombs, retention of menses, and illnesses of the kidneys, and old sores of the hips and legs, and similar ailments.
And the quality of bloodletting is such that the sick person should insert his foot into warm water: and make friction upon it until the veins swell: and bind above the joint of the foot with a strap. And the place of the veins is near the heel, appearing towards the big toe: and many branches branch out from it on the surface of the foot.
Therefore, bloodletting should be done in the larger branch of it, or near the heel at its gathering: for it is better and safer.
If you bloodlet from it on the surface of the foot, then beware of the nerves which are beneath it on the surface of the foot.
And place your bloodletting tool across where you bloodlet it, as if you want to cut it: and let the bloodletter be Nesil.
If the flow of blood is prevented, then dip his foot in warm water again: and let the blood run into it until it is evacuated.
If the bloodletter misses the vein on the first attempt, then repeat the bloodletting slightly higher up, for the area is safe, and you need not fear any harm from it when you are careful of the nerves, as we have said.
And similarly with the Saphena of the other foot equally.
The location of the Sciatic veins, as we have said, is near the heel on the outer side.
And the benefit of its bloodletting is for the pain of gout, when it is due to hot blood.
And the quality of his bloodletting is that the patient should enter the bath and hurry: and bind his leg from the side of the ankle up to four digits above the heel with a fine long thread: for it does not appear unless because of this.
When therefore it appears, then bloodlet from it according to whatever method is possible for you, or diagonally: and this is better, or cut it with an incision, or sever it with a section. For its location is safer, and it is very hidden in most people.
For its location is safer, and it is very hidden in most people. If you do not find it and it does not appear at all to the senses: then bloodlet from one of its branches, and that is the one which appears on the back of the foot, towards the little toe: and be careful of the nerves, and let as much blood flow as you wish.
Then loosen the binding, and place skin over the site of bloodletting, and bind the area. For it heals quickly.
Concerning ventosation, and the quality of its use.
Ventouses are made from horns, and from metal, and from glass.
And ventosation is performed in two ways. With scarification and extraction of blood: the other is ventosation without scarification.
And this ventosation which is without scarification is performed in two ways. For it is with fire. Or it is without fire.
And for windy conditions which are treated with scarification and bloodletting, there are fourteen parts of the body. Of which one is Ventosatio Alnocrati, and it is at the back of the head: and Alkehel, and it is in the middle of the neck: and windy Alhagdahim, and they are two plates of the neck from both sides simultaneously: and windiness of the chin, and it is below the jaw on the lower part of the mouth: and windiness of the two spatulas: and windiness of Alachosos at the end of the tail: and windiness of the two focilium, and they are in the middle of the two arms: and windiness of the two thighs: and windiness of the two cavillarum.
And Ventosatio indeed does not draw blood from you from the small veins scattered in the flesh, and because of that, strength does not fall from them, as is the case with bloodletting. Nor should ventosatio be administered, whether with fire or without fire, in any diseases that arise from excess, until the whole body is evacuated.
If necessity prompts ventosation due to illness or habit, we administer it at any hour at the beginning of the month, at the end of it, and in the middle of it, and at whatever time it may be.
This is because there are people for whom when blood multiplies in them to the point that they need its extraction through ventosation, they find heaviness and sodahan in their head.
And among them is he who finds swelling and redness on his face, his head, and his neck. And among them is he who finds itching on his face, and forehead, and darkness, and dullness in his eyes.
And among them is he who scrapes the place of his swelling. And among them is he whose laughter multiplies. And among them is he who finds the taste of blood in his mouth: or his tongue swells, and he spits out blood. And among them is he whose sleep multiplies. And among them is he who sees in his sleep blood and redness, and the dead, and wounds, and things similar to these.
When therefore we see any of these things, and especially if it is in the middle third of the month: then we prescribe that swelling be treated, after two or three hours have passed.
The remedy for swelling of the neck is: for it contributes to heaviness in the head, and what flows to the eyes. But it should be done after the evacuation of the whole body.
And this swelling is in place of cephalic bloodletting.
And it is not permissible for one of a cold temperament to use it, or for one who has catarrh. For it causes him great harm.
And for that reason, the elderly should not use it, and those who have cold diseases in their heads.
But he who becomes accustomed to it is overcome by forgetfulness.
And for that reason, you should instruct the cupper to temporarily place his hand with the cup towards the lower parts, fearing the onset of forgetfulness.
Cupping or Alkehel is in place of black bloodletting and general bloodletting, and for that reason it benefits asthma, constriction of breathing, windpipe splitting, cough, and congestion.
And it is necessary to apply the cupping Alkehel temporarily, for if placed lower, it generates weakness in the heart and stomach.
Cupping with alhagdahim benefits accidental pains in the head, opthalmia, migraines, piercings, and pain in the roots of teeth: and it is a substitute for general bloodletting.
And you should instruct the cupper not to press his hand with scarification so as not to hit an artery and cause a flow of blood.
Cupping under the chin benefits alcoholism in the mouth, corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth: and it serves as a substitute for bloodletting from the veins in both lips.
Cupping of the spatulae benefits alchafacham, which occurs from obstruction and heat.
Indeed, the blowing upon the interior parts of the two bellows brings benefit equivalent to the bloodletting from three veins, Basilicae, Fuscae, and Cephalicae: for it attracts blood from all those tiny veins which are in the flesh: and these tiny veins attract from other veins thicker than themselves, until the attraction reaches the three veins.
And you must instruct the Ventosator not to proceed too much in scarification: for the area is devoid of flesh, and beneath it are nerves and arteries.
The ventosa which is applied over the alchausos provides relief to hemorrhoids of the anus and lower ulcers.
And you must instruct the Ventosator to use a large ventosa, and let it be of air: for the area requires strong suction, and perhaps delicate Ventosae may break: and it should be scarified with a large incision.
The Ventosae of the legs noticeably reduce: for they attract blood from the whole body, and relieve old pains in the kidneys, uterus, and bladder: they provoke menstruation, and help bothor and ademenul: and serve in place of bloodletting from two saphenous veins and alhorcobeni.
However, they greatly weaken the body and cause syncope in many people.
And the benefit of the Ventosae of alhorcobeni is similar to the benefit of the Ventosae of both legs.
The quality of the placement of the Ventosae is to place the ventosa initially empty, and suck with moderate suction: and do not prolong the placement of the ventosae, but place them quickly and remove them quickly, so that the humors come to the place with an equal arrival: and do not stop iterating and continuing this until you see the area already redden and swell, and the redness of blood appears: then scarify, and repeat the suction gradually. Then consider in the arrangement of bodies.
For he who is of tender flesh and fine pores, you must scarify him once, not more: so that the place does not become ulcerated.
And instruct the bloodletter to enlarge the scarification and make it a little deep: and regulate the suction with ease, speed, and gentle movement.
If there is thickness in the blood, then you must scarify him twice. In the first juice, the way is opened for the refinement of blood and its aqueous quality: and in the second, for the thorough extraction of thick blood.
If the blood is very feculent, then let the scarification be done a third time: so as to achieve the ultimate.
And finally, when we wish to extract blood gradually or for a short while, one scarification is sufficient for us. If we wish for the extraction of much blood, we scarify with multiple scarifications.
And if we measure that the blood is thick: then it must be scarified with deep incisions: and the limit in scarification is the depth of the skin.
What should be administered from oils at the site of bloodletting, and what the person being bled should beware of.
For him whose skin is thick, hard, dark, and whose pores are tight, the areas for bloodletting should be anointed with opening, soothing, and resolving oils: if it is in the summertime, such as oil of alkeiri, or violet oil, or oil of sweet almonds, or oil of pumpkin seed.
And if it is in winter time, then use narciss oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or balsam: and things like these.
And if the excess is thick and cold: then the oil should be rue oil, or balsamite oil, or dittany oil, or anise oil: and things like these.
And if the windiness is of large pores, tender flesh: then it is necessary to prohibit oil, and these places of windiness should be washed after windiness with rose water, or with cold water, or with water of solatri, or with water of cucumber, or with water of portulaca: and things like these.
He whose blood is of much moisture, should wash windiness with vinegar, or with myrtle water, and sumach: and things like these.
Whose excesses are thick, should wash his windiness with old wine, or with henbane water, or anise decoction, or chamomile: and things like these.
And it is necessary to be cautious about windiness in a bath, or near the bath, rather it should be administered after exiting the bath by one hour, or by two hours.
And it is not advisable for someone to sleep after windiness.
What is it that should regulate windiness or bloodletting before windiness.
And after that, it is necessary to first consider: then if the windiness or bloodletting is for a choleric person, and sharpness and inflammation overcome his blood: then it is necessary for him to take cooling things, such as pomegranate molasses: and also endive with vinegar and lettuce, and cyclamen, and rue: and things like these.
And place his foods as chicks, and meats of sheep satebiget, and seasoned foods with herbs: and things similar to these.
And for one whose complexion is cold, he must take in drink syrup of honey, or of almaua, or alsecaniabin made from seeds: and let him take fragrant wine that is middle-aged, which is between old and new: and let it be ordered that he use sparingly of food. And place his food as chicks, and canebir: and sparrows, that is, small birds: and chicks of pigeons should be cooked with issia.
And it must be that the drink on the day of bloodletting and phlebotomy be more than food: and it must be that in some men's drinks there is given at certain times theriac alfaroch, or medicine of musk, that is, muscata, or alesselite before bloodletting: and before phlebotomy, or after: so that the principal limbs may be strengthened, and the blood made finer. And it should not be taken in heated drink.
Regarding Windiness without Scarification. Windiness which is without scarification, is windiness that is placed upon the liver, and spleen, and gout, and upon the stomach, navel, and areas of the kidneys, and the anus: because these members do not tolerate scarification upon them.
And they are not sought for, except for the transmission of blood from one member to another: as we place windiness upon the breasts in the illness of nasal bleeding. And we use them to resolve cold invisible swelling in the limb: just as we place swollen on the stomach and navel. For it rarefies the limb, and heats it, and removes pain because it resolves that swelling.
It is also placed on the kidneys when obstruction or stone occurs in them. For by the power of its attraction, it perhaps opens the obstruction or removes the stone from its place.
And it does the same when placed on the spleen and liver for swelling to be treated in both of them.
And these swellings are treated empty with only incision. And sometimes they are treated with fire.
And sometimes they are administered full of warm water in pleurisy illnesses: and this is done by filling the Ventosa with hot water alone, or water in which herbs suitable for the condition have been decocted.
The method of applying the Ventosa with fire.
Let the diameter of its opening be that of two spread fingers, according to how we have formed it: and let its depth be half a palm: and let there be a small hole on its side at a place which is about the middle of it, according to the size through which a needle can enter: it should be made of copper or brass, with thick, smooth, equal, clean edges: so that it does not harm the limb when placed upon it: and let there be a crossbar in the middle of it made of metal or iron where a candle with fire is placed.
And now this becomes large and inflated, larger than what we mentioned, and somewhat smaller than that, according to the illnesses and age of the one who uses it.
For the flatus of children and those who are emaciated is different from that of men and those with thicker bodies.
The quality of placing this inflated device over a limb with fire is to light wax with fire properly from linen, or a small candle from tallow: and place it on the middle crossbar which is in the middle of the inflated device: so that the fire ignites around the lower part of the inflated device, so that the body of the sick person is not burned.
Then it should be placed on the limb: and a finger should be over the hole I mentioned, until when we hold the inflated device: while we need to, remove the finger, and the vapor will escape through that hole, and the inflated device will deflate immediately.
Then light the wax according to its manner, and repeat it, if you need it.
In the cupping device used for the illness of pleuresis with water, there is no crossbar, nor a hole: and it is not used except that it is filled with water and placed on the limb only.
And this is its form.
And this cupping device, the larger it is, to hold more water, is better.
Regarding the suspension of bloodletting devices.
Leeches are not applied to many places, except where it is not possible to place cupping vessels on the limbs due to their small size, such as the lip, and gum, and similar areas. Or on a bare limb of flesh, such as the finger, and nose, and similar areas.
And the quality of using them is: to use leeches that are from sweet waters, clean from putrefactions.
